Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Raising Hands and Pausing Between Extra Takbirs of Eid
Intra-Hanafi ruling with proof and additional instruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during Eid extra takbirs, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and describe the recommended pause between takbirs.

Core Idea
Hands raised in each extra takbir of Eid; pause three tasbihs to avoid confusion.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical aspect of Eid prayer: the extra takbirs (takbīrāt zawā'id). While the basic ruling that these takbirs are wājib is settled, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether to raise the hands with each takbir. Additionally, the imam is instructed to pause between takbirs to allow the congregation to follow. Understanding these rulings ensures proper performance of the Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act: raising hands during the extra takbirs of Eid. State the mufta bihi ruling: sunnah (recommended) to raise hands, based on a hadith listing seven places for raf' al-yadayn.
The hadith is narrated from the Prophet (S).
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view (hands raised) with Abu Yusuf's view (not raised). Identify each scholar's evidence: Abu Hanifa uses the explicit hadith; Abu Yusuf uses analogy (qiyas) with the takbir for bowing.
The text sides with Abu Hanifa, stating his evidence overrides the analogy.
3
Analyse the evidence for Abu Hanifa's position
The hadith 'La tarfa' al-aydi illa fi sab'i mawatina' (Do not raise hands except in seven places) explicitly includes Eid takbirs. Since the general prohibition is restricted by the exception, raising hands is commanded in these places.
This is a dalīl naqli (textual evidence) with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the objection and the response
Abu Yusuf argues that raising hands is a sunnah of the opening takbir only; extra takbirs are not opening takbirs. The response: the hadith overrides qiyas, and the explicit inclusion of Eid takbirs in the list is decisive.
The Hanafi principle: a nass (explicit text) takes precedence over qiyas.
5
Note the additional ruling on pause
Between each extra takbir, the imam should pause for the duration of three tasbīhs. This is to prevent confusion among the congregation, especially those far from the imam.
This ruling is from Abu Hanifa and is operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويرفع يديه في تكبيرات العيدين يريد به ماسوى التكبير فى الركوع لقوله صلى لا ترفع الايدى لا في سبع مواطن وذكر من جملتها تكبيرات الاعياد وعن ابى يوسف انه لا يرفع والحجة عليه ماروينا رجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ عیدین کی تکبیروں میں اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے اس سے مراد تکبیر رکوع کے علاوہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں مگر سات جگہوں میں منجملہ ان میں سے عیدین کی تکبیروں کا ذکر کیا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں اور امام ابو یوسف پر حجت وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ فریح ہمارے نزدیک تکبیرات عیدین میں کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھائے جائیں گے یہی امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا مذہب ہے۔ دلیل انحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا ترفع الايدى الا فی سبع مواطن ہے۔ ان سات جگہوں میں عیدین کی تکبیرات زوائد بھی ہیں۔ امام یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ تکبیرات عیدین میں ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہاتھوں کا اٹھانا افتتاح کی سنت ہے چونکہ تکبیرات زوائد میں افتتاح صلوۃ نہیں اس لئے رفع یدین بھی نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ رکوع کی تکبیر کے اندر رفع یدین نہیں ہے امام ابو ہف کے خلاف حدیث لا ترفع الابدی حجت ہوگی رہی یہ بات کہ تکبیرات زوائد کے درمیان کوئی مسنون ذکر ہے یا نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو نیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ ہر دو تکبیروں کے درمیان تین تسبیحات کی مقدار سکوت کرے۔ کیونکہ عید کی نماز جم غفیر کے ساتھ ادا کی جاتی ہے اگر نبیرات کے درمیان موالات اور وصل کیا گیا تو جولوگ امام سے دور ہوں گے ان پر امام کا حال مشتبہ ہو جائے گا کہ امام کون کی تکبیر کہہ رہا ہے البتہ اتنی مقدار ٹھہرنے سے اشتباہ دور ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے تکبیرات کے درمیان تین تسبیحات کی مقدار خاموش رہنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔
He said: And he raises his hands in the takbirs of the two Eids – he means other than the takbir for bowing – because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not raise hands except in seven places,' and he mentioned among them the takbirs of the Eids. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he does not raise. The proof against him is what we have narrated. Al-Quduri said: In the takbirs of the two Eids, he raises both his hands; this means other than the takbir of bowing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places,' and among them are the takbirs of the Eids. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he does not raise, and the proof against Abu Yusuf is the hadith we narrated. So, in our view, hands are raised to the ears in the takbirs of the two Eids, and this is also the school of Shafi'i and Ahmad. The proof is the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places.' Among these seven places are the extra takbirs of the Eids. From Imam Yusuf it is narrated that hands are not raised in the takbirs of the Eids. The proof of Abu Yusuf is that raising hands is a sunnah of the opening takbir, and since in the extra takbirs there is no opening of the prayer, there is no raising of hands, just as in the takbir for bowing there is no raising of hands. Against Imam Abu Hanifa, the hadith 'la tarfa' al-aydi' is evidence. As for whether there is any prescribed dhikr between the extra takbirs or not: From Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he pauses between every two takbirs for the measure of three tasbihs, because the Eid prayer is performed with a large congregation. If there is continuity (muwālāt) and connection between the takbirs, then those who are far from the imam will be confused about the imam's state, not knowing which takbir the imam is saying. By pausing for this amount, confusion is dispelled. Therefore, it is commanded to remain silent between the takbirs for the measure of three tasbihs.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether to raise hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the extra takbirs of Eid prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa (and the school's relied-upon position) holds that hands should be raised with each extra takbir, citing the hadith of the Prophet (S) listing seven places where hands are raised, including Eid takbirs. This is also the view of Shafi'i and Hanbali schools. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that raising hands is a sunnah specific to the opening takbir (takbīrat al-ihrām) and since extra takbirs are not opening takbirs, hands should not be raised, analogous to the takbir for bowing. The Hanafi response dismisses this analogy because the hadith explicitly includes Eid takbirs among the places for raising hands. The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa. Additionally, the passage rules that between each extra takbir, one should pause silently for the duration of three tasbīhs. This is to prevent confusion in the congregation, especially for those far from the imam. This ruling is from Abu Hanifa and is operative.

Key Terms
رفع یدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears during takbirs, a practice in prayer.
تکبیرات زوائد (takbīrāt zawā'id): The extra takbirs in Eid prayer beyond the regular prayer structure.
سکوت (sukūt): Silence, specifically the pause between extra takbirs for three tasbihs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position on raising hands during the extra takbirs of Eid prayer?
A) Hands are not raised
B) Hands are raised with each extra takbir
C) Hands are raised only in the first takbir
D) Hands are raised only by the imam

Key Takeaway
Hands are raised in each extra takbir of Eid, and a pause of three tasbihs between takbirs is sunnah to aid congregation.

The Ruling on the Timing of the Eid Khutbah
Ruling with proof on Eid khutbah timing, with distinction from Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the Eid khutbah and identify the two key differences from the Jumu'ah khutbah.

Core Idea
The Eid prayer is valid without the khutbah, which follows the prayer.

What is the proper sequence for Eid prayer and khutbah? The Hanafi school, relying on the widespread practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, affirms that the two khutbahs are delivered after the prayer. This lesson examines the proof for this ruling and highlights how the Eid khutbah differs from the Jumu'ah khutbah in both obligation and order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The author states that the imam delivers two khutbahs after the Eid prayer. This is the established Hanafi position.
The ruling is about the timing of the khutbah relative to the prayer.
2
Examine the dalil
The proof comes from widespread transmission (naql mustafīḍ) and the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas in Bukhari and Muslim, which state that the Prophet and the first three caliphs prayed the Eid prayer before the khutbah.
The hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning, providing certainty in transmission.
3
Derive the legal implication
The practice of the Prophet and the caliphs establishes the sunnah order. The widespread transmission (naql mustafīḍ) is a strong authority in Hanafi usul.
The ruling is based on practice, not just verbal command.
4
Contrast with Jumu'ah
The passage identifies two differences: (1) Jumu'ah is invalid without khutbah, Eid is valid without it; (2) Jumu'ah khutbah precedes prayer, Eid khutbah follows it.
These distinctions highlight the different legal nature of the two prayers.
5
Note the concession
If the khutbah is accidentally given before the Eid prayer, the prayer remains valid and does not need to be repeated.
This shows that the khutbah is not a condition (shart) for the prayer's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نال ويخطب بعد الصلواة خطبتين بذلك ورد النقل المستفيض يعلم الناس فيها صدقة الفطر واحكامها لانها شرعت لا جله زمہ کہا کہ نماز عید کے بعد امام دو خطبہ پڑھے اسی پر نقل جو شائع ہے دار ہوئی خطبہ عید میں لوگوں کو صدقہ فطر اور اس کے احکام سکھلائے کیونکہ خطبہ اسی وجہ سے مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب نے کہا کہ نماز عید سے فارغ ہو کر امام دو خطبہ پڑھے گا اسی پر نقل اور عمل شائع ہے۔ چنانچہ بخاری اور ملر میں حدیث ابن عمر کے الفاظ نہیں کہ قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم ابوبكر وعمرر يصلون العبدين قبل الخطبة اور ابن عباس کا قول ہے شهت العيد مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و ابي بكر و عمر وعثمان كلهم كانوا يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبته ( رواه الشيخان ) دونوں حدیثوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ اور خلفاء ثلاثہ عیدین کی نماز پہلے اور خطبہ بعد میں پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ البتہ عید کا خطبہ خطبہ جمعہ سے دو باتوں میں مخالف ہے اول یہ کہ جمعہ بغیر خطبہ کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عید کی نماز بغیر خطبہ کے جائز ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ جمعہ کا خطبہ نماز جمعہ پر مقدم ہے اور عیدین کا خطبہ نماز سے مؤخر ہے۔ لیکن اگر عید کا خطبہ نماز سے مقدم کر دیا گیا تو بھی جائز ہے۔ نماز عید کے بعد اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ واضح ہو کر عید الفطر کے خطبہ میں صدقۃ الفطر اور اس کے احکام کی تعلیم دیجائے گی کیونکہ یہ خطبہ اسی مقصد کے پیش نظر مشروع ہوا ہے۔
He said: And he delivers two khutbahs after the prayer. Upon this the widespread transmission (naql mustafīḍ) has come, teaching the people therein about sadaqat al-fitr and its rulings, because it (khutbah) was legislated for that purpose. The author said: After the Eid prayer, the imam delivers two khutbahs. The transmission and practice upon this are widespread. Thus in Bukhari and Muslim, the hadith of Ibn Umar has the words: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him), then Abu Bakr and Umar used to pray the two Eids before the khutbah.' And the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'I witnessed the Eid with the Messenger of Allah, and with Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman; all of them used to pray the two Eids before the khutbah.' (narrated by al-Shaykhan). The conclusion of both hadiths is that the Messenger and the three Caliphs used to pray the Eid prayer first and the khutbah after. However, the Eid khutbah differs from the Jumu'ah khutbah in two matters: First, that Jumu'ah is not valid without a khutbah, whereas the Eid prayer is valid without a khutbah. Second, that the Jumu'ah khutbah precedes the Jumu'ah prayer, while the Eid khutbah is after the prayer. But if the Eid khutbah is given before the prayer, it is still valid; there is no need to repeat the prayer. It is understood that in the khutbah of Eid al-Fitr, the teachings of sadaqat al-fitr and its rulings are given, because this khutbah was legislated with this purpose in mind.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the timing and nature of the Eid khutbahs. The author of the matn states that the imam delivers two khutbahs after the Eid prayer. This is based on widespread transmission (naql mustafīḍ) and the practice of the Prophet (S) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, as narrated in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. The passage then distinguishes the Eid khutbah from the Jumu'ah khutbah in two key ways: (1) Jumu'ah is invalid without khutbah, but Eid prayer is valid even if no khutbah is delivered; (2) In Jumu'ah, khutbah comes before prayer; in Eid, it comes after. However, if the khutbah is accidentally given before the Eid prayer, the prayer remains valid and does not need to be repeated. The purpose of the Eid al-Fitr khutbah is specifically to educate the people about sadaqat al-fitr and its rulings, as that is why it was legislated. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam, consisting of two parts, after the Eid prayer.
نقل مستفیض (naql mustafīḍ): A widely transmitted report, though not reaching the level of tawātur, it is reliable and acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the imam delivers the khutbah before the Eid prayer?
A) The prayer must be repeated after the khutbah
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
C) The prayer is still valid and does not need repetition
D) The khutbah must be given again after the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the Eid khutbah is a sunnah delivered after the prayer, distinct from Jumu'ah where it is a condition before the prayer.

Making Up Missed Eid Prayer as an Individual
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on qada of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up a missed Eid prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using conditional reasoning.

Core Idea
Missed Eid prayer is not made up because its validity requires conditions impossible for a lone individual.

When the Eid congregation concludes, what should a latecomer do? The Hanafi school says: nothing—the prayer is not made up. This ruling hinges on two conditions that cannot be replicated alone: congregation and the presence of the ruler. The Shafi'i school disagrees, viewing congregation as non-essential. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is the point of disagreement? The Hanafi school says the individual does not make up the Eid prayer; the Shafi'i school says he may (and it is mustahabb).
The act in question is qaḍā' of ṣalāt al-ʿīd, not the original performance.
2
State the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument: The Eid prayer is only known to be a valid act of worship (qurbah) when performed with specific conditions—congregation and the presence of the ruler (sulṭān or his deputy). These conditions cannot be met by an individual alone.
This proof is based on istidlāl: from the continuous practice (tawātur ʿamalī) of the Prophet and caliphs.
3
State the Shafi‘i proof
The Shafi‘i school holds that congregation is not a condition for Eid prayer; therefore, a person can pray it alone. The general command to pray applies, and making it up is recommended (mustahabb).
They rely on the generality of commands for prayer and do not accept the restrictive conditions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response counters that the general command is restricted (muqayyad) by these specific conditions, as demonstrated by the consistent practice. Without them, the act is not the prescribed worship.
This is a classic Hanafi example of takhṣīṣ al-ʿāmm by ʿamal.
5
Determine the practical difference
A Hanafi who misses the Eid prayer does not pray it at all; a Shafi‘i prays it alone as qaḍā’. The muftā bihī position is the Hanafi one, which also aligns with Imam Mālik.
This is the thamarah al-khilāf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من فاتته صلواة العيد مع الامام لم يقضها لان الصلوة بهذه الصفة لم تعرف قربة الا بشرائط لاتتم بالمنفرد ترجمہ اور وہ شخص جس کی نماز عید امام کے ساتھ فوت ہوگئی تو وہ اس کی قضاء نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ نماز عید کا اس صفت کے ساتھ عبادت ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا مگر ایسی شرطوں کے ساتھ جو تنہا آدمی سے پوری نہیں ہوتیں۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام اگر عید کی نماز ادا کر چکا اور ایک آدمی باقی رہ گیا۔ اس نے عید کی نماز ادا نہیں کی ہے تو اس کو قضاء کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ شخص تنہا نماز عید پڑھ سکتا ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک جواز عیدین کے لئے نہ جماعت شرط ہے اور نہ سلطان کا ہونا۔ اس لئے ان کے نزدیک نماز عید کی قضاء کرنا مستحب ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نماز عید قائم کرنے کے لئے کچھ ایسی شرطیں ہیں جو تنہا آدمی سے پوری نہیں ہو سکتیں۔ مثلاً جماعت سلطان وقت پس چونکہ منفرد میں یہ شرطیں نہیں پائی جاتیں اس لئے اس کے واسطے تنہا نماز عید پڑھنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
And whoever misses the Eid prayer with the imam does not make it up, because the prayer in this form is not known to be an act of worship except with conditions that are not fulfilled by an individual. Translation: And the person whose Eid prayer was missed with the imam will not make it up, because the Eid prayer in this form is not known to be worship except with conditions that are not fulfilled by an individual. Explanation: The scenario is that if the imam has performed the Eid prayer and one person remains who did not pray it, he is not permitted to make it up. This is also the saying of Imam Malik. Imam Shafi'i said that this person can pray the Eid prayer alone, because according to Shafi'i, congregation is not a condition for the validity of Eid, nor the presence of a ruler. Therefore, according to him, making up the Eid prayer is mustahabb. Our proof is that for establishing the Eid prayer, there are certain conditions that cannot be fulfilled by an individual, such as congregation and the ruler of the time. Since these conditions are not found in an individual, it is not permissible for him to pray the Eid prayer alone.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the qaḍā' (make-up) of the Eid prayer for a person who missed it with the congregation. The Hanafi ruling, supported by Imam Malik, is that such a person does not make up the prayer because the Eid prayer is only valid as an act of worship when specific conditions are met: congregation and the presence of the ruler (sulṭān) or his deputy. These conditions cannot be fulfilled by an individual praying alone. The Shafi'i school holds that congregation is not a condition for Eid prayer; therefore, a person can pray it alone, and making it up is mustahabb (recommended). The Hanafi response is that the Eid prayer was legislated with these conditions, as evidenced by the continuous practice of the Prophet (S) and the Caliphs in congregation. Without these conditions, the prayer is not considered a valid act of worship (qurbah). Therefore, qaḍā' is not allowed. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed obligatory or sunnah prayer.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
سلطان (sulṭān): The ruler or his deputy whose permission or presence is considered for the Eid congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he misses the Eid prayer with the imam?
A) Pray it alone with the same takbirs
B) Make it up later with congregation
C) Do not make it up at all
D) Pray two rak'ahs without extra takbirs

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, missed Eid prayer is not made up because the conditions of its validity (congregation and ruler) cannot be fulfilled by an individual.

Delaying Eid Prayer Due to Crescent Confusion
Ruling on delaying Eid prayer due to late crescent testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for delaying Eid prayer when the crescent is obscured after zawal, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the limitation that the prayer is not made up if missed on the second day.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is delayed to the next day for a valid excuse, but if missed again, it is never made up.

This lesson covers a specific scenario: the crescent of Eid is hidden by clouds, and witnesses come to the imam after the customary time for Eid prayer has passed. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling based on a hadith, but with an important limitation. Understanding this demonstrates how exceptions to general principles operate within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage states: if the crescent is obscured (ghumma al-hilāl) and testimony of sighting occurs after zawal (afternoon), what is the ruling? Note the key conditions: obscured crescent, testimony after zawal.
2
State the ruling
The imam prays the Eid prayer the next day. This is a delay due to the excuse of late testimony.
3
Locate the dalil
The text references a hadith: 'waqad warada fīhi al-ḥadīth'. This is a specific hadith (ahad) permitting the delay.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but is authoritative.
4
Understand the original principle
The original principle (asl) is that Eid prayer is not made up (lā tuqḍā), similar to Jumu'ah. The hadith creates an exception for this specific case.
5
Note the limitation
If on the second day an excuse prevents the prayer, it is not performed after that, reverting to the original principle of no make-up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان غم الهلال وشهدوا عند الامام برؤية الهلال بعد الزوال، صلى العيد من الغدلان هذا تاخير بعذر، وقد ورد فيه الحديث، فان حدث عذر يمنع من الصلوة فى اليوم الثانى لم يصلها بعده، لان الأصل فيها ان لا تقضى كالجمعة الا انا تركناه بالحديث وقد ورد بالتاخير الى اليوم الثاني عند العذر ترجمہ پھر اگر چاند ابر میں چھپ گیا اور لوگوں نے زوال کے بعد امام کے سامنے چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دی تو امام دوسرے دن نماز عید پڑھے۔ کیونکہ یہ تاخیر عذر کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور اس میں حدیث دارد ہوئی ہے۔ اور اگر ایسا عذر پیدا ہوا جو دوسرے دن بھی نماز عید سے روکنا رہے تو اس کے بعد یہ نماز نہیں پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ نماز عید میں اصل تو یہی ہے کہ اس کی قضاء کی جائے مگر ہم نے اس اصل کو حدیث کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا اور عذر کے وقت دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے پر حدیث کا درود ہوا ہے۔
For if the crescent is obscured (ghumma al-hilāl) and they testify before the imam of sighting the crescent after zawal (noon), he prays the Eid prayer the next day, because this is a delay due to an excuse, and the hadith has come concerning this. If an excuse occurs that prevents the prayer on the second day, he does not pray it after that, because the original principle is that it is not made up (qadā'), like Jumu'ah, except that we abandoned this principle due to the hadith, and the hadith has come regarding delaying to the second day when there is an excuse.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the timing of Eid prayer when the sighting of the crescent is uncertain. The scenario: on the 29th of Ramadan, the moon is hidden by clouds (ghumma al-hilāl). On the 30th, after zawal (afternoon), witnesses come to the imam to testify that they sighted the moon the previous night. Since the news came after the usual time for Eid prayer (which is before zawal), the imam postpones the Eid prayer to the following day (i.e., on the 31st if Ramadan was 29 days, or on the actual Eid day after zawal? Actually, the text says 'next day' meaning the day after the testimony). This delay is permitted due to the excuse of late testimony. The evidence is a hadith allowing such delay. However, if even on the second day an excuse prevents the prayer (e.g., continued rain or conflict), then the prayer is not performed at all after that, because the original principle is that Eid prayer is not made up (qaḍā'), similar to Jumu'ah prayer. This exception is only made for the specific case of delayed testimony, based on the hadith. The principle is that Eid prayer is not made up, but the hadith creates a dispensation for this particular situation. After the second day, the ruling reverts to the original principle: no qaḍā'.

Key Terms
غم الهلال (ghumma al-hilāl): The crescent is obscured by clouds or fog, making it invisible.
زوال (zawāl): The sun's declination from the meridian, i.e., noon when the sun begins to tilt westward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses testify after zawāl on the 30th of Ramadan that they saw the crescent the previous night, when is the Eid prayer performed according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately after the testimony
B) The next day (31st)
C) It is not performed at all
D) After Maghrib the same day

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer may be delayed only one day due to late crescent testimony; if missed on the second day, it is permanently omitted.

Order of Khutbah in Eid Prayer
Explaining that Eid khutbah follows the prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the Eid khutbah and distinguish it from the Jumu'ah khutbah based on dalil.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is valid without khutbah; the khutbah is sunnah and follows the prayer.

In this passage, the author clarifies a key difference between Jumu'ah and Eid prayers: the order of the khutbah. While Jumu'ah requires a pre-prayer khutbah for validity, the Eid khutbah is a post-prayer sunnah. This ruling is supported by the consistent practice of the Prophet and the first three caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delivering the khutbah for Eid prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, the khutbah is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
This means the prayer is valid even without the khutbah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas recorded in Bukhari and Muslim. Both describe that the Prophet and the caliphs prayed the Eid before the khutbah.
The hadith are sahih and mutawatir in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'they pray the two Eids before the khutbah' indicates that the prayer takes precedence in time over the khutbah.
The word 'before' modifies the prayer, not the khutbah.
4
Derive the practical implication
If the khutbah is given before the prayer by mistake, the prayer remains valid and no repetition is needed, unlike Jumu'ah.
This is a key difference between Eid and Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح صاحب کتاب نے کہا کہ نماز عید سے فارغ ہو کر امام دو خطبہ پڑھے گا اسی پر نقل اور عمل شائع ہے۔ چنانچہ بخاری اور مسلم میں حدیث ابن عمر کے الفاظ ہیں کہ قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم ابوبكر وعمر يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبة اور ابن عباس کا قول ہے شهدت العيد مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و ابي بكر و عمر و عثمان كلهم كانوا يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبة ( رواه الشيخان ) دونوں حدیثوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ اور خلفاء ثلاثہ عیدین کی نماز پہلے اور خطبہ بعد میں پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ البتہ عید کا خطبہ خطبہ جمعہ سے دو باتوں میں مخالف ہے اول یہ کہ جمعہ بغیر خطبہ کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عید کی نماز بغیر خطبہ کے جائز ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ جمعہ کا خطبہ نماز جمعہ پر مقدم ہے اور عیدین کا خطبہ نماز سے مؤخر ہے۔ لیکن اگر عید کا خطبہ نماز سے مقدم کر دیا گیا تو بھی جائز ہے۔ نماز عید کے بعد اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ واضح ہو کر عید الفطر کے خطبہ میں صدقۃ الفطر اور اس کے احکام کی تعلیم دیجائے گی کیونکہ یہ خطبہ اسی مقصد کے پیش نظر مشروع ہوا ہے۔
The commentator (sahib al-kitab) said that after finishing the Eid prayer, the imam will deliver two khutbahs. Upon this (practice) transmission and action are widespread. Thus, in Bukhari and Muslim, the hadith of Ibn Umar has the words: 'He said: The Prophet (peace be upon him), then Abu Bakr and Umar used to pray the two Eids before the khutbah.' And the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'I witnessed Eid with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman — all of them used to pray the two Eids before the khutbah.' (Narrated by al-Shaykhan). The gist of both hadiths is that the Messenger of Allah and the three caliphs used to pray the two Eid prayers first and the khutbah afterwards. However, the Eid khutbah differs from the Jumu'ah khutbah in two matters: First, that Jumu'ah is not valid without a khutbah, and the Eid prayer is valid without a khutbah. Second, that the Jumu'ah khutbah precedes the Jumu'ah prayer, and the Eid khutbah is after the prayer. But if the Eid khutbah is given before the prayer, it is also valid; there is no need to repeat the Eid prayer. It will be clear that in the khutbah of Eid al-Fitr, instructions about sadaqat al-fitr and its rulings are given, because this khutbah was legislated for this purpose.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, the Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah. The author begins by stating the ruling: the Imam delivers two khutbahs after the Eid prayer. He supports this with the practice of the Prophet and the first three caliphs, as narrated in authentic hadith. He then contrasts Eid khutbah with Jumu'ah khutbah in two ways: (1) Jumu'ah is invalid without khutbah, but Eid prayer is valid without it; (2) Jumu'ah khutbah precedes the prayer, while Eid khutbah follows. However, if the khutbah is given before the Eid prayer, it is still valid and no repetition is needed. Finally, he notes that the Eid al-Fitr khutbah should include teachings on sadaqat al-fitr, as the khutbah was legislated for that purpose.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam after Eid prayer.
عيدين (al-eidayn): The two Eids: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if the Eid khutbah is given before the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated after the khutbah.
D) The khutbah cannot be given before the prayer under any circumstance.

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is a sunnah that follows the prayer; giving it before does not invalidate the prayer.

Delay of Eid Prayer Due to Late Moon Sighting
Ruling on Eid prayer delay due to late moon sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Eid prayer when the moon is sighted after zawaal and explain the dalil from hadith.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is only delayed to the next day for a valid excuse, not made up beyond that.

When the Eid moon is not sighted on the 29th of Ramadan, but is sighted after zawaal on the 30th, the Eid prayer is delayed to the next day (1st Shawwal). This delay is based on a hadith that permits it due to the excuse of late sighting. However, if an excuse prevents the prayer on the second day as well, it is not delayed further, because the original principle is that Eid prayer is not made up at all, similar to Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The scenario is when the moon is hidden on the 29th and sighted after zawaal on the 30th. The ruling is that the imam prays Eid the next day.
The delay is only to the next day, not further.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from al-Hidayah: 'When they testified to the sighting of the moon after zawaal, he ordered going out to the musalla the next day.'
This is a mursal hadith, so it is zanni in thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly commands going out the next day, indicating that the delay is permitted for the excuse of late sighting.
The command indicates permission, not obligation to delay.
4
Note the exception: no further delay
If an excuse prevents prayer on the second day (2nd Shawwal), it is not delayed further. The original principle (asl) is that Eid prayer is not made up, like Jumu'ah. The hadith only provides an exception for a one-day delay.
The hadith specifically mentions 'the next day' (min al-ghad).
5
Understand the principle of non-qada for Eid
Eid prayer is sunnah muakkadah, not fard. Unlike fard prayers, it is not made up if the time passes. This is similar to Jumu'ah prayer, which is also not made up if missed.
Only the one-day delay is allowed; beyond that, the original rule of no qada applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان غم الهلال وشهدوا عند الامام برؤية الهلال بعد الزوال، صلى العيد من الغد لان هذا تاخير بعذر، وقد ورد فيه الحديث، فان حدث عذر يمنع من الصلوة فى اليوم الثانى لم يصلها بعده، لان الأصل فيها ان لا تقضى كالجمعة الا انا تركناه بالحديث وقد ورد بالتاخير الى اليوم الثاني عند العذر ترجمہ پھر اگر چاند ابر میں چھپ گیا اور لوگوں نے زوال کے بعد امام کے سامنے چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دی تو امام دوسرے دن نماز عید پڑھے۔ کیونکہ یہ تاخیر عذر کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور اس میں حدیث وارد ہوئی ہے۔ اور اگر ایسا عذر پیدا ہوا جو دوسرے دن بھی نماز عید سے روکنا رہے تو اس کے بعد یہ نماز نہیں پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ نماز عید میں اصل تو یہی ہے کہ اس کی قضاء کی جائے مگر ہم نے اس اصل کو حدیث کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا اور عذر کے وقت دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے پر حدیث کا درود ہوا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ۲۹ رمضان کو اگر چاند ابر میں چھپ گیا اور ۳۰ رمضان کو زوال کے بعد لوگوں نے امام کے سامنے چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دی اور امام نے ان کی گواہی قبول بھی کر لی تو روزہ توڑ دیں اور امام دوسرے دن لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تاخیر عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے اس تاخیر میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اس تاخیر کے سلسلہ میں حدیث بھی موجود ہے چنانچہ ہدایہ میں گذشتہ صفحہ پر یہ حدیث اس طرح ذکر کی گئی ہے ولما شهدوا بالهلال بعد الزوال امر بالخروج الى المصلى من الغد اور اگر دو شوال کو بھی کوئی ایسا عذر پایا گیا جو نماز عید کے لئے مانع ہو تو اب اس کے بعد ۳ شوال کو نماز عید پڑھنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نماز عید میں اصل تو یہی کہ اس کی قضاء نہ کی جائے جیسے جمعہ فوت ہونے کی صورت میں اس کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی لیکن عذر کی وجہ سے دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے میں حدیث مذکور کی وجہ سے اس اصل کو ترک کر دیا گیا ہے پس چونکہ حدیث کے اندر فقط دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے کی تصریح کی گئی ہے اس لئے ۲ شوال تک نماز عید مؤخر کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی اس کے بعد اجازت نہ ہوگی۔
If the moon is hidden (on 29th) and they testify before the imam of sighting the moon after zawaal, he prays the Eid on the next day, because this delay is due to an excuse, and the hadith has come regarding it. If an excuse occurs that prevents the prayer on the second day, he does not pray it after that, because the original principle regarding it is that it is not made up (qada'), like Jumu'ah, except that we left that principle due to the hadith, and the hadith has come regarding delaying to the second day when there is an excuse. Translation: Then if the moon is hidden in the clouds and people give testimony of sighting the moon before the imam after zawaal, the imam will pray the Eid the next day, because this delay is due to an excuse, and a hadith has been narrated regarding it. And if such an excuse occurs that prevents from the prayer on the second day as well, then he will not pray it after that, because the original ruling regarding the Eid prayer is that it is not made up, like Jumu'ah, but we have abandoned that original due to the hadith, and the hadith has entered regarding delaying until the next day at the time of excuse. Commentary: The scenario is that if on the 29th of Ramadan the moon is hidden, and on the 30th after zawaal people give testimony of sighting the moon before the imam, and the imam accepts their testimony, then they break their fast and the imam leads the people in prayer the next day. The proof is that this delay is due to an excuse, so there is no harm in this delay, and there is also a hadith regarding this delay. In al-Hidayah on the previous page, this hadith is mentioned: 'When they testified to the sighting of the moon after zawaal, he ordered going out to the musalla the next day.' And if on the 2nd of Shawwal also some obstacle is found that prevents the Eid prayer, then after that on the 3rd of Shawwal there will be no permission to pray the Eid prayer, because the original principle regarding the Eid prayer is that it is not made up, just as in the case of missing Jumu'ah it is not made up. But due to the excuse, the original was abandoned for delaying until the next day because of the mentioned hadith. Since the hadith specifies only delaying to the next day, permission is given to delay the Eid prayer until the 2nd of Shawwal; after that there will be no permission.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when the Eid moon is not sighted on the 29th, and then is sighted after zawaal on the 30th. The Eid prayer is delayed to the next day (1st Shawwal) due to this excuse. The hadith allows this delay. However, if an obstacle prevents prayer on that day as well, it is not delayed further (e.g., to 3rd Shawwal), because the original principle is that Eid is not made up (like Jumu'ah), and the hadith only permits delay to the second day. The commentary explains the scenario: on 30th after zawaal, moon sighting is accepted; they break fast and pray Eid the next day. If something prevents on 2nd Shawwal, no further delay is allowed.

Key Terms
زوال (zawaal): The time when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., around noon.
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that allows relaxation of normal rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if the moon is sighted after zawaal on the 30th of Ramadan, when is the Eid prayer performed?
A) Immediately after the sighting.
B) The next day (1st Shawwal).
C) The day after the next (2nd Shawwal).
D) It is not performed at all.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is delayed to the next day only when the moon is sighted after zawaal; no further delay is allowed beyond that.

Mustahabbat of Eid al-Adha
Listing recommended acts on Eid al-Adha: ghusl, perfume, delaying eating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mustahabbat (recommended acts) for Eid al-Adha and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice, including the exception for villagers.

Core Idea
Delay eating on Eid al-Adha until after prayer is a separate sunnah, even without a sacrifice.

This lesson covers the recommended acts (mustahabbat) specific to Eid al-Adha, as stated by Imam al-Quduri. These acts are rooted in the Prophet's practice, which serves as the primary proof. Understanding these sunan helps you align your worship with the prophetic model and avoid common misconceptions, such as thinking that delaying eating only applies to those who sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Recommended Acts
From the text, list the three acts described as mustahabb or sunnah on Eid al-Adha: performing ghusl (bath), applying perfume, and delaying eating until after the Eid prayer.
The text also mentions eating from one's sacrifice, but that is a separate sunnah tied to sacrifice.
2
Determine the Hukm Level
Recognize that these acts are classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) or mustahabb. They are not obligatory, but following them is praiseworthy.
In Hanafi terminology, mustahabb is often synonymous with sunnah in this context.
3
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof cited is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not eat on the day of Nahr until he returned from prayer and ate from his sacrifice. This is a specific narrated practice showing recommendation.
The hadith is not given with a full chain, but it is accepted as sound in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice of delaying eating indicates it is a recommended act (sunnah). The fact that he would eat from his own sacrifice shows the connection, but the text clarifies that delaying eating is a separate sunnah, valid even without a sacrifice.
The phrase 'ما روى' indicates a narrated action as the basis.
5
Apply the Exception for Villagers
The text adds an exception: villagers (those living outside the city where Eid prayer is not obligatory) are permitted to eat before the prayer because the obligation of attending Eid prayer is not upon them.
This shows that the ruling is tied to the obligation of the prayer; where prayer is not fard, the recommendation is relaxed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب في يوم الاضحى ان يغتسل ويتطيب لما ذكرناه ويؤخر الاكل حتى يفرغ من الصلوة لما روى ان النبي كان لا يطعم فى يوم النحر حتى يرجع فياكل من اضحيته ترجمہ اور بقر عید کے دن غسل کرنا اور خوشبو لگانا مستحب ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور کھانے کو مؤخر کرے یہاں تک کہ نماز سے فارغ ہو جائے کیونکہ مروی ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم بقر عید کے دن کھاتے نہ تھے یہاں تک کہ نماز سے واپس ہوتے پھر اپنی قربانی سے کھاتے تھے ۔ تشریح . صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ بقر عید کے دن غسل کرنا اور خوشبو لگانا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے اور یہ بھی مسنون ہے کہ کھانا نماز کے بعد کھائے اور اپنی قربانی سے کھائے۔ دلیل آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل ہے کہ آپ بقر عید کے دن نماز عید کے بعد کھانا تناول فرماتے تھے اور اپنی قربانی سے تناول فرماتے تھے اگر کسی نے قربانی نہیں کی تب بھی نماز عید سے پہلے نہ کھائی کیونکہ عید سے پہلے نہ کھانا الگ سنت ہے اور اپنی قربانی سے کھان الگ سنت ہے ہاں گاؤں والوں لئے جائز ہے کیونکہ وہاں نماز واجب نہیں ہے۔
It is mustahabb (recommended) on the day of Adha to perform ghusl and apply perfume, for the reason we mentioned, and to delay eating until after finishing the prayer, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not eat on the day of Nahr until he returned and then ate from his sacrifice. Translation: On the day of Eid al-Adha (Baqra Eid), performing ghusl and applying perfume are mustahabb, based on the proof we mentioned earlier. And he should delay eating until after finishing the prayer, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to not eat on the day of Nahr until he returned from prayer and then ate from his sacrifice. Commentary: Al-Quduri said that on the day of Eid al-Adha, ghusl and perfume are mustahabb. The proof has passed earlier. And it is also sunnah to eat after the prayer and to eat from one's own sacrifice. The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to eat after the Eid prayer and eat from his sacrifice. If someone has not sacrificed, he still should not eat before the Eid prayer, because not eating before the Eid prayer is a separate sunnah, and eating from one's sacrifice is a separate sunnah. Yes, for villagers it is permissible (to eat before), because there the Eid prayer is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage lists the mustahabbat (recommended acts) for Eid al-Adha, as stated by al-Quduri. These include: performing ghusl, applying perfume, and delaying eating until after the Eid prayer and then eating from one's sacrifice. The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated. Even if one has not sacrificed, one should still delay eating until after the prayer, as the delay itself is a separate sunnah. For villagers where Eid prayer may not be obligatory (i.e., not fard, but perhaps sunnah), it is permissible to eat before.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is encouraged but not obligatory.
اضحية (udhiyah): Sacrificial animal offered on Eid al-Adha.

Sunnah Acts of Eid: Takbir, Prayer, and Khutbah
Describing sunnah acts while going to Eid musalla and the prayer format

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts related to going to the Eid musalla and performing the Eid prayer, and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Saying takbir aloud on the way and giving two khutbahs after Eid prayer are sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's action.

This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines the sunnah practices for Eid al-Adha and, by analogy, Eid al-Fitr. The author emphasizes three elements: saying takbir aloud on the way to the musalla, performing two rak'ahs of prayer, and delivering two khutbahs after. The purpose of the khutbah is to teach about sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq. Understanding these sunnah acts allows one to follow the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
List the sunnah acts
Identify each act: takbir on the way, two-rak'ah prayer, two khutbahs.
These are explicitly mentioned in the text.
2
Identify the hukm level
The text and commentary affirm these are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah is a level between wajib and mustahab.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's practice as transmitted: 'because he used to say takbir on the way' and 'because he did so.'
The dalil is ahad hadith but sufficient for sunnah.
4
Understand the purpose of the khutbah
The khutbah was legislated specifically to teach the rulings of udhiyah and takbir al-tashriq.
The text says: 'the khutbah was only prescribed for teaching.'
5
Apply to practice
Today, imams should follow these sunnah acts in both Eid prayers.
These are established practices, not optional.

And he proceeds to the musalla while saying takbir, because he (the Prophet) used to say takbir on the way. And he prays two rak'ahs like (Eid) al-Fitr; similarly it is transmitted. And he delivers two khutbahs after it, because he (the Prophet) did so. And he teaches the people in them about the sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq, because this is legislated for the time, and the khutbah was only legislated for teaching. Translation: He goes to the Eid musalla while saying takbir aloud, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say takbir on the way. And the imam prays two rak'ahs like Eid al-Fitr; this is transmitted similarly. And after the prayer he delivers two khutbahs, because the Prophet did so. And in both khutbahs he teaches about the sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq, because this is what is prescribed for the time; and the khutbah was only prescribed for this teaching. Commentary: The ruling is that while going to the Eid musalla, he should say takbir aloud, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do that.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah acts for going to the Eid prayer and the format of the prayer itself. It is sunnah to say takbir (Allahu Akbar) aloud on the way to the musalla, following the practice of the Prophet. The Eid prayer is two rak'ahs, exactly like Eid al-Fitr. After the prayer, the imam delivers two khutbahs, in which he teaches the people about the sacrifice (udhiyah) and the takbir al-tashriq (the takbirat said after fard prayers during the days of tashriq). The khutbah was legislated specifically for the purpose of teaching these matters.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' aloud on the way to Eid prayer.
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The prescribed takbirat said after fard prayers from Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah to Asr of 13th.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) To announce the next prayer.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Eid includes saying takbir aloud on the way, praying two rak'ahs, and delivering two khutbahs focused on teaching the rulings of sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq.

Delaying Eid Salah Due to a Valid Excuse
Rulings on postponing Eid salah when a valid excuse prevents it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for delaying Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha prayers due to a valid excuse, and identify the hadith proof and its application.

Core Idea
Eid prayer delayed for a valid excuse remains ada (on-time) not qada, but only within one day for Fitr and three days for Adha.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi position on postponing Eid salah when a valid excuse (udhr) prevents its performance on the prescribed day. It distinguishes between Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, citing a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. The key principle is that delay is permissible only to a limited extent, and without excuse, it is sinful though valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the hukm (wajib) and the specific act being considered: delaying Eid salah due to a valid excuse.
Eid prayer is wajib per Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith about sighting the moon after noon and the Prophet ordering prayer the next day.
Hadith text: 'When they testified to sighting the new moon after noon, he ordered going out to the musalla the next day.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the permissibility of a one-day delay? The word 'amara' indicates a command, and 'min al-ghad' limits the delay to one day.
The command implies permissibility/necessity; the phrase specifies duration.
4
Apply to Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha
For Eid al-Fitr, delay only one day (2nd Shawwal). For Eid al-Adha, up to three days (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) because the prayer is tied to the days of sacrifice.
If an excuse persists on the last allowed day, no further delay is permitted.
5
Note consequence of delay without excuse
The prayer is valid (sahih) but the person is sinful (ithm) for contradicting transmitted practice.
The prayer is still considered ada, not qada.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم ۳۲۳ بات العيدين دیکھنے کی گواہی دی اور امام نے ان کی گواہی قبول بھی کر لی تو روزہ توڑ دیں اور امام دوسرے دن لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے دیہ تا خیر عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے اس تاخیر میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اس تاخیر کے سلسلہ میں حدیث بھی موجود ہے چنانچہ ہدایہے گذشتہ صفحہ پر یہ حدیث اس طرح ذکر کی گئی ہے ولما شهد و ابالهلال بعد الزوال امر بالخروج الى المصلى من الغد اور اگر دو شوال کو بھی کوئی ایسا عذر پایا گیا جو نماز عید کے لئے مانع ہو تو اب اس کے بعد 3 شوال کو نماز عید پڑھنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نماز عید میں اصل تو یہی کہ اس کی قضاء نہ کی جائے جیسے جمعہ فوت ہونے کی صورت میں اس کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی لیکن عذر کی وجہ سے دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے میں حدیث مذکور کی وجہ سے اس اصل کو ترک کر دیا گیا ہے پس چونکہ حدیث کے اندر فقط دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کرنے کی تصریح کی گئی ہے اس لئے ۲ شوال تک نماز عید مؤخر کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی اس کے بعد اجازت نہ ہوگی ۔
فان كان عذر يمنع من الصلوة فى يوم الاضحى صلاها من الغدو بعد الغدو لا يصليها بعد ذلك لان الصلوة موقتة بوقت الاضحية فيقدر بايامها لكنه مسئ فى التاخير من غير عذر لمخالفة المنقول ترجمہ ... پس اگر کوئی عذر ائیں اہو جو دسویں ذی الحجہ کو نماز عید پڑھنے سے مانع ہو تو دوسری یا تیسرے روز نماز پڑھے اور اس کے بعد نہ پڑھے کیونکہ بقر عید کی نماز ایام اضحیہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے لہذا اس کا وقت بھی اضحیہ کے ایام کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا لیکن بغیر عذر تا خیر کرنے میں وہ گنہگار ہوگا کیونکہ منقول سے مخالفت کی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ذی الحجہ کی دسویں تاریخ میں مانع صلوۃ عذر پایا گیا تو گیارہویں تاریخ میں نماز پڑھے اور اگر گیارہویں تاریخ میں بھی عذر باقی رہا تو بار ہوئیں میں نماز عید پڑھے۔ اور اگر اس میں بھی عذر موجود ہے تو اس کے بعد تاخیر کی اجازت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ بقرعید کی نماز الضحیہ (قربانی) کے ساتھ مقید ہے اس لئے نماز کا وقت بھی اضحیہ کے ایام تک مقید ہوگا۔ پس قربانی کے تین روز تک ہر روز آفتاب بلند ہونے کے بعد زوال تک نماز عید کا وقت رہے گا اور اگر تاخیر کرنا بغیر عذر ہوا تو بھی نماز جائز ہے۔ لیکن بغیر عذر تاخیر کرنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا کیونکہ حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم اور خلفاء راشدین سے ایسی ناظر منقول نہیں ہے یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ نماز باوجود تاخیر کے ادا ہے نہ کہ قضاء کیونکہ اپنے وقت میں میں واقع ہوئی ہے۔
From Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Volume 2, page 323, Chapter of the Two Eids: If the moon is sighted after noon and the imam accepts the testimony, then they break the fast and the imam leads the people in prayer the next day. The proof is that the delay is due to an excuse, so there is no harm in this delay, and there is a hadith regarding this delay. As mentioned in Hidayah on the previous page: 'When they testified to sighting the new moon after noon, he ordered going out to the musalla the next day.' And if on the 2nd of Shawwal there is also an excuse preventing the Eid prayer, then after that there is no permission to pray Eid on the 3rd of Shawwal, because the original ruling for Eid prayer is that it is not made up, like when Jumu'ah is missed it is not made up. But due to the excuse, delaying to the next day is allowed, and the original ruling is abandoned because of the hadith. Since the hadith only specifies postponement to the next day, permission is only for the 2nd of Shawwal, not beyond. 
Then if there is an excuse preventing the prayer on the day of Adha, he prays it on the next day or the day after, and does not pray after that, because the prayer is tied to the time of sacrifice, so its time is limited to those days. But without an excuse, the one who delays is sinful for contradicting what is transmitted. Translation: So if an excuse arises that prevents the Eid prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, he prays on the 2nd or 3rd day, and after that not, because the Eid of Sacrifice is tied to the days of sacrifice, so its time is limited to those days. But without excuse, he is sinful for delaying. 
Commentary: The issue is that if on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah there is an excuse preventing prayer, then pray on the 11th; if the excuse remains on the 11th, then pray on the 12th; if excuse remains there as well, no further delay is allowed. The proof is that the Eid of Sacrifice is tied to the days of sacrifice, so the time for prayer is limited to the days of sacrifice. So on each of the three days, after sunrise until noon, the time for Eid prayer remains. If the delay is without excuse, the prayer is still valid, but he is sinful for delaying without excuse because no such practice is transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Note that this prayer, even with delay, is performance (ada) not make-up (qada) because it occurred within its time.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on delaying Eid salah due to a valid excuse. It covers both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. For Eid al-Fitr: if the moon is sighted after noon on 30th Ramadan (which would make it 1st Shawwal), but the prayer cannot be held that day due to the delay, the imam accepts the testimony, breaks his fast, and leads the Eid prayer the next day (2nd Shawwal). This is based on a hadith where the Prophet ordered going to the musalla the next day when the moon was sighted after noon. However, if an excuse arises on the 2nd Shawwal as well, the prayer cannot be further delayed to the 3rd, because the original principle is that Eid is not made up (qada) like Jumu'ah. The exception for one day delay comes from the hadith, which only permits one day. For Eid al-Adha: if an excuse prevents prayer on the 10th Dhul Hijjah, it can be delayed to the 11th or 12th (since the days of sacrifice are three). After that, no delay is allowed because the prayer is tied to the time of sacrifice (ayyam al-adha). Without a valid excuse, delaying is sinful because it contradicts the sunnah of performing it on the first day, but the prayer itself is still valid and considered ada (on time) because it is performed within the permissible time window. The commentary explains that the time for Eid al-Adha prayer extends over three days from sunrise to noon each day, but only if there is an excuse for delay; otherwise, it should be on the 10th.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that prevents performing Eid salah on its prescribed day, such as extreme weather, illness, or delayed moon sighting.
ادا (ada): Performance of a prayer within its prescribed time. The delayed Eid prayer is still ada because it falls within the extended time due to excuse.
قضاء (qada): Make-up prayer performed after the valid time has passed. The text clarifies that the delayed Eid is not qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum number of days Eid al-Adha can be delayed if a valid excuse exists?
A) 1 day
B) 2 days
C) 3 days
D) 4 days

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer delayed for a valid excuse remains ada and is limited to one day for Fitr and three days for Adha; delay without excuse is sinful but valid.

Sunnah Acts of the Eid Prayer
Lists sunnah acts of Eid prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts of the Eid prayer (takbir on the way, two rak'ahs, and two khutbahs) and explain their purpose based on the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Eid prayer's sunnah acts are established by the Prophet's consistent practice and have specific educational aims.

Eid prayer is a unique congregational worship with specific sunnah acts that distinguish it from the five daily prayers. This lesson covers three key sunnah acts: saying takbir aloud on the way to the prayer, praying two rak'ahs, and delivering two khutbahs after the prayer. Understanding these acts helps you perform Eid in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnah acts
List the three sunnah acts mentioned: (1) saying takbir aloud on the way to the musalla, (2) praying two rak'ahs like Eid al-Fitr, (3) delivering two khutbahs after the prayer.
These are all sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the proof for each act
For each act, note the proof given: the Prophet's action (he used to do so). The text explicitly links each act to the Prophet's practice.
The proof is dalil naqli (transmitted evidence).
3
Understand the purpose of the khutbah
The text states that the khutbah is legislated for teaching: teaching the rulings of sacrifice (udhiyah) and takbir al-tashriq.
This purpose distinguishes Eid khutbah from Jumu'ah khutbah.
4
Differentiate from Jumu'ah
Note that the Eid khutbah comes after the prayer, unlike Jumu'ah where the khutbah precedes the prayer.
This is a key structural difference.

راستہ میں جہرا تکبیر کہنے کا حکم ويتوجه الى المصلى وهو يكبر لانه كان يكبر فى الطريق ويصلى ركعتين كالفطر كذلك نقل ويخطب بعدها خطبتين لانه كذلك فعل ويعلم الناس فيها الاضحية و تكبير التشريق لانه مشروع الوقت والخطبة ما شرعت الالتعليمه ترجمہ اور عید گاہ جائے درانحالیکہ تکبیر کہتا ہو کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم راہ میں تکبیر کہتے تھے اور امام عید الفطر کی طرح دو رکعت پڑھے۔ ایسا ہی نقل کیا گیا ہے اور نماز کے بعد دو خطبہ پڑھے کیونکہ مدنی آقا نے ایسا ہی کیا ہے اور دونوں خطبوں میں قربانی اور تکبیر تشریق کی تعلیم کرے کیونکہ اس وقت کس مشروع یہی ہے۔ اور خطبہ نہیں مشروع ہوا مگر اسی تعلیم کے واسطے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عید گاہ جاتے ہوئے راستہ میں باآواز بلند تکبیر کہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم بھی یہ مل فرمایا کرتے تھے۔ اور عید قربان عید الفطر کی طرح دو رکعت ہیں۔ امام صاحب سے یہی منقول ہے۔ نماز کے بعد دو خطبہ کے احکام سکھا ئے کیونکہ ان ایک میں یہی چیزیں مشروع ہیں اور خطبہ انہیں چیزوں کی تعلیم کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے۔
Ruling on saying takbir aloud on the way: He goes to the musalla while saying takbir because he (the Prophet) used to say takbir on the way. He prays two rak'ahs like (Eid) al-Fitr; thus it is transmitted. And he delivers two khutbahs after it because he (the Prophet) did so. And he teaches the people in them about the sacrifice and the takbir of tashriq because that is what is legislated for that time. And the khutbah was only legislated for teaching. Translation: He goes to the Eidgah while saying takbir aloud because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say takbir on the way. And the imam prays two rak'ahs like Eid al-Fitr; thus it is transmitted. And after the prayer he delivers two khutbahs because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. And in both khutbahs he teaches about sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq because that is what is legislated for that time. And the khutbah was only legislated for this teaching. Commentary: The issue is that while going to the Eidgah, he says takbir aloud on the way because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do so. And Eid al-Adha is two rak'ahs like Eid al-Fitr; this is transmitted from Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa). After the prayer, he delivers two khutbahs teaching the rulings because these matters are legislated in them, and the khutbah was only legislated for teaching these things.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage provides the sunnah rulings for the Eid prayer procedure. It covers four aspects: (1) Going to the musalla (Eidgah) while reciting takbir aloud (jahar) because the Prophet did so. (2) The prayer consists of two rak'ahs, identical in form to Eid al-Fitr. This is the transmitted position from Imam Abu Hanifa. (3) After the prayer, the imam delivers two khutbahs (sermons), just as the Prophet did. (4) The content of the khutbahs should include teaching about the sacrifice (udhiyah) and the takbir al-tashriq (the extra takbirs recited after every fard prayer from the 10th to the 12th of Dhul Hijjah). The text emphasizes that the khutbah is legislated solely for the purpose of teaching these matters to the people. The commentary reiterates these points, specifying that takbir is recited aloud on the way, and the two rak'ahs are exactly like those of Eid al-Fitr. The khutbahs are meant to educate the congregation about the important rituals of the day.

Key Terms
تکبیر تشریق (takbir al-tashriq): The extra takbirs recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah until Asr of the 13th (for the Hanafi school). In this context, it is taught in the Eid khutbah.
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer; two khutbahs are sunnah, and their purpose is to teach the congregation about the rulings of sacrifice and takbir al-tashriq.

D) The rulings of Zakat

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer includes three sunnah acts: takbir on the way, two rak'ahs, and two khutbahs after the prayer for teaching.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Ruling on Delaying Eid al-Adha Prayer Due to an Excuse
Gives ruling and proof for delaying Eid prayer within days of udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer due to an excuse, identify the proof (dalil) based on qiyas with udhiyah, and explain why delaying without excuse is sinful yet valid.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days if excused; without excuse it's sinful but valid.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: what happens if a legitimate excuse prevents performing the Eid prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling grounded in qiyas with the days of udhiyah. We will explore the legal reasoning and the distinction between valid delay and sinful delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer beyond its primary time (10th of Dhul Hijjah). The ruling: if done due to an excuse, it is permissible within the 11th and 12th; if done without excuse, it is sinful (makruh tahrimi) but the prayer remains valid.
The prayer is considered ada (on time) within these days.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas: the prayer is tied (muqayyad) to the days of udhiyah (sacrifice). Since udhiyah is legislated for three days, the prayer's time is similarly confined.
This is a dalil aqli (reasoning by analogy).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The link is that both the prayer and the sacrifice are legislated for the same occasion (Eid al-Adha). The Prophet and caliphs prayed on the 10th, but if prevented, the time extends as long as the sacrifice is valid (three days).
The prayer's time is sunrise to zawal on each of those days.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may allow delay beyond the 12th or consider the prayer qada if delayed. The Hanafi school restricts it to three days based on the link to udhiyah.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because it follows the transmitted practice (manqul) of the Prophet and caliphs, and the qiyas is sound. Delaying without excuse contradicts that practice, hence sinful.
The mufta bihi is as stated in the text.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين
اور عید قربان عید الفطر کی طرح دو رکعت ہیں۔ امام صاحب سے یہی منقول ہے۔ نماز کے بعد دو خطبہ کے احکام سکھا ئے کیونکہ ان ایک میں یہی چیزیں مشروع ہیں اور خطبہ انہیں چیزوں کی تعلیم کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے۔
کسی مانع کی وجہ سے پہلے دن عید نہیں پڑھی ، دوسرے دن یا پھر تیسرے دن پڑھ لیں
فان كان عذر يمنع من الصلوة فى يوم الاضحى صلاها من الغدو بعد الغدو لا يصليها بعد ذلك لان الصلوة موقتة بوقت الاضحية فيقدر بايامها لكنه مسئ فى التاخير من غير عذر لمخالفة المنقول ترجمہ ... پس اگر کوئی عذر ائیں ہو جو دسویں ذی الحجہ کو نماز عید پڑھنے سے مانع ہو تو دوسری یا تیسرے روز نماز پڑھے اور اس کے بعد نہ پڑھے کیونکہ بقرعید کی نماز ایام اضحیہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے لہذا اس کا وقت بھی اضحیہ کے ایام کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا لیکن بغیر عذر تا خیر کرنے میں وہ گنہگار ہوگا کیونکہ منقول سے مخالفت کی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ذی الحجہ کی دسویں تاریخ میں مانع صلوۃ عذر پایا گیا تو گیارہویں تاریخ میں نماز پڑھے اور اگر گیارہویں تاریخ میں بھی عذر باقی رہا تو بار ہوئیں میں نماز عید پڑھے۔ اور اگر اس میں بھی عذر موجود ہے تو اس کے بعد تاخیر کی اجازت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ بقرعید کی نماز الضحیہ (قربانی) کے ساتھ مقید ہے اس لئے نماز کا وقت بھی اضحیہ کے ایام تک مقید ہوگا۔ پس قربانی کے تین روز تک ہر روز آفتاب بلند ہونے کے بعد زوال تک نماز عید کا وقت رہے گا اور اگر تاخیر کرنا بغیر عذر ہوا تو بھی نماز جائز ہے۔ لیکن بغیر عذر تاخیر کرنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور خلفاء راشدین سے ایسی نقل منقول نہیں ہے یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ نماز باوجود تاخیر کے ادا ہے نہ کہ قضاء کیونکہ اپنے وقت میں واقع ہوئی ہے۔
Chapter of the Two Eids. Eid al-Adha is two rak'ahs like Eid al-Fitr. This is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. After the prayer, two sermons: because these things are legislated in both Eids, and the sermon is legislated for teaching these things. If there is an excuse preventing prayer on the day of Adha, one prays it the next day or the day after, and not after that, because the prayer is tied to the time of udhiyah, so it is confined to its days. But one who delays without excuse is sinful for opposing the transmitted practice. Explanation: If on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah there is an excuse, pray on the 11th; if excuse remains, pray on the 12th; if still excuse, no further delay. The prayer time is limited to the three days of udhiyah, from sunrise to zawal each day. Delaying without excuse is valid but sinful because it is not transmitted from the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. This prayer is ada, not qada, because it falls within its time.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Eids gives the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer due to an excuse. It states the prayer can be performed on the 11th or 12th of Dhul Hijjah if prevented on the 10th, but not after the 12th. The proof is that the prayer is tied to the days of udhiyah (sacrifice), analogous to the sacrifice itself. Delaying without an excuse is makruh tahrimi (sinful) because it contradicts the transmitted practice of the Prophet and caliphs, but the prayer itself remains valid and is considered ada (on time), not qada, because it is still within the legislated window. The commentary emphasizes that the prayer's time is from sunrise to zawal on each of the three days.

Key Terms
عذر (uthr): A valid excuse (e.g., rain, travel, illness) that prevents attending the Eid prayer.
صلاة العيد (salat al-'id): The two-rak'ah prayer performed on Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only on the 10th
B) 10th and 11th only
C) 11th and 12th only
D) Up to 13th

Key Takeaway
The Eid al-Adha prayer can be performed on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah; delaying without excuse is sinful (makruh tahrimi) but the prayer remains valid (ada).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Timing of Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on end time of Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq end after 'Asr of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn extend them to the last Tashrīq day.

This passage tackles a notable intra-Hanafi difference concerning the Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq, the special takbirs recited after fard prayers during Eid al-Adha. While all agree these takbirs are wajib, the point of disagreement is when they cease. Abu Hanifa, relying on Ibn Mas'ud, stops them after 'Asr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The Sahibayn, following Ali, continue until 'Asr on the 13th. Understanding this dispute clarifies how a single school can accommodate multiple valid positions and how the mufta bihi is determined.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the starting and ending points for the Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq according to Abu Hanifa: start after Fajr of 'Arafah (9th), end after 'Asr of Nahr (10th).
This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the takbirs continue until 'Asr of the last day of Tashrīq (13th).
This is a valid intra-school difference, though not the relied-upon view.
3
Follow each side's dalil
Abu Hanifa relies on Ibn Mas'ud (shorter period to avoid bid'ah). The Sahibayn rely on Ali (longer period out of ihtiyat).
Both are Companion practices, showing ikhtilaf among the Sahaba.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that prolonging the takbir could lead to innovation; the sahih sunnah is the shorter period.
The school's tarjih mechanism prioritizes the stronger evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi following the mufta bihi stops on the 10th; one following the Sahibayn continues through the 13th.
In fatwa, Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon.

فصل في تكبيرات التشريق
(یہ) فصل تکبیرات تشریق (کے بیان میں ) ہے
تکبیرات تشریق کا بیان تکبیر تشریق کا آغاز کب ہوگا اور اختتام کب ہوگا
ويبدأ بتكبير التشريق بعد صلاة الفجر من يوم عرفة ويختم عقيب صلاة العصر من يوم النحر عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يختم عقيب صلاة العصر من آخر أيام التشريق والمسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة فأخذا بقول علي أخذا بالأكثر لأنه الاحتياط في العبادات وأخذ بقول ابن مسعود أخذا بالأقل لأن الجهر بالتكبير بدعة والتكبير أن يقول مرة واحدة الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد هذا هو المأثور عن الخليل صلوات الله عليه
ترجمہ اور عرفہ کے دن نماز فجر کے بعد تکبیر تشریق شروع کرنے اور یوم نحر کو نماز عصر کے بعد ختم کرے (یہ حکم) ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ آخری ایام تشریق کو عصر کی نماز کے بعد ختم کرے امام صاحب کے درمیان مختلف پایا گیا ہے پس صاحبین نے اکثر کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے حضرت علی کے قول کو لیا ہے کیونکہ عبادت میں یہی احتیاط ہے اور ابو حنیفہ نے اقل کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے ابن مسعودؓ کے قول کو لیا ہے کیونکہ جہر کے ساتھ تکبیر کرنا بدعت ہے اور تکبیر یہ ہے کہ ایک بار کہے اللہ اکبر اللہ اکبر لا الہ الا اللہ والله اكبر الله اكبر ولله الحمد یہی حضرت ابراہیم علیہ السلام سے منقول ہے۔ تشریح تشریق خود تکبیر ہے تو اب معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ ان تکبیرات کے بیان میں جن کا نام تشریق ہے عنایہ میں ہے کہ تکبیر تشریق چونکہ ایام اضحیہ کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے اس لئے علیحدہ فصل میں ذکر کیا ہے کفایہ میں ہے کہ تکبیرات کی اضافت تشریق کی طرف صاحبین کے قول پر درست ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک بعض تکبیریں ایام تشریق یعنی گیارہویں بارہویں اور تیرہویں تاریخ میں بھی واقع ہوتی ہیں۔ لیکن ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یوم نحر یعنی دسویں ذی الحجہ کی عصر کی نماز کے بعد تکبیر ختم ہو جاتی ہے حالانکہ ایام تشریق کا آغاز گیارہویں ذی الحجہ سے ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ خلاصہ کے حوالہ سے صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر فرمایا ہے کہ ایام نحر تین ہیں۔ اور ایام تشریق بھی تین ہیں اس طرح پر کہ ذی الحجہ کی دسویں تاریخ خاص طور پر یوم نحر ہے اور تیرہویں تاریخ خاص طور پر یوم تشریق ہے اور گیارہویں اور بارہویں نحر اور تشریق دونوں کے لئے ہیں ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تکبیرات تشریق کا عنوان کس طرح درست ہوگا اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ اگر چہ یوم نحر ہے۔ یوم تشریق نہیں ہے۔ مگر یوم تشریق یعنی گیارہویں ذی الحجہ سے قریب ہے۔ اس قرب کی وجہ سے تشریق کی طرف تکبیرات کی اضافت کی گئی ہے جیسا کہ جامع صغیر میں ہے قال یعقوب صلیت بهم المغرب يوم عرفة یعقوب نے کہا ہے کہ میں نے ان کو عرفہ کے دن مغرب کی نماز پڑھائی حالانکہ آفتاب غروب ہوتے ہی عرفہ کا دن ختم ہو گیا مگر چونکہ مغرب کا وقت عرفہ کے دن سے قریب ہے اس لئے یوم عرفہ کہہ دیا گیا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ تشریق سے مراد عید الاضحی کی نماز ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے لا جمعة ولا تشريق إلا في مصر جامع اور دوسری حدیث میں ہے لا ذبح إلا بعد التشريق دونوں حدیثوں میں تشریق سے مراد نماز عید ہے پس اس صورت میں
Section on Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq. Statement of Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq: when does it begin and end. It begins after Fajr prayer on the day of 'Arafah and ends after 'Asr prayer on the day of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: it ends after 'Asr of the last day of Tashrīq. The matter is disputed among the Companions: the two took the view of Ali (taking the majority, because it is caution in worship), and Abu Hanifa took the view of Ibn Mas'ud (taking the minimum, because loud takbir is an innovation). The takbir is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd. This is transmitted from Khalil (Abraham) peace be upon him. ... Explanation: The word 'tashrīq' itself means takbir. ... Two answers are given for the name 'Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq' under Abu Hanifa's view: 1) proximity of the 10th to the day of Tashrīq, 2) tashrīq refers to the Eid prayer as in hadith.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This section details the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of the Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq, the special takbirs recited after fard prayers during the Eid al-Adha period. According to Abu Hanifa, they begin after Fajr on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (day of 'Arafah) and end after 'Asr on the 10th (day of Nahr). His two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that they end after 'Asr on the 13th (last day of Tashrīq). Each side relies on a different Companion report: Sahibayn adopt the view of Ali (holding the longer period as ihtiyat/caution), while Abu Hanifa follows Ibn Mas'ud (holding the shorter period because loud takbir could become bid'ah). The text also gives the precise wording of the takbir. Then it addresses the terminological issue: how can these takbirs be called 'Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq' if Abu Hanifa cuts them off before the days of Tashrīq? Two explanations: (1) the 10th is adjacent to the first Tashrīq day, and (2) the word 'tashrīq' in hadith refers to the Eid prayer itself.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The specific takbirs recited after fard prayers from the day of 'Arafah through the days of Tashrīq.
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, when do the Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq end?
A) After Fajr of 'Arafah
B) After 'Asr of the day of Nahr
C) After 'Asr of the 13th
D) After Maghrib of the 12th

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq end after 'Asr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, but a valid intra-school opinion extends them to the 13th.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Takbīr al-Tashrīq: Timing, Ruling, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains beginning, end, obligation, and wording of Takbīr al-Tashrīq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing of Takbīr al-Tashrīq according to Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn, identify the mufta bihi position, and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school has two positions on when Takbīr al-Tashrīq ends; the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) extends it to the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of Takbīr al-Tashrīq, its ruling (wajib vs sunnah), and its wording. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi imams resolved conflicting companion traditions, balancing caution in worship against avoiding innovation. We will follow the commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core dispute is the timing of the end of Takbīr al-Tashrīq: after 'Asr of Yawm al-Nahr (10th) or after 'Asr of the last day of Tashrīq (13th).
The beginning (after Fajr of 9th) is uncontested within the Hanafi school.
2
State Abu Hanifah's position
Abu Hanifah holds that the takbīr ends after 'Asr of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, following the view of Ibn Mas'ud.
This results in 8 prayers.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the takbīr ends after 'Asr of the 13th, following the view of 'Ali.
This results in 23 prayers.
4
Trace the companion sources and reasoning
Abu Hanifah follows Ibn Mas'ud to minimize bid'ah (raising voice); Sahibayn follow 'Ali for caution in worship.
Both rely on sound companion traditions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and ruling level
Practice and fatwa are upon the Sahibayn's view (ends 13th). The majority of Hanafis consider the takbīr wajib based on Quran 2:203.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah explicitly chooses the Sahibayn's view.
