فصل في تكبيرات التشريق (یہ) فصل تکبیرات تشریق (کے بیان میں ) ہے تکبیرات تشریق کا بیان تکبیر تشریق کا آغاز کب ہوگا اور اختتام کب ہوگا

ويبدأ بتكبير التشريق بعد صلوة الفجر من يوم عرفة ويختم عقيب صلواة العصر من يوم النحر عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يختم عقيب صلواة العصر من اخر ايام التشريق والمسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة فاخذا بقول على اخذا بالاكثر اذهو الاحتياط فى العبادات واخذ بقول ابن مسعود اخدا بالاقل لان الجهر با لتكبير بدعة والتكبير ان يقول مرة واحدة الله اكبر الله اكبر لا اله الا الله والله اكبر الله اكبر و الله الحمد هذا هو الماثور عن الخليل صلوات الله عليه

ترجمہ اور عرفہ کے دن نما فجر کے بعد تکبیر تشریق شروع کرنے اور یوم نحر کونماز عصر کے بعد ختم کرے (یہ حکم ) ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ آخری ایام تشریق کو عصر کی نماز کے بعد ختم کرے امام صاحب کے درمیان مختلف پایا گیا ہے پس صاحبین نے اکثر کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے حضرت علی کے قول کو لیا ہے کیونکہ عبادت میں یہی احتیاط ہے اور ابو حنیفہ نے اقل کو اختیار کرتے ہوئی ابن مسعودؓ کے قول کو لیا ہی کیونکہ جہر کے ساتھ تکبیر کرنا بدعت ہی اور تکبیر یہ ہے کہ ایک بار کہے اللہ اکبر اللہ اکبر لا الاه الا الله والله اكبر الله اکبر ولله الحمد یہی حضرت ابراہیم علیہ السلام سے منقول ہے۔ تشریح تشریق خود تکبیر ہی تو اب معنی یہ ہوں گے کہ ان تکبیرات کے بیان میں جن کا نام تشریق ہے عنایہ میں ہے کہ تکبیر تشریق چونکہ ایام اضحیہ کیسا تھ مخصوص ہے اس لئے علیحدہ فصل میں ذکر کیا ہے کفایہ میں ہے کہ تکبیرات کی اضافت تشریف کی طرف صاحبین کے قول پر درست ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک بعض تکبیریں ایام تشریق یعنی گیارہویں بارہویں اور تیرہویں تاریخ میں بھی واقع ہوتی ہیں۔ لیکن ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یوم تحریعنی دسویں ذی الحجہ کی عصر کی نماز کے بعد تکبیر ختم ہو جاتی ہے حالانکہ ایام تشریق کا آغاز گیارہویں ذی الحجہ سے ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ خلاصہ کے حوالہ سے صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر فرمایا ہے کہ ایام نحرمین ہیں۔ اور ایام تشریق بھی تین ہیں اس طرح پر کہ ذی الحجہ کی دسویں تاریخ خاص طور پر یوم نحر ہے اور تیرہویں تاریخ خاص طور پر یوم تشریق ہے اور گیارہویں اور بارہویں نحر اور تشریق دونوں کے لئے ہیں ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تکبیرات تشریق کا عنوان کس طرح درست ہوگا اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ اگر چہ یوم نحر ہے۔ یوم تشریق نہیں ہے۔ مگر یوم تشریق یعنی گیارہویں ذی الحجہ سے قریب ہے۔ اس قرب کی وجہ سے تشریق کی طرف تکبیرات کی اضافت کی گئی ہے جیسا کہ جامع صغیر میں ہے قال یعقوب صليت بهم المغرب يوم عرفة یعقوب نے کہا ہے کہ میں نے ان کو عرفہ کے دن مغرب کی نماز پڑھائی حالانکہ آفتاب غروب ہوتے ہی عرفہ کا دم ختم ہو گیا مگر چونکہ مغرب کا وقت عرفہ کے دن سے قریب ہے اس لئے یوم عرفہ کہہ دیا گیا۔ دوسرا جواب یہی کہ تشریق سے مراد عید الاضحی کی نماز ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے لا جمعة ولا تشريق الافي مصر جامع اور دوسری حدیث میں ہے لا ذبح الا بعد التشريق دونوں حدیثوں میں تشریق سے مراد نماز عید ہے پس اس صورت میں بالا تفاق اضافت درست ہوگی رہی یہ بات کہ تکبیر تشریق واجب ہے یا سنت ہے تو اکثر علماء وجوب کے قائل ہیں اور بعض مسنون ہونے کے قائل ہیں دلیل وجوب باری تعالیٰ کا قول [واذكروا] الله في ايام معدودات ہے اور [سنت؟] کے قائلین نے ان پر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی مداومت اور ہمیشگی فرمانے کی دلیل بنایا ہے۔ تکبیرات تشریق کی ابتداء اور انتہا میں چونکہ صحابہ کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے ائمہ کے درمیان بھی یہ مسئلہ مختلف فیہ رہا ہے کبار صحابہ مثلاً حضرت عمر علی ، ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہم فرماتے ہیں کہ تکبیرات تشریق کی ابتداء عرفہ کے دن یعنی ذی الحجہ کی نویں تاریخ سے کی جائے گی اس کو بالا تفاق علماء احناف نے اختیار کیا ہے اور صغار صحابہ مثلاً عبداللہ بن عباس عبد اللہ بن عمر زید بن ثابت نے کہا کہ یوم تخریعہ بقر عید کے دن کی ظہر سے تکبیرات کا آغاز کیا جائے گا انتہا کے سلسلہ میں عبداللہ بن مسعود کا قول ہے کہ ایام نحر کا پہلا دن یعنی دسویں ذی الحجہ کی نماز عصر ہے۔ مطلب یہ کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کی عصر کی نماز کے بعد تکبیرات کہ کر ختم کر دے پس عبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ کے نزدیک کل آٹھ نمازوں کے بعد یقینی نویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر سے دسویں کی عصر تک تکبیر تشریق پڑھی جائے گی ۔ یہی مذہب حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کا ہے۔ حضرت علی نے فرمایا ہے کہ تکبیر تشریق ایام تشریق کے آخری دن یعنی تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کی عصر کی نماز پر ختم کی جائے گی ۔ پس حضرت علی کے نزدیک کل ۲۳ نمازوں کے بعد یعنی نویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر سے تیرہویں کی عصر تک تکبیر پڑھی جائے گی اسی قول کو حضرات صاحبین نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ صاحبین نے اکثر کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے حضرت علی کے قول پر اعتماد کیا ہے کیونکہ تکبیر بھی عبادت ہے اور عبادات کے اندر احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ اکثر کو لیا جائے امام ابو حنیفہ کا کمتر اور اقل کو اختیار کرنا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ بآواز بلند تکبیر کہنا بدعت ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَاذْكُرْ رَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًا وَخِيفَةً وَدُونَ الْجَهْرِ اور حدیث ہے راى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اقواماً يرفعون اصواتهم عند الدعا فقال انكم لن تدعوا اصم ولا غائباً یعنی رسول اللہ نے ایک قوم کو دیکھا کہ دعا کے وقت وہ لوگ اپنی آوازوں کو بلند کرتے ہیں تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم لوگ نہ تو بہرے کو پکار رہے ہو اور نہ غائب کو آپ کی مراد یہ ہے کہ اللہ جس کو تم پکار رہے ہو نہ تو وہ بہرہ ہے اور نہ غائب ہے بلکہ سمیع (بہت سننے والا) ہے اور ہر جگہ موجود ہے اس لئے بآواز بلند اس کو پکارنے کی قطعا ضرورت نہیں اس آیت اور روایت سے معلوم ہوا کہ دعا اور ذکر میں اصل اخفاء اور جہر خلاف اصل اور بدعت ہے امام صاحب کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکبیر کی ابتدا ء ایسے دن میں کی جاتی ہے جس کے اندر جج کا ایک رکن یعنی وقوع عرفہ ادا کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس اس کو منقطع کرنا بھی اس یوم نحر میں مناسب ہوگا جس میں حج کا دوسرا رکن یعنی طواف زیارت ادا کیا جاتا ہے تا کہ تکبیر کی ابتداء اور انتہاء دونوں برابر ہو جائیں یہ یاد رہے کہ عمل اور فتوی صاحبین کے قول پر ہے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تکبیر مذکور کلمات اللہ اکبر اللہ اکبرالح کا ایک مرتبہ کہنا ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ تین بار کہے یا پانچ بار یا سات بار کہے۔ یہ کلمات سید نا ابراہیم علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام سے منقول ہیں ان کلمات کا تاریخی پس منظر یہ ہے کہ جب بار خداوندی ابراہیم نے اپنے لخت جگر اسماعیل کو ذبح کرنے کے لئے ہاتھ پاؤں باندھ کر زمین پر پیشانی کے بل لٹا دیا اور چھری
Chapter on the Takbīrs of Tashrīq. (This) chapter is about the Takbīrs of Tashrīq. Statement: The Takbīr of Tashrīq begins after the Fajr prayer of the day of 'Arafah and ends after the 'Asr prayer of the day of Nahr according to Abu Hanifah. And the two said: It ends after the 'Asr prayer of the last day of Tashrīq. The issue is differed among the Companions. So they (the two) adopted the statement of 'Ali, taking the more (prayers) because it is caution in worship. And he (Abu Hanifah) adopted the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, taking the less because raising the voice in takbīr is an innovation. And the takbīr is to say once: Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd. This is what is transmitted from al-Khalil (Ibrahim), peace be upon him. Translation: And to begin the Takbīr of Tashrīq after Fajr of the day of 'Arafah and to end after 'Asr of the day of Nahr (this ruling) is according to Abu Hanifah. And the two companions said that it ends after 'Asr of the last days of Tashrīq. There is a difference among the imams. So the two companions chose the majority and took the statement of 'Ali because this is caution in worship. And Abu Hanifah chose the lesser and took the statement of Ibn Mas'ud because raising the voice in takbīr is an innovation. And the takbīr is to say once: Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd. This is transmitted from Ibrahim, peace be upon him. Explanation: Tashrīq itself is the takbīr. So the meaning would be: in the statement of these takbīrs which are named Tashrīq. In al-'Inayah: Since the Takbīr of Tashrīq is specific to the days of sacrifice, it is mentioned in a separate chapter. In al-Kifayah: The addition of the takbīrs to Tashrīq is correct according to the statement of the two because according to them some takbīrs occur in the days of Tashrīq, i.e., the 11th, 12th, and 13th. But according to Abu Hanifah, the takbīr ends after the 'Asr prayer of the day of Nahr, i.e., the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, while the days of Tashrīq begin from the 11th of Dhul Hijjah. As the author of al-'Inayah wrote with reference to al-Khulasah: The days of Nahr are three, and the days of Tashrīq are also three, such that the 10th of Dhul Hijjah is specifically the day of Nahr, and the 13th is specifically the day of Tashrīq, and the 11th and 12th are for both Nahr and Tashrīq. According to Abu Hanifah, how is the title 'Takbīrs of Tashrīq' correct? One answer is that the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, although it is the day of Nahr and not the day of Tashrīq, is close to the day of Tashrīq, i.e., the 11th. Due to this proximity, the takbīrs are attributed to Tashrīq. As in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Ya'qub said: I led them in the Maghrib prayer on the day of 'Arafah, even though the day of 'Arafah ended with sunset, but because the time of Maghrib is close to the day of 'Arafah, it was called the day of 'Arafah. The second answer is that Tashrīq means the prayer of Eid al-Adha, as in the hadith: 'There is no Jumu'ah nor Tashrīq except in a congregational city' and another hadith: 'No slaughter except after Tashrīq.' In both hadiths, Tashrīq means the Eid prayer. So in that case, by agreement, the attribution is correct. As for the matter that Takbīr al-Tashrīq is obligatory or sunnah, most scholars believe in its obligation, and some believe it is sunnah. The proof of obligation is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And remember Allah during the appointed days' (2:203). And those who say it is sunnah use the continuity and permanence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as proof. Since there is a difference among the Companions regarding the beginning and end of the Takbīrs of Tashrīq, this issue has also been disputed among the imams. The senior Companions, such as 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with them), say that the Takbīr of Tashrīq begins on the day of 'Arafah, i.e., the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. This has been adopted by the Hanafi scholars by agreement. And the junior Companions, such as 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, and Zayd ibn Thabit, said that it begins from the Zuhr of the day of Nahr (the day of slaughter). Regarding the end, the statement of Ibn Mas'ud is that it is the 'Asr of the first day of Nahr, i.e., the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Meaning that after the 'Asr prayer of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the takbīrs are said and then ended. So according to Ibn Mas'ud, the Takbīr of Tashrīq is read after a total of eight prayers, from the Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah to the 'Asr of the 10th. This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifah. 'Ali said that the Takbīr of Tashrīq ends at the 'Asr prayer of the last day of Tashrīq, i.e., the 13th of Dhul Hijjah. So according to 'Ali, the takbīr is read after a total of 23 prayers, from the Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah to the 'Asr of the 13th. This statement has been adopted by the two companions (Sahibayn). The two companions chose the majority and relied on the statement of 'Ali because takbīr is also worship, and caution in worship is to take the majority. Imam Abu Hanifah's choosing the lesser is because raising the voice in takbīr is an innovation. Because Allah Almighty said: 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and in fear and without loudness of speech' (7:205). And the hadith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) saw some people raising their voices during supplication, so he said: 'You are not calling upon a deaf one nor an absent one.' That is, you are not calling upon a deaf one nor an absent one. His meaning is that the One you are calling upon is neither deaf nor absent, but He is All-Hearing and present everywhere, so there is absolutely no need to call upon Him with a loud voice. From this verse and narration, it is understood that in supplication and remembrance, the original principle is concealment, and raising the voice is contrary to the original and is an innovation. Imam's second proof is that the takbīr begins on a day in which one pillar of Hajj, i.e., the standing at 'Arafah, is performed. So its termination should also be appropriate on the day of Nahr, in which the second pillar of Hajj, i.e., the Tawaf of Ziyarah, is performed, so that the beginning and end of the takbīr are symmetrical. It should be remembered that practice and fatwa are upon the statement of the two companions. The author of al-Hidayah says that the takbīr mentioned: the words 'Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar' etc. is said once. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Say three times, or five times, or seven times. These words are transmitted from our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him. The historical background of these words is that when, by the command of Allah, Ibrahim tied the hands and feet of his beloved son Isma'il, laid him on his forehead on the ground, and the knife...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the chapter (Fasl) on Takbīrāt al-Tashrīq from Ashraf al-Hidayah, which is an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah. The passage covers several key aspects: the timing of the takbīr, the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the ruling on obligation vs. sunnah, and the wording of the takbīr. The passage begins by establishing the basic position: according to Abu Hanifah, Takbīr al-Tashrīq begins after Fajr on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm 'Arafah) and ends after 'Asr on the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr). The Sahibayn, however, extend it to after 'Asr on the last day of Tashrīq (13th). The author explains that this stems from a difference among the Companions: Ibn Mas'ud (followed by Abu Hanifah) advocated for fewer prayers (8 total) to minimize what he considered a bid'ah (innovation) of raising the voice, while 'Ali (followed by the Sahibayn) preferred caution by including more prayers (23 total). The commentary then addresses why the term 'Tashrīq' is used even though Abu Hanifah's timing excludes the actual days of Tashrīq. Two answers are given: (1) proximity of the 10th to the 11th, analogous to calling Maghrib on 'Arafah as 'the day of 'Arafah', and (2) interpreting 'Tashrīq' in hadith as referring to the Eid prayer. Next, the passage discusses whether the takbīr is obligatory (wajib) or sunnah. Most Hanafi scholars consider it wajib, citing the Quranic verse 'and remember Allah during the appointed days' (2:203). Those who consider it sunnah rely on the Prophet's continuous practice. Finally, the wording is given as one recitation of 'Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd', transmitted from Ibrahim (AS). Imam al-Shafi'i is noted to allow 3, 5, or 7 repetitions. The passage concludes with the historical context of Ibrahim's sacrifice. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for practice and fatwa is the Sahibayn's view (ending on 13th).

Key Terms
تكبيرات التشريق (takbīrāt al-tashrīq): The specific takbīrs recited after obligatory prayers from Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah until 'Asr of 10th (Abu Hanifa) or 13th (Sahibayn).
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
يَمْ النحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, after which prayer does Takbīr al-Tashrīq end?
A) After 'Asr of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) After 'Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah
C) After Maghrib of the 12th of Dhul Hijjah
D) After Fajr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Takbīr al-Tashrīq is wajib after each obligatory prayer from Fajr of 9th to 'Asr of 13th of Dhul Hijjah (mufta bihi), and its wording is transmitted from Prophet Ibrahim.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Takbir al-Tashriq: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq, identify the conditions of its obligation according to Abu Hanifa, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib only for residents in cities praying in congregation, not for all who pray.

This lesson revisits a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: on whom does Takbir al-Tashriq become obligatory? Imam Abu Hanifa sets specific conditions – residence in a city, congregation – while his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold it incumbent on every person who performs the obligatory prayer, regardless of location or congregation. The difference rests on the interpretation of a hadith and the principle of taba'iyyah (following). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh proofs and appreciate the precision of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, clearly separate what Abu Hanifa states from what the Sahibayn state. Abu Hanifa restricts takbir to residents in cities who pray in congregation; the Sahibayn extend it to all who pray fard.
This is the core of the dispute.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's conditions (quyud)
Break down the restrictions in Abu Hanifa's ruling: 'after obligatory prayers' (excludes nafl, Eid, janazah), 'residents' (excludes travelers), 'in cities' (excludes villages), 'in congregation' (excludes individuals), 'recommended manner' (excludes women-only congregations).
Each condition has a specific exclusion; see the commentary for the full breakdown.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The key dalil for Abu Hanifa is the hadith 'لا جمعة و لا تشريق و لا فطر و لا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع'. The negation (لا) and exception (إلا) establish that takbir is only valid in a major city.
The linguistic definition of tashriq as 'loud takbir' also supports that loud takbir is normally against the Sunnah unless specifically permitted.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning and the Hanafi response
The Sahibayn argue that takbir is a consequence (taba') of the prayer, so it applies to all who pray. Imam Abu Hanifa responds that the hadith overrides this analogy, and loud takbir is only permitted under the stated conditions.
The incident with Abu Yusuf illustrates that the imam's omission does not relieve the follower, because takbir is outside the prayer.
5
Apply the concept of taba'iyyah
Even according to Abu Hanifa, women following a male imam and travelers following a resident imam become obligated by way of following (taba'iyyah). This shows that the obligation can transfer from the imam to the follower.
This is similar to a traveler completing four rak'ahs when following a resident.

Chapter of the Two Eids: Time of Takbir al-Tashriq. It is after the obligatory prayers upon the residents in the cities in the recommended congregations according to Abu Hanifa. It is not upon the congregations of women if there is no man with them, nor upon the congregation of travelers if there is no resident with them. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is upon everyone who prays the obligatory prayer because it follows the obligatory prayer. And for us (Abu Hanifa) is what we narrated before. And al-Tashriq is saying the takbir loudly. Thus it is narrated from al-Khalil ibn Ahmad. And because saying takbir loudly is against the Sunnah, and the Shariah has come with it when these conditions are gathered. Rather, it becomes obligatory upon women when they follow a man, and upon travelers when they follow a resident by way of following. Ya'qub said: I led them in the maghrib prayer on the day of Arafah and I forgot to say the takbir, so Abu Hanifa said the takbir. This indicates that if the imam leaves the takbir, the follower does not leave it. And this is because it is not performed within the sanctity of the prayer, so the imam is not a determinant in it; rather, it is mustahabb. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, reciting takbir after each obligatory prayer is wajib provided that the people are resident in a city and the prayer was performed in congregation in the recommended manner. Imam Abu Hanifa placed the restriction 'after the obligatory prayer' so that if after the obligatory prayer another action occurred, e.g., he left the mosque or engaged in conversation, then this person does not recite the takbir. The restriction 'obligatory prayers' excludes funeral prayer, Eid prayer, and nafl prayers, meaning takbir al-tashriq is not wajib after them. The restriction 'residents' excludes the traveler, as there is no takbir upon him. The restriction 'in the cities' proves the non-obligation of takbir al-tashriq in villages. The restriction 'congregation' excludes the individual. And the restriction 'recommended' excludes the congregation of women alone, i.e., if only women form a congregation, there is no takbir upon them. Yes, if the imam of the women is a man and the imam of the travelers is a resident, then takbir is wajib upon those women and travelers. The two Sahibayn said: Takbir is wajib upon every person who prays the obligatory prayer, whether city dweller or villager, traveler or resident, in congregation or alone, man or woman. This is the opinion of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Their proof is that takbir follows the obligatory prayer, so whoever prays the fard will recite the takbir. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith we mentioned earlier, i.e., 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Tashriq, no Fitr, and no Adha except in a major city.' From this hadith, the condition of the city for takbir al-tashriq is known. Imam al-Khalil ibn Ahmad, the lexicographer, narrated that al-Tashriq is the name for saying takbir loudly. The second proof is that saying takbir loudly is against the Sunnah, i.e., it is innovation, except in the place where the Shariah has permitted it, and the Shariah's permission for loud takbir occurred only in the situation where all these conditions are gathered: city, congregation, recommendation, residence, etc. Yes, if women follow a man or travelers follow a resident, then takbir becomes wajib upon the women and travelers. This obligation is by way of following (taba'iyyah), meaning that since the imam who is followed has takbir wajib upon him, it becomes wajib upon his follower, just as four rak'ahs become obligatory upon a traveler when he follows a resident. The author of al-Hidayah gave a reminder through an incident: If the imam forgets to say the takbir, the follower should not leave it but should say the takbir loudly to alert the imam. In contrast, if the imam forgets to perform sajdah al-sahw, the follower should also leave it. The reason is that sajdah al-sahw is performed during the prayer, so following the imam in doing or not doing it is necessary, while takbir is not performed during the prayer but after finishing it, so the imam's presence in saying it is not wajib but mustahabb. Thus, if the imam does not say the takbir, the follower must say it. The incident is that Imam Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub) narrated: Once I led the people in the Maghrib prayer on the day of Arafah, and by chance I forgot to recite takbir al-tashriq. Then my respected teacher, Imam Abu Hanifah, said the takbir from behind to alert me, so I said the takbir. This incident shows the status of Imam Abu Yusuf, that Imam Abu Hanifah made him the imam and himself followed. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq and presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn). The passage begins by stating Imam Abu Hanifa's position: Takbir al-Tashriq is mustahabb (recommended) and is recited after the obligatory prayers specifically by those who are residents in a city and have prayed in congregation. It is not upon women's congregations without a man, nor upon travelers' congregations without a resident. The Sahibayn, however, hold that it is upon everyone who performs the obligatory prayer, regardless of location or congregation, because it follows the prayer itself. The text then provides the proofs: For Abu Hanifa, the key proof is a hadith that restricts takbir to a major city (مصر جامع), and the linguistic definition from Khalil ibn Ahmad that tashriq means loud takbir, which is otherwise against the Sunnah except where the Shariah allows. For the Sahibayn, the proof is that takbir is a consequence of the prayer, so all who pray must recite it. The passage then clarifies the conditions of Abu Hanifa's position through a detailed analysis of the restrictions (قيود) mentioned: 'after the obligatory prayer' excludes actions after prayer; 'obligatory prayers' excludes funeral, Eid, and nafl prayers; 'residents' excludes travelers; 'in the cities' excludes villages; 'congregation' excludes individuals; 'recommended' excludes women-only congregations. However, if women follow a male imam or travelers follow a resident imam, takbir becomes wajib upon them by way of following (تبعية). The author then narrates an incident involving Imam Abu Yusuf forgetting the takbir, and Imam Abu Hanifa saying it behind him to alert him. This illustrates that the imam's leaving the takbir does not cause the follower to leave it, unlike sajdah al-sahw, because takbir is outside the prayer and the imam's action is not binding. The entire discussion shows the precise legal reasoning (ta'lil) and the practical consequences (thamarah) of the differing views. For fatwa, the relied-upon position is generally that of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
تکبیر تشریق (Takbir al-Tashriq): The takbir recited after obligatory prayers from the morning of the day of Arafah until the afternoon of the last of the days of tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) according to the Hanafi school.
تبعية (Taba'iyyah): Obligation by way of following: when a follower (women or traveler) prays behind an imam upon whom takbir is wajib, the obligation transfers to the follower.
مصر جامع (Misr Jami'): A major city that has a congregational mosque and is a population center large enough for the Jumu'ah to be established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, under which condition is Takbir al-Tashriq wajib?
A) For every person who prays the obligatory prayer, regardless of location.
B) Only for residents in a city who pray in congregation.
C) Only for the imam, not the followers.
D) Only during the afternoon of the Eid day.

Key Takeaway
When studying Takbir al-Tashriq, remember that the Hanafi mufta bihi ties its obligation to three conditions: residence in a city, performance of fard prayer, and congregational prayer in the recommended manner. The Sahibayn's broader view, though known, is not the operative ruling for fatwa.

Conditions for Wajib Takbir al-Tashriq: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explaining the conditions for wajib Takbir and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's conditions for the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq and explain why the Sahibayn disagree.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib only for residents praying in congregation in a city—not for travelers, villagers, or individuals.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a special recitation after fard prayers during the days of Hajj. But on whom is it obligatory? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), hold different views. This lesson breaks down the conditions and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib (not fard) per Abu Hanifa, and need to distinguish the conditions he sets.
Wajib level means obligation with zanni proof.
2
State Abu Hanifa's conditions
List the five restrictions: after fard (not janazah/Eid/nafl), for residents (not travelers), in a city (misr jami'), in congregation (not alone), and in mustahabb manner (not women-only congregation).
Exception: taba'iyyah if follower's imam qualifies.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn hold that Takbir is wajib for anyone who prays any fard prayer, regardless of location, travel, or congregation.
They argue Takbir is subordinate to fard prayer.
4
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof: a hadith restricting Takbir to a congregational city. The Sahibayn's proof: subordination (taba'iyyah) of Takbir to fard.
Note the implicit hanafi response: the hadith's explicit restriction overrides general subordination.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The difference appears for a traveler praying alone in a village—Abu Hanifa says no Takbir, Sahibayn say yes.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

بھی واجب ہوگی جیسے مقیم کی اقتداء کرنے سے مسافر پر چار رکعت لازم ہوتی ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے ایک واقعہ کے ذریعہ تنبیہ فرمائی ہے کہ اگر امام تکبیر کہنا بھول گیا تو مقتدی تکبیر نہ چھوڑے بلکہ بآواز بلند تکبیر کہ کر امام کو بھی باخبر کر دے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر امام نے سجدہ سوہ چھوڑ دیا تو مقتدی بھی اس کو ترک کر دے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ سجدہ سہو درمیان نماز ادا کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے سجدہ سہو کرنے یا نہ کرنے میں امام کا اتباع ضروری ہوگا اور تکبیر در میان نماز ادا نہیں کی جاتی بلکہ نماز سے فارغ ہو نے کے بعد پڑھی جاتی ہے اس لئے تکبیر کہنے میں امام کا موجود ہوانا واجب نہیں بلکہ مستحب ہے پس اگر امام نہ بھی تکبیر کہے تو مقتدی ضرور کہے۔ واقعہ یہ ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف (یعقوب) نے بیان کیا کہ ایک بار میں نے لوگوں کو عرفہ کے دن مغرب کی نماز پڑھائی اتفاق ہے میں تکبیر تشریق کہنا بھول گیا تو استاد مکرم حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے پیچھے سے تکبیر کہہ کر مجھے متنبہ کیا تب میں نے تکبیر کہی۔ اس واقعہ سے امام ابو یوسف کی قدرومنزلت کا پتہ چلتا ہے کہ حضرت امام صاحب نے آپ کو امام بنایا اور خود اقتداء کی واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد غفرلہ۔
Explanation: According to Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifa, it is wajib to recite Takbir after every fard prayer, provided those people are residents within the city and the prayer was performed in congregation in the mustahabb manner. Hadrat Imam Sahib placed the restriction of 'after the fard' so that if another action occurs after the fard prayer, e.g., he left the mosque or engaged in conversation, then this person does not recite Takbir. By the restriction of 'fard prayers', funeral prayer, Eid prayer, and nafl are excluded, meaning Takbir al-Tashriq is not wajib after them. By the restriction of 'residents', a traveler is excluded because Takbir is not upon a traveler. By the restriction of 'in the cities', the non-obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq in villages is established. By the restriction of 'congregation', the individual (munfarid) is excluded. And by the restriction of 'mustahabb (way)', the congregation of only women is excluded, i.e., if only women pray together, then Takbir is not upon them. However, if the imam of the women is a man, and the imam of the travelers is a resident, then Takbir becomes wajib upon those women and travelers. The Sahibayn have stated that Takbir is wajib upon every person who prays a fard prayer, whether he is a city dweller or villager, traveler or resident, in congregation or individually, man or woman. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Their proof is that Takbir is subordinate to the fard prayer, so whoever prays the fard will recite the Takbir. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith which we mentioned before: La jumu'ata wa la tashriqa wa la fitra wa la adha illa fi misrin jami'. From this hadith, it is understood that a city is a condition for Takbir al-Tashriq. It is narrated from the lexicographer Khalil ibn Ahmad that Tashriq is the name for reciting Takbir aloud. The second proof is that reciting the Takbir aloud is against the Sunnah, i.e., innovation, except in the place where the Shari'ah has allowed it. And regarding the loud Takbir, the Shari'ah has allowed it in the case where all these conditions are combined: city, congregation, mustahabb manner, residence, etc. However, if women follow a man, or a traveler follows a resident, then Takbir becomes wajib upon those women and travelers. This obligation is by way of following (taba'iyyah), i.e., since the imam, who is followed, has Takbir wajib upon him, therefore it becomes wajib upon the follower, just as a traveler who follows a resident must pray four rak'ahs. The author of Hidayah has given a reminder through an incident: if the imam forgets to recite Takbir, the follower should not leave the Takbir, but should recite it aloud to alert the imam. Conversely, if the imam leaves out sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness), the follower should also leave it. The reason is that sajdah al-sahw is performed during the prayer, so following the imam in performing or leaving it is necessary. Takbir is not performed during the prayer but is recited after completing the prayer, so it is not wajib to follow the imam in reciting it, rather it is mustahabb. Thus, if the imam does not recite the Takbir, the follower must recite it. The incident is that Imam Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub) narrated: Once I led the people in Maghrib prayer on the day of 'Arafah. By chance I forgot to recite Takbir al-Tashriq. Then my respected teacher, Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifah, alerted me by reciting Takbir from behind, so I then recited the Takbir. This incident shows the status of Imam Abu Yusuf, that Hadrat Imam Sahib made him the imam and himself followed (in prayer). And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq. It first presents Imam Abu Hanifa's position, which is specific and restrictive: Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib only after fard prayers performed in congregation in a mustahabb manner (i.e., with the prescribed method of congregation) within a city (misr). Each condition is explained: only after fard prayers (excluding janazah, Eid, nafl), only for residents (excluding travelers), only in cities (excluding villages), only for congregational prayer (excluding individuals), and only when the congregation is in the mustahabb manner (excluding women's congregation alone). However, if women follow a male imam or a traveler follows a resident imam, then due to taba'iyyah (following), Takbir becomes wajib upon them. Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oppose this, stating that Takbir is wajib upon every person who prays any fard prayer, regardless of city/village, traveler/resident, congregation/individual, man/woman. This is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. The Sahibayn's reasoning is that Takbir is subordinate to the fard prayer itself, so it applies universally. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is a hadith that conditions a congregational city for Jumu'ah, Takbir, etc. He also argues that loud Takbir is generally impermissible except where the Shari'ah has specified, and that specification includes these conditions. The passage ends with a practical lesson from a historical incident with Imam Abu Yusuf, emphasizing that the follower should still recite Takbir if the imam forgets, unlike sajdah al-sahw where following the imam is obligatory. This illustrates the principle that Takbir is recited after the prayer, so leadership in recitation is not required, but it is mustahabb to alert the imam.

Key Terms
تکبیر تشریق (Takbir al-Tashriq): The specific Takbir recited aloud after fard prayers from the Fajr of the Day of 'Arafah to the 'Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation at the level of wajib, which is not as strong as fard. Missing it incurs sin but the act is still valid.
مصر جامع (misr jami'): A city or town where congregational Friday prayer is established, with a central mosque.
تبعیت (taba'iyyah): Following; the principle that a follower (ma'mum) takes the ruling of the imam in matters of obligation related to the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is Takbir al-Tashriq not wajib?
A) After fard prayer in a city with congregation
B) After a fard prayer performed individually in a village
C) After a fard prayer performed by a resident in a city with congregation
D) After a fard prayer performed by a congregation in a city in the mustahabb manner

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib with precise conditions per Imam Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn broaden it to all who pray fard, but the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Salat al-Kusuf: Definition, Consensus, and Method Dispute
Introducing Salat al-Kusuf, its definition, consensus, and the dispute over its method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Kusuf (hukm level and method) and explain why the Hanafi school prefers one ruku' per rak'ah over the Shafi'i position of two ruku'.

Core Idea
Salat al-Kusuf is sunnah muakkadah, performed like nafl: two rak'ahs with one ruku' each — the Hanafi method prioritizes a male narration over Aisha's hadith.

This passage opens the chapter on Salat al-Kusuf (eclipse prayer). The author first establishes the linguistic background, the consensus on its prescription, and the conditions. He then presents the Hanafi method — two rak'ahs like nafl with one ruku' per rak'ah — and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position of two ruku' per rak'ah. The dispute centers on which hadith is stronger: the narration of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As (Hanafi) or the hadith of Aisha (Shafi'i). The Hanafi school gives preference to Ibn Umar's narration based on the principle that men are more reliable witnesses due to their proximity to the event.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared foundation
Both schools agree that Salat al-Kusuf is prescribed (ijma). The dispute is only about the number of ruku' per rak'ah.
Consensus on prescription is unanimous.
2
State each school's method
Hanafi: two rak'ahs, one ruku' each. Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali: two rak'ahs, two ruku' each.
The number of ruku' is the sole point of disagreement.
3
Examine the proofs
Hanafi: narration of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As (not fully quoted). Shafi'i: hadith of Aisha (quoted in detail describing two ruku' per rak'ah).
Both are ahad hadith, so issues of tarjih arise.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The Hanafi school argues that men, being closer to the event, are more reliable. Hence they prefer Ibn Umar's narration over Aisha's.
This is a methodological preference, not a rejection of Aisha's hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi prayer has two ruku' total (shorter); Shafi'i prayer has four ruku' total (longer).
The structure of the prayer changes significantly.

ينصرف ثم قام مخطب الناس فافنى على الله بما هوا هله ثم ان الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله تعالى لا ينخسفان لموت احد ولا لحياته فاذراء يتم ذلك فافزعوا الى الصلوۃ یعنی عائشہ صدیقہ نے فرمایا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حیات میں ایک بار سورج گہن ہو گیا تو آپ مسجد تشریف لے گئے اور کھڑے ہو کر اپنے پیچھے لوگوں کی صف بندی فرمائی پھر تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ کر طویل قرآت فرمائی پھر تکبیر کہہ کر طویل رکوع کیا پھر اپنا سر رکوع سے اٹھایا اور سمع اللہ لمن حمد ربنا ولک الحمد کہا پھر آپ کھڑے ہو گئے اور ایک طویل قرآت کی لیکن یہ قرآت قرآت اولی سے کم تھی پھر تکبیر کہہ کر ایک طویل رکوع کیا لیکن یہ رکوع پہلے سمع
Chapter of the Prayer of Eclipse. Translation: This is regarding the prayer of solar eclipse. Explanation: The relationship between Eid prayer, eclipse prayer, and rain prayer is apparent: all three are performed during the day without adhan and iqamah. Among them, Eid prayer is wajib, eclipse prayer is sunnah according to the majority, and the sunnah status of rain prayer is disputed. Therefore, the order of chapters is appropriate. 'Kusuf' means the sun inclining towards darkness. There is another lexical form 'Khusuf'. Imam Mundhiri said that the hadith of eclipse has been narrated by 19 persons, some with 'kaf' (kusuf) and some with 'kha' (khusuf); thus these two words are synonyms, or kusuf is specific to the sun while khusuf is general for both the sun and the moon. Some said that kusuf is used for solar eclipse and khusuf for lunar eclipse; this is the terminology of the jurists. This is supported by the word of Allah: 'So when the sight is stunned and the moon is eclipsed.' The cause of eclipse prayer is the occurrence of an eclipse, i.e., the sun being eclipsed. Its conditions are the same as those for other prayers. There is consensus of the entire Ummah on the prescription of eclipse prayer; no one has denied it. The Method of Solar Eclipse Prayer: He (the author) said: When the sun is eclipsed, the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs in the manner of nafl prayer, with one bowing in each rak'ah. And al-Shafi'i said: Two bowings (per rak'ah). For him is the hadith narrated by Aisha, and for us is the narration of Ibn Umar. And the state of prayer is more apparent to men due to their closeness, so preference is given to the narration of Ibn Umar. Translation: When the sun is eclipsed, the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs like nafl, with one bowing in each rak'ah. Al-Shafi'i said there are two bowings. His proof is the hadith narrated by Aisha, and our proof is the narration of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As. And the state of prayer is more apparent to men because they are closer, so preference is given to the narration of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As. Explanation: The issue is that when the sun is eclipsed, the imam in the Friday congregational mosque or the Eidgah leads the people in two rak'ahs like nafl, i.e., just as nafl is without adhan and iqamah, so eclipse prayer is performed without adhan and iqamah. There is one bowing in each rak'ah. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad have said that in one rak'ah of eclipse prayer there are two bowings. Their proof is the hadith of Aisha. The wording of the hadith is: She said: The sun was eclipsed during the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah, so he went out to the mosque, stood, and had the people line up. He said the takbir and recited a long recitation, then said takbir and made a long bowing. Then he raised his head saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa laka al-hamd.' Then he stood and recited a long recitation, shorter than the first. Then he said takbir and made a long bowing. Then he raised his head saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa laka al-hamd.' Then he prostrated. He did the same in the second rak'ah, completing four bowings and four prostrations. The sun cleared before he finished. Then he stood and addressed the people, praised Allah as He deserves, and said: 'The sun and the moon are two signs among the signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death or life of anyone. So when you see that, hasten to prayer.' That is, Aisha Siddiqa said: Once during the life of the Messenger of Allah, the sun was eclipsed. He went to the mosque, stood, and arranged the people in rows behind him. He said the takbir (of ihram) and recited a long recitation. Then he said takbir and made a long bowing. Then he raised his head from bowing and said 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa laka al-hamd.' Then he stood and recited a long recitation, but it was shorter than the first recitation. Then he said takbir and made a long bowing, but this bowing was [...]
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new chapter: Bab Salat al-Kusuf (Chapter of Eclipse Prayer). The commentary first explains the appropriateness of placing this chapter after the previous ones, noting that Eid prayer, eclipse prayer, and rain prayer share the feature of being performed during the day without adhan and iqamah, with differences in their legal status. It then provides linguistic details: 'kusuf' and 'khusuf' are synonyms or have specific usages, and the juristic terminology is that kusuf is for solar eclipse and khusuf for lunar eclipse, supported by a Quranic verse. The cause (sabab) of this prayer is the solar eclipse itself, and its conditions (shurut) are the same as for other prayers. The author emphasizes that there is ijma' (consensus) of the entire Ummah on the prescription of this prayer; no one denies it. Then the method is presented: the imam leads two rak'ahs like nafl (i.e., without adhan and iqamah, and with the intention of nafl), with one ruku' in each rak'ah. This is the Hanafi position. The text then introduces the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i (and also Malik and Ahmad according to the later commentary) hold that there are two ruku' in each rak'ah. The Hanafi proof is the narration of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, which the author argues is preferred because men are closer to the event and thus more reliable. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Aisha, which describes the Prophet performing four ruku' (two per rak'ah). The commentary then reproduces Aisha's hadith in detail, showing the method with two ruku' per rak'ah. The passage cuts off mid-hadith, but the point is clear: the Hanafis take the narration of Ibn Umar over that of Aisha due to their criteria of tarjih.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse, the darkening of the sun. Used specifically for the sun in juristic terminology.
صلاة الكسوف (salat al-kusuf): The prescribed prayer performed during a solar eclipse, consisting of two rak'ahs without adhan and iqamah.
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer, an integral (rukn) of each rak'ah. In kusuf prayer, the Hanafi method has one ruku' per rak'ah, while others have two.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the Hanafi method of Salat al-Kusuf (one ruku' per rak'ah)?
A) Hadith of Aisha
B) Hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As
C) Consensus of the Ummah
D) Quranic verse

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Kusuf is sunnah muakkadah, performed like nafl with two rak'ahs and one ruku' each, based on the Hadith of Ibn Umar preferred over Aisha's hadith.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Eclipse Prayer: One Ruku or Two? A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
States Hanafi ruling and refutes Shafi'i view on ruku count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the eclipse prayer, identify the evidence from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and the Shafi'i evidence from 'Aisha, and evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preference) based on the principle of proximity.

Core Idea
In eclipse prayer, the Hanafi school insists on one ruku per rak'ah—proven by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and the logic of clearer observation by men close to the imam.

This passage addresses a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: how many bowings (ruku) are performed in each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer? The Hanafi school, represented by Al-Marghinani, holds firmly to a single ruku per rak'ah, while the Shafi'i school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) holds two. The debate hinges on the interpretation of conflicting hadith reports from 'Aisha and 'Abdullah bin 'Amr bin al-'As, as well as a rational principle about the reliability of eyewitnesses based on their proximity to the imam. By the end of this lesson, you will navigate the evidence and understand why the Hanafi position is considered stronger.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Hanafi ruling
Find the sentence where the author states the Hanafi position: the eclipse prayer is two rak'ahs like nafl, with one ruku in each rak'ah.
The author uses the phrase 'في كل ركعة ركوع واحد' (one ruku in each rak'ah).
2
Identify the opposing view
Note the Shafi'i view (and others) that each rak'ah contains two ruku. The author mentions this immediately after stating the Hanafi ruling.
The phrase 'وقال الشافعي ركوعان' indicates the opposing view.
3
Examine the proofs
The Shafi'i evidence is the hadith of 'Aisha, which describes two bowings per rak'ah. The Hanafi evidence is the hadith of 'Abdullah bin 'Amr bin al-'As (referred to as Ibn 'Umar), which describes one bowing per rak'ah.
Both hadith are quoted in the Urdu explanation.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The passage gives two grounds for preferring the Hanafi evidence: (1) men are closer to the imam, so their observation is more reliable, and (2) Imam Muhammad's ta'wil suggests that the prolonged ruku in 'Aisha's report may have created an illusion of two bowings.
The ta'wil is crucial: it reconciles the reports without rejecting 'Aisha's narration.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis perform one ruku per rak'ah, while Shafi'is perform two. This affects how the prayer is conducted, especially in mixed congregations.
The difference is a real, observable difference in the prayer form.

Chapter of the Eclipse Prayer. (Explanation of why this chapter follows 'Id prayer). The meaning of kusuf is the sun tending towards blackness. Linguistically also khusuf. Imam Mundhiri said 19 narrators narrated hadith of kusuf, some with kaf and some with kha. They are synonymous or kusuf is specific to sun and khusuf general. The scholars' terminology: kusuf for solar eclipse, khusuf for lunar. Supported by Quran 'Wa khasafa al-qamar'. The cause of eclipse prayer is solar eclipse. Its conditions are the same as other prayers. There is consensus of the entire ummah on its legitimacy. The method: He (the author) said: When the sun is eclipsed, the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs like the nafl prayer, with one bowing in each rak'ah. Al-Shafi'i said: two bowings due to the narration of 'Aisha. Our evidence is the narration of Ibn 'Umar, and the condition of the prayer is clearer to men due to their proximity, so the preference is for the narration (of Ibn 'Umar). Translation... (Urdu explanation). Then the Shafi'i evidence from 'Aisha's hadith (Arabic text). Then our evidence from 'Abdullah bin 'Amr bin al-'As's hadith (Arabic text). Then (Urdu) analysis showing that Ibn 'Umar's hadith is preferred because men are closer. Imam Muhammad's ta'wil: the long bowing led to a misunderstanding that there were two bowings. 'Aisha was far back among women, so her report is less reliable.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the number of bowings (ruku) per rak'ah in the eclipse prayer. The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: two rak'ahs like nafl, with one ruku each. Then he presents the Shafi'i view (two ruku per rak'ah) and their evidence from the hadith of 'Aisha. The Hanafi counter-evidence is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (actually 'Abdullah bin 'Amr bin al-'As). The preference for Ibn 'Umar's narration is based on the principle that men, being closer to the imam, have clearer observation. The author then provides a detailed Urdu commentary explaining both hadiths and concludes with Imam Muhammad's ta'wil to reconcile the reports, which casts doubt on 'Aisha's narration due to her distance from the imam.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the event that triggers the eclipse prayer.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse; according to Hanafi terminology, used for lunar eclipse, though general usage may apply to both.
ركوع (ruku): Bowing posture in prayer. In this context, the number of bowings per rak'ah.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer. The eclipse prayer is compared to nafl in form (no adhan/iqamah, one ruku per rak'ah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, how many ruku are performed in each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer?
A) Two ruku
B) One ruku
C) Three ruku
D) Four ruku

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the eclipse prayer has one ruku per rak'ah, supported by the hadith of 'Abdullah bin 'Amr bin al-'As and the principle that men's observation is more reliable due to proximity to the imam.

Ruling on Recitation in the Eclipse Prayer: Length and Audibility
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the length and audibility of recitation in the solar eclipse prayer and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer recitation is recommended to be long but may be shortened; the imam should recite quietly per the relied Hanafi view.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two aspects of recitation in the solar eclipse prayer: its length and audibility. While the length is a matter of preference (mustahabb), the audibility involves a well-known disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students, the Sahibayn. Understanding this ikhtilaf is key to applying the correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Separate the two rulings
Note that the passage discusses two distinct issues: the length of recitation (tatwil) and whether it should be loud (jahr) or quiet (ikhfa).
The length ruling is straightforward; the audibility is contested.
2
Analyse the length ruling
The text states that lengthening is an expression of 'the preferred' (al-afdal), and the imam may shorten if he wishes, as the sunnah is to fill the time with prayer and supplication.
This is a recommendation (sunnah), not an obligation.
3
Examine the audibility dispute
Identify the three positions: Abu Hanifa (quiet), Sahibayn (loud), and a narration from Muhammad agreeing with Abu Hanifa. Note the proof for each: Sahibayn rely on the hadith of 'Aisha; Abu Hanifa relies on hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah.
Also note the additional reasoning: the eclipse prayer is a daytime prayer, which are normally recited quietly.
4
Apply tarjih
The author gives preference to Abu Hanifa's view because it is a daytime prayer ('and because it is a daytime prayer and it is speechless'). This is the mufta bihi position.
The tarjih is based on the qiyas to other daytime prayers like Zuhr and 'Asr.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa: quiet recitation. If one follows the Sahibayn, the prayer would still be valid but contrary to the preferred view.
This thamarah al-khilaf is important for muftis and imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويطول القراءة فيهما و يخفى عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يجهر وعن محمد مثل قول ابي حنيفة اما التطويل في القراءة فبيان الافضل ويخفف ان شاء لان المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلوة والدعاء فاذا اخفف احدهما طول الاخر واما الاخفاء والجهر فلهما رواية عائشة انه جهر فيها ولابي حنيفة رواية ابن عباس و سمرة ابن جندب و الترجيح قدمر من قبل كيف و انها صلوة النهار وهي عجماء
And he lengthens the recitation in both (rak'ahs) and he recites quietly according to Abu Hanifa, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he recites aloud. And from Muhammad (a narration) like the saying of Abu Hanifa. As for lengthening the recitation, it is an expression of the preferred (action); he may shorten if he wishes, because the sunnah is to fill the time with prayer and supplication, so if he shortens one (the recitation) he lengthens the other (the supplication). As for quiet and loud recitation, they (Sahibayn) have the narration of 'Aisha that he (the Prophet) recited aloud in it, and Abu Hanifa has the narration of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah ibn Jundub. And the preference has already been mentioned (previously) and because it is a daytime prayer and it is speechless (i.e., the recitation is not loud).
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage covers two aspects of recitation in the eclipse prayer: its length and whether it should be loud or quiet. The Hanafi school recommends lengthy recitation, but it is not obligatory; the imam may shorten it if he wishes and compensate with longer supplications. On audibility, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that recitation should be quiet (ikhfa), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that it should be loud (jahr). There is also a narration from Muhammad agreeing with Abu Hanifa. The text gives evidence: the Sahibayn rely on the hadith of 'Aisha that the Prophet recited aloud; Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah. The author then gives a reason for preferring Abu Hanifa's view: because it is a daytime prayer and daytime prayers are usually recited quietly (silent recitation). This is a characteristic of daytime prayers in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation, i.e., making the recitation audible to the congregation.
إخفاء (ikhfa): Quiet recitation, i.e., reciting silently without making the congregation hear.
تطويل (tatwil): Lengthening the recitation. Here, it is recommended to make the recitation long, but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Loud recitation (jahr)
B) Quiet recitation (ikhfa)
C) No recitation at all
D) Recitation only in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In the solar eclipse prayer, recitation may be shortened if needed, and the imam should recite quietly according to the relied Hanafi view.

Prolonging Recitation in Eclipse Prayer
Ruling on prolonging recitation in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prolonging recitation in eclipse prayer and explain the principle of occupying the time (isti'ab al-waqt).

Core Idea
Prolonging recitation is sunna, but shortening is allowed if compensated by longer supplication.

In eclipse prayer, the Prophet ﷺ would recite long surahs, but the primary sunna is to fill the eclipse duration with worship. This lesson clarifies the ruling on recitation length and the flexibility permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is recitation in eclipse prayer. The ruling: it is sunna to prolong recitation, but not obligatory.
The text says 'yutawwil' (prolongs) and 'yukhaffif in sha'a' (shortens if he wishes).
2
Understand the underlying principle
The sunna is to occupy the entire eclipse time (isti'ab al-waqt) with prayer and supplication until the eclipse clears.
This is based on the hadith: 'When you see them, supplicate to Allah and pray until it clears.'
3
Note the flexibility
If the imam shortens recitation, he should lengthen the supplication (du'a) to fill the time. Prolonging recitation is one means, not the only means.
4
Distinguish from wajib
Prolonging recitation is mustahabb, not wajib. The prayer is valid even with short recitation.
The consequence: no compensation (sajdah sahw) required if shortened.

Source Text

باب صلوة الكسوف
ويطول القراءة فيهما ويخفى عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجهر وعن محمد مثل قول أبي حنيفة. أما التطويل في القراءة فبيان الأفضل ويخفف إن شاء لأن المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء فإذا خفف أحدهما طول الآخر. وأما الإخفاء والجهر فلهما رواية عائشة أنه جهر فيها ولأبي حنيفة رواية ابن عباس وسمرة بن جندب والترجيح قد مر من قبل كيف وإنها صلاة النهار وهي عجماء.

تشريح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کسوف کی دونوں رکعتوں میں طویل قرآت کرنے چنانچہ بعض احادیث میں اول رکعت بقد رسورۃ بقرہ اور دوسری رکعت بقدر آل عمران ہاں اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ قرآت جہری کرے یا سری چنانچہ حضرت امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ نماز کسوف میں سری قرآت کرے اس کے قائل امام مالک امام شافعی اور جمہور فقہاء ہیں۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جہری کرے یہی قول امام احمد کا ہے اسن کو امام طحاوی نے اختیار کیا ہے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام محمد سے ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ کے مانند ہے اس صورت میں طرفین اختفاء اور سری قرآت کے قائل ہوں گے اور ابو یوسف جر ہی قرآت کے قائل ہوں گے حاصل یہ کہ یہاں دو باتیں ہیں قرآت میں طول دینا اور قرأت میں جہر پا اخفاء کرنا سوقرات کو طویل دینا تو افضل ہے کیونکہ یہ ثابت ہی کہ رکعت اولی میں رسول اللہ کا قیام بقدر بقرہ اور رکت ثانیہ میں بقدر آل عمران ہوتا تھا پس قرآت کو طول دینے میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی متابعت ہے اور جی چاہے تو قرآت میں تخفیف کرئے بنی قرآت مختصر کرے کیونکہ مسنون تو یہ ہے کہ گہن کا وقت نماز اور دعا میں گھر جائے لہذا اگر ایک کو تخفیف کرے تو دوسرے کو طویل دیدئے علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا ہے و الحق ان السنة التطويل المندوب مجرد استيعاب الوقت یعنی حق یہ ہے کہ قرآت کو طول دینا مسنون ہے اور وقت کسوف کا استیعاب کرنا مستحب ہے جیسا کہ حدیث مغیرہ بن شعبہ میں ہے فاذا رايتموها فادعوا الله وصلو احتى تنجلی ( صحیحین) پھر جب تم ان چیزوں کو دیکھو کسوف وغیرہ کو) تو اللہ تعالیٰ سے دعا کرو اور نماز پڑھا یہاں تک کہ وہ روشن ہو جائے دیکھئے سورج روشن ہونے تک نماز کو طول دینے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور اسی وقت وہ جب کہ قرآت کو طویل دیا جائے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت کو طول دینا مسنون ہے۔۔

قرآت کے جہری ہونے پر صاحبین یا فقط امام ابوید من کی دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے قالت جهر النبي صلى الله علیه وسلم لى صلوة الحسوف بقراته ( صحيحين ) عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے فرمایا کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز کسوف میں بالجبر قرآت کی نے امام ابو حنیفہ یا طرفین کی دلیل ابن عباس اور سمرہ بن جندب کی حدیث ہے۔ ابن عباس کی حدیث کے الفاظ تو یہ ہیں عن ابن عباس صليت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فلم اسمع منه حرفا من القرأۃ یعنی ابن عباس نے کہا کہ میں نے نبی علیہ السلام کے ساتھ کسوف کی نماز پڑھی ہے لیکن میں نے آپ کی قرآت سے کوئی حرف نہیں سنا اسی کے ہم معنی سمرہ بن جندب کی حدیث ہے صلی بنافي كسوف الشمس لا نسمع به صوتا یعنی ہم کو کسوف شمس کی حالت میں نماز پڑھائی اور ہم نے آپ کی آواز نہیں سنی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے قرآت کے جہری اور سری ہونے میں تعارض حدیث کو اس طرح دور کیا ہے کہ ابن عباس اور سمرہ بن جندب کی روایت کو حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کی روایت پر ترجیح دی ہے اور وجہ ترجیح یہ ہے کہ نماز کے اندر مرد چونکہ امام سے قریب ہوتے ہیں اس لئے عورتوں کی بہ نسبت ان کا حال زیادہ واضح ہوگا اور امام کی کیفیت نماز اور قرآت کے بالجبر اور بالا حفلہ ہونے میں مردوں کا ہی قول
Chapter of Eclipse Prayer
He prolongs recitation in both rak'ahs and recites silently according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He recites aloud. And from Muhammad, similar to the saying of Abu Hanifa. As for prolonging recitation, it is a statement of preference; he may shorten if he wishes, because the sunna is to occupy the time with prayer and supplication. So if he shortens one, he prolongs the other. As for silent and loud recitation, they have the hadith of Aisha that he recited aloud in it, and Abu Hanifa has the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub. The preference has already been mentioned before, because it is a daytime prayer and it is silent.

Explanation of the issue: In eclipse prayer, recitation is prolonged in both rak'ahs. In some hadith, the first rak'ah is like Surah al-Baqarah and the second like Surah Al-Imran. There is disagreement whether recitation is aloud or silent. Imam Abu Hanifa says silent recitation in eclipse prayer, and this is the view of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and the majority of jurists. The Sahibayn said aloud, and this is the view of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Tahawi chose this. The author of Hidayah says that from Imam Muhammad there is a narration like Imam Abu Hanifa's; in that case the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) are for silent recitation, and Abu Yusuf is for loud recitation. The conclusion is that there are two matters: prolonging recitation and loud/silent recitation. Prolonging recitation is superior because it is established that the Prophet's standing in the first rak'ah was like Surah al-Baqarah and in the second like Surah Al-Imran. So prolonging recitation follows the Prophet. If one wishes, he may shorten recitation, because the sunna is to occupy the time of eclipse with prayer and supplication. If he shortens one, he prolongs the other. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said: The truth is that the sunna is prolonging recitation, and occupying the time is mustahabb, as in the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'When you see them, supplicate to Allah and pray until it clears.' (Sahihayn) So prayer is commanded until the sun becomes bright, which necessitates prolonging recitation. Thus it is known that prolonging recitation is sunna.

As for loud recitation, the evidence of the Sahibayn or only Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet recited aloud in the eclipse prayer.' (Sahihayn) The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa or the two sides is the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub. The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'I prayed with the Prophet the eclipse prayer and I did not hear from him any letter of recitation.' The hadith of Samura: 'He led us in the eclipse prayer and we did not hear his voice.' The author of Hidayah resolved the conflict between the hadith by giving preference to the narration of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub over Aisha's narration. The reason for preference is that men are closer to the imam in prayer, so their observation is clearer than that of women. And the quality of the imam's prayer and recitation being aloud or silent, the statement of men is [given precedence].
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses two rulings for Salat al-Kusuf (eclipse prayer): (1) whether recitation should be prolonged or shortened, and (2) whether it should be recited aloud (jahr) or silently (ikhfa). The text first states the madhhab positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that recitation is silent (yukhfi), while Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad initially held that it is aloud (yajhar). However, a narration from Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, making the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf alone. As for prolonging recitation, the text clarifies it is a sunna and preferred (afdal), but if one shortens it, one may compensate by lengthening the supplication (du'a) because the objective is to fill the time with worship until the eclipse clears. The commentator then elaborates on the evidence: the Sahibayn rely on Aisha's hadith that the Prophet recited aloud; Abu Hanifa relies on Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub who state they did not hear the Prophet's recitation. The author of al-Hidayah prefers the latter due to the rule that men in the front rows have better perception than women in the back. Hence the Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is silent recitation in eclipse prayer, as it is a daytime prayer which is normally silent.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the sun's light being obscured.
استيعاب الوقت (isti'ab al-waqt): Occupying the entire duration of the eclipse with prayer and supplication until it clears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended) but flexible
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
Prolonging recitation in eclipse prayer is sunna, but the primary objective is to occupy the eclipse time with worship; flexibility is allowed.

Loud vs Silent Recitation in Eclipse Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr vs ikhfa in eclipse prayer with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on recitation volume in eclipse prayer and state the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position is silent recitation, preferring the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura over Aisha's hadith.

A key dispute among the early Hanafi masters is whether the imam recites aloud or silently in eclipse prayer. This lesson breaks down the positions, evidence, and the tarjih given in al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi core positions
Abu Hanifa: silent. Abu Yusuf: aloud. Muhammad: two narrations, one silent, one aloud. The mufta bihi is silent.
Also note that Imam Malik, Shafi'i agree with silent; Ahmad and Tahawi agree with loud.
2
Identify the evidence for each side
The loud side: hadith of Aisha that the Prophet recited aloud. The silent side: hadith of Ibn Abbas (did not hear any letter) and Samura (did not hear voice).
All ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Understand the tarjih (preference) mechanism
Al-Hidayah gives preference to the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura over Aisha's because men are closer to the imam and their observation is more reliable than women's.
This is a rule of witness testimony: proximity and gender are considered.
4
Apply the broader principle
Eclipse prayer is a daytime prayer; daytime prayers are normally silent (jahr only in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha). This analogy supports silent recitation.
The text says 'since it is a daytime prayer and it is silent'.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafi imams should recite silently in eclipse prayer. Those following the loud position would recite aloud.
The difference is purely in volume; all other elements are the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الكسوف
ويطول القراءة فيهما ويخفى عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجهر وعن محمد مثل قول أبي حنيفة. أما التطويل في القراءة فبيان الأفضل ويخفف إن شاء لأن المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء فإذا خفف أحدهما طول الآخر. وأما الإخفاء والجهر فلهما رواية عائشة أنه جهر فيها ولأبي حنيفة رواية ابن عباس وسمرة بن جندب والترجيح قد مر من قبل كيف وإنها صلاة النهار وهي عجماء.

تشريح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کسوف کی دونوں رکعتوں میں طویل قرآت کرنے چنانچہ بعض احادیث میں اول رکعت بقد رسورۃ بقرہ اور دوسری رکعت بقدر آل عمران ہاں اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ قرآت جہری کرے یا سری چنانچہ حضرت امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ نماز کسوف میں سری قرآت کرے اس کے قائل امام مالک امام شافعی اور جمہور فقہاء ہیں۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جہری کرے یہی قول امام احمد کا ہے اسن کو امام طحاوی نے اختیار کیا ہے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام محمد سے ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ کے مانند ہے اس صورت میں طرفین اختفاء اور سری قرآت کے قائل ہوں گے اور ابو یوسف جر ہی قرآت کے قائل ہوں گے حاصل یہ کہ یہاں دو باتیں ہیں قرآت میں طول دینا اور قرأت میں جہر پا اخفاء کرنا سوقرات کو طویل دینا تو افضل ہے کیونکہ یہ ثابت ہی کہ رکعت اولی میں رسول اللہ کا قیام بقدر بقرہ اور رکت ثانیہ میں بقدر آل عمران ہوتا تھا پس قرآت کو طول دینے میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی متابعت ہے اور جی چاہے تو قرآت میں تخفیف کرئے بنی قرآت مختصر کرے کیونکہ مسنون تو یہ ہے کہ گہن کا وقت نماز اور دعا میں گھر جائے لہذا اگر ایک کو تخفیف کرے تو دوسرے کو طویل دیدئے علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا ہے و الحق ان السنة التطويل المندوب مجرد استيعاب الوقت یعنی حق یہ ہے کہ قرآت کو طول دینا مسنون ہے اور وقت کسوف کا استیعاب کرنا مستحب ہے جیسا کہ حدیث مغیرہ بن شعبہ میں ہے فاذا رايتموها فادعوا الله وصلو احتى تنجلی ( صحیحین) پھر جب تم ان چیزوں کو دیکھو کسوف وغیرہ کو) تو اللہ تعالیٰ سے دعا کرو اور نماز پڑھا یہاں تک کہ وہ روشن ہو جائے دیکھئے سورج روشن ہونے تک نماز کو طول دینے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور اسی وقت وہ جب کہ قرآت کو طویل دیا جائے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت کو طول دینا مسنون ہے۔۔

قرآت کے جہری ہونے پر صاحبین یا فقط امام ابوید من کی دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے قالت جهر النبي صلى الله علیه وسلم لى صلوة الحسوف بقراته ( صحيحين ) عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے فرمایا کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز کسوف میں بالجبر قرآت کی نے امام ابو حنیفہ یا طرفین کی دلیل ابن عباس اور سمرہ بن جندب کی حدیث ہے۔ ابن عباس کی حدیث کے الفاظ تو یہ ہیں عن ابن عباس صليت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فلم اسمع منه حرفا من القرأۃ یعنی ابن عباس نے کہا کہ میں نے نبی علیہ السلام کے ساتھ کسوف کی نماز پڑھی ہے لیکن میں نے آپ کی قرآت سے کوئی حرف نہیں سنا اسی کے ہم معنی سمرہ بن جندب کی حدیث ہے صلی بنافي كسوف الشمس لا نسمع به صوتا یعنی ہم کو کسوف شمس کی حالت میں نماز پڑھائی اور ہم نے آپ کی آواز نہیں سنی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے قرآت کے جہری اور سری ہونے میں تعارض حدیث کو اس طرح دور کیا ہے کہ ابن عباس اور سمرہ بن جندب کی روایت کو حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کی روایت پر ترجیح دی ہے اور وجہ ترجیح یہ ہے کہ نماز کے اندر مرد چونکہ امام سے قریب ہوتے ہیں اس لئے عورتوں کی بہ نسبت ان کا حال زیادہ واضح ہوگا اور امام کی کیفیت نماز اور قرآت کے بالجبر اور بالا حفلہ ہونے میں مردوں کا ہی قول
Chapter of Eclipse Prayer
He prolongs recitation in both rak'ahs and recites silently according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He recites aloud. And from Muhammad, similar to the saying of Abu Hanifa. As for prolonging recitation, it is a statement of preference; he may shorten if he wishes, because the sunna is to occupy the time with prayer and supplication. So if he shortens one, he prolongs the other. As for silent and loud recitation, they have the hadith of Aisha that he recited aloud in it, and Abu Hanifa has the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub. The preference has already been mentioned before, because it is a daytime prayer and it is silent.

Explanation of the issue: In eclipse prayer, recitation is prolonged in both rak'ahs. In some hadith, the first rak'ah is like Surah al-Baqarah and the second like Surah Al-Imran. There is disagreement whether recitation is aloud or silent. Imam Abu Hanifa says silent recitation in eclipse prayer, and this is the view of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and the majority of jurists. The Sahibayn said aloud, and this is the view of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Tahawi chose this. The author of Hidayah says that from Imam Muhammad there is a narration like Imam Abu Hanifa's; in that case the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) are for silent recitation, and Abu Yusuf is for loud recitation. The conclusion is that there are two matters: prolonging recitation and loud/silent recitation. Prolonging recitation is superior because it is established that the Prophet's standing in the first rak'ah was like Surah al-Baqarah and in the second like Surah Al-Imran. So prolonging recitation follows the Prophet. If one wishes, he may shorten recitation, because the sunna is to occupy the time of eclipse with prayer and supplication. If he shortens one, he prolongs the other. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said: The truth is that the sunna is prolonging recitation, and occupying the time is mustahabb, as in the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'When you see them, supplicate to Allah and pray until it clears.' (Sahihayn) So prayer is commanded until the sun becomes bright, which necessitates prolonging recitation. Thus it is known that prolonging recitation is sunna.

As for loud recitation, the evidence of the Sahibayn or only Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet recited aloud in the eclipse prayer.' (Sahihayn) The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa or the two sides is the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub. The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'I prayed with the Prophet the eclipse prayer and I did not hear from him any letter of recitation.' The hadith of Samura: 'He led us in the eclipse prayer and we did not hear his voice.' The author of Hidayah resolved the conflict between the hadith by giving preference to the narration of Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub over Aisha's narration. The reason for preference is that men are closer to the imam in prayer, so their observation is clearer than that of women. And the quality of the imam's prayer and recitation being aloud or silent, the statement of men is [given precedence].
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses two rulings for Salat al-Kusuf (eclipse prayer): (1) whether recitation should be prolonged or shortened, and (2) whether it should be recited aloud (jahr) or silently (ikhfa). The text first states the madhhab positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that recitation is silent (yukhfi), while Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad initially held that it is aloud (yajhar). However, a narration from Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, making the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf alone. As for prolonging recitation, the text clarifies it is a sunna and preferred (afdal), but if one shortens it, one may compensate by lengthening the supplication (du'a) because the objective is to fill the time with worship until the eclipse clears. The commentator then elaborates on the evidence: the Sahibayn rely on Aisha's hadith that the Prophet recited aloud; Abu Hanifa relies on Ibn Abbas and Samura ibn Jundub who state they did not hear the Prophet's recitation. The author of al-Hidayah prefers the latter due to the rule that men in the front rows have better perception than women in the back. Hence the Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is silent recitation in eclipse prayer, as it is a daytime prayer which is normally silent.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation, raising the voice so others can hear.
إخفاء (ikhfa): Silent recitation, moving the lips without audible sound.
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the sun's light being obscured.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), how should the imam recite in eclipse prayer?
A) Loudly (jahr)
B) Silently (ikhfa)
C) Loudly only in the first rak'ah
D) It is optional

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab's relied-upon position is silent recitation in eclipse prayer, preferring the witness of male companions and analogy to daytime prayers.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Recitation in Eclipse Prayer: Jahar vs Ikhfa'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr vs ikhfa' in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in Salat al-Kusuf and explain why the preferred view is ikhfa' (silent recitation).

Core Idea
In eclipse prayer, recitation is silent because it is a daytime prayer, and the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas is preferred over that of 'A'ishah.

The eclipse prayer (Salat al-Kusuf) is a sunnah prayer performed during a solar eclipse. While there is consensus on lengthening the recitation, a key intra-Hanafi dispute exists on whether the recitation should be audible (jahr) or silent (ikhfa'). This lesson unpacks the evidence and the reasoning behind the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The central question: In Salat al-Kusuf, should the imam recite aloud or silently?
Also note the subsidiary issue of whether lengthening is sunnah or mustahabb.
2
State the mufta bihi position
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, recitation is silent (ikhfa'). Lengthening the recitation is sunnah.
Mufta bihi: ikhfa'.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (in one narration) hold ikhfa'; Abu Yusuf holds jahr. The majority of other schools also prefer jahr.
Thus the internal dispute is essentially between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze the proofs
For ikhfa': hadith of Ibn 'Abbas ('I did not hear a letter') and Samurah ('we did not hear his voice') plus the principle 'salat al-nahar 'ajma''. For jahr: hadith of 'A'ishah ('he recited aloud').
All proofs are ahad hadith, so epistemological weight is zanni.
5
Understand the tarjih
Al-Marghinani (Hidayah) preferred Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah because men are closer to the imam and thus more reliable witnesses. Additionally, eclipse prayer is a daytime prayer, and daytime prayers are silent by established principle.
The tarjih also relies on the general principle that daytime prayers are silent.
