نمازوں کے بارے میں رحمت دو عالم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے صلواۃ النھار عجماء یعنی دن کی نماز گونگی ہے مراد یہ ہے کہ دن کی نمازوں میں قرآت آہستہ کی جاتی ہے نہ کہ بآواز بلند۔
Chapter of Eclipse Prayer: Translation: And he should prolong the recitation in both rak'ahs, and according to Abu Hanifa he should recite silently, while the Two Companions said he should recite aloud. Imam Muhammad has a narration similar to Abu Hanifa's statement. In any case, lengthening the recitation is a matter of virtue, and if he wishes he may shorten the recitation because the sunnah is to occupy the time of eclipse with prayer and supplication. So when one of these is lightened, the other is lengthened. As for silence and aloudness, the proof of the Two Companions is the narration of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah ibn Jundub. The preference has been given earlier because silence is not established, whereas the eclipse prayer is a daytime prayer, and daytime prayer is silent without audible recitation. Explanation: The issue is that in both rak'ahs of the eclipse prayer, lengthy recitation is performed. Indeed, in some hadith, the first rak'ah is up to the length of Surah al-Baqarah and the second rak'ah up to the length of Surah Al 'Imran. However, there is a difference of opinion whether the recitation should be aloud or silent. Accordingly, Imam Abu Hanifa said that in the eclipse prayer, silent recitation should be done. Imam Malik, Imam al-Shafi'i, and the majority of jurists are of this view. The Two Companions said that it should be aloud; this is also the statement of Imam Ahmad, and Imam al-Tahawi chose it. The author of al-Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad has a narration like Imam Abu Hanifa's, so in that case both parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) would be proponents of silent recitation, and only Abu Yusuf would be proponent of jahr. The conclusion is that here there are two matters: lengthening the recitation and doing it aloud or silently. Lengthening the recitation is superior because it is established that in the first rak'ah the Prophet's standing was up to the length of al-Baqarah and in the second up to Al 'Imran. So in lengthening the recitation, there is following of the Prophet. And if he wishes, he may shorten the recitation because the sunnah is that the time of eclipse be spent in prayer and supplication; hence if one is shortened, the other is lengthened. 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam said: 'The truth is that lengthening is sunnah, and occupying the time is mustahabb, as in the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'When you see these things, then supplicate to Allah and pray until it becomes clear' (Sahihayn). So it is commanded to prolong the prayer until the sun becomes clear, and this is when the recitation is lengthened. Thus it is known that lengthening the recitation is sunnah. The proof for the Two Companions (or only Imam Abu Yusuf) for jahr is the hadith of 'A'ishah: 'The Prophet recited aloud in the eclipse prayer' (Sahihayn). And the proof for Imam Abu Hanifa (or both parties) is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah ibn Jundub. The wording of Ibn 'Abbas's hadith: 'I prayed with the Prophet the eclipse prayer and I did not hear from him a single letter of recitation.' Similar in meaning is the hadith of Samurah: 'He led us in prayer during a solar eclipse and we did not hear his voice.' The author of al-Hidayah resolved the apparent contradiction between these hadith by giving preference to the narration of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah over the narration of 'A'ishah. The reason for preference is that men are closer to the imam in prayer, so their condition is more clear compared to women, and men's statement regarding the quality of the imam's prayer and recitation being aloud or silent will be authoritative. Then on page 331: The author of al-Hidayah, to strengthen Imam Abu Hanifa's school, says emphatically: How can silence in recitation in the eclipse prayer not be established, whereas the eclipse prayer is a daytime prayer? And regarding daytime prayers, the mercy to the worlds said: 'Daytime prayers are silent,' meaning that in daytime prayers, recitation is done softly, not aloud.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of recitation in Salat al-Kusuf (solar eclipse prayer). The author begins by presenting the basic ruling: the recitation should be lengthened, and then introduces the ikhtilaf regarding jahr (audible) versus ikhfa' (silent) recitation. Abu Hanifa holds that the recitation should be silent, while the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and in one narration Imam Muhammad) hold that it should be aloud. Imam Muhammad, however, has another narration agreeing with Abu Hanifa, so the only persistent opponent within the Hanafi school is Abu Yusuf. The author then discusses lengthening the recitation: it is sunnah to prolong the recitation up to the length of Surah al-Baqarah in the first rak'ah and Al 'Imran in the second, based on the practice of the Prophet. However, if one wishes, one may shorten it, because the main objective is to occupy the time of eclipse with prayer and supplication. The text then presents the proofs: for jahr, the hadith of 'A'ishah stating that the Prophet recited aloud; for ikhfa', the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah stating that they did not hear the Prophet's recitation. The author of al-Hidayah resolves the apparent contradiction by giving preference to the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and Samurah, arguing that men are closer to the imam in congregation, so their testimony is more reliable regarding whether the recitation was audible or not. Additionally, the passage invokes the general principle that daytime prayers are silent (salat al-nahar 'ajma'), citing the hadith: 'Daytime prayers are deaf-mute' (meaning silent). Therefore, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that recitation in Salat al-Kusuf should be silent (ikhfa'), and lengthening it is a sunnah.

Key Terms
اخفاء (ikhfā'): Silent recitation, where the voice is not audible to others.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation, where the voice is heard by those nearby.
كسوف (kusūf): Solar eclipse, a celestial event that triggers the sunnah prayer of the eclipse.
صلاة النهار عجماء (ṣalāt al-nahār 'ajmā'): Daytime prayers are 'deaf-mute' meaning they are performed with silent recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how should the recitation be in Salat al-Kusuf?
A) It should be recited aloud (jahr)
B) It should be recited silently (ikhfa')
C) It should be recited in a whisper
D) It should be recited only in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In eclipse prayer, the Hanafi mufta bihi is silent recitation (ikhfa') due to the principle of daytime prayers being silent and the preferred hadith of Ibn 'Abbas.

Who Leads the Eclipse Prayer
Specifies the leadership of eclipse prayer with fitna avoidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who leads the eclipse prayer and explain the rationale of avoiding fitna.

Core Idea
The Jumu'ah imam leads the eclipse prayer; if absent, pray individually to prevent fitna.

This lesson addresses the leadership of the solar eclipse prayer in the Hanafi school. The matn gives a clear rule: the same imam who leads the Friday prayer should lead the eclipse prayer. If that imam is unavailable, the congregation must pray individually. The commentary explains that this restriction prevents social disorder, reflecting the Hanafi priority of communal harmony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is sunnah muakkadah. The matn states that it should be led by the imam who leads Jumu'ah.
This is a leadership rule, not about validity of the prayer itself.
2
State the two scenarios
Scenario 1: The Jumu'ah imam is present → he leads the congregation. Scenario 2: He is absent → each person prays individually (furada).
3
Explain the rationale
Avoiding fitna (disorder) is the reason. Congregation without the official imam could lead to disputes over leadership.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of prioritizing social harmony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى بهم الإمام الذى يصلى بهم الجمعة و ان لم يحضر صلى الناس فرادى تحرزا عن الفتنة تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کسوف میں اس کو امام مقرر کیا جائی جولوگوں کو جمعہ اور عیدین کی نماز پڑھاتا ہے اور اگر امام جمعہ موجود نہ ہوتو لوگ بینہ اتنہا نماز ادا کریں کیونکہ اس میں فتنہ کا امکان نہیں ہے اور جماعت کی صورت میں فتنہ کا غالب امکان ہے بایں طور کہ ہر شخص امام بنے کی کوشش کرے گا یا اپنی حسب منشاء امام کو آگے بڑھائے گا۔ اس خلفشار سے بہتر یہی ہے کہ فرادی فرادی نماز کسوف ادا کریں۔
And the imam who leads them in Jumu'ah should lead them in it (the eclipse prayer). If he is not present, the people should pray individually to avoid fitna. Explanation: The issue is that for the eclipse prayer, the imam who leads the people in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eid prayers should be appointed. If the Jumu'ah imam is not present, the people should pray individually because there is no possibility of fitna in that. In the case of congregation, there is a strong possibility of fitna, in that every person will try to become the imam or will push forward an imam of their liking. To avoid such confusion, it is better that they perform the eclipse prayer individually.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement addressing the proper leadership for the solar eclipse prayer. The matn says that the same imam who leads the Friday prayer should lead the eclipse prayer. If that imam is absent, then the people should pray individually, not as a congregation. The commentary explains the rationale: having a congregation without the established imam can lead to fitna (disorder, conflict) as people may compete to lead or insist on different imams. To prevent such discord, it is better for each person to pray alone. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle of prioritizing social harmony (maslaha) and avoiding fitna. The text does not cite a prophetic hadith here; rather, it relies on ijtihad based on the general objective of preventing disorder.

Key Terms
امام جمعہ (imām al-jum'ah): The imam appointed to lead the Friday prayer; he is the official imam for the community.
فرادى (furādā): Individually, each person prays alone without congregation.
فتنہ (fitnah): Disorder, conflict, or tribulation that may arise from communal disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the eclipse prayer is led by the Jumu'ah imam; if absent, praying individually prevents fitna.

No Congregation for Lunar Eclipse Prayer
States rulings on congregation and sermon for lunar eclipse prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lunar eclipse prayer regarding congregation and khutbah, and identify the proof used.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse prayer is prayed individually, not in congregation, due to practical difficulty and lack of transmitted evidence.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two clear rulings about the lunar eclipse prayer: there is no congregational prayer and no sermon. These rulings are grounded in practical considerations and a general prophetic command. Let's examine the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and list the two distinct rulings: no congregation for lunar eclipse, and no khutbah in eclipse prayer.
The rulings are separate but connected.
2
Understand the reasons
Note the two reasons given for no congregation: difficulty of gathering at night (ta'addhur al-ijtima' fi al-layl) and fear of fitna. For no khutbah, the reason is simply that it was not transmitted (lam yunqal).
Reasons are practical and based on transmission.
3
Analyze the proof
The hadith 'When you see any of these terrors, resort to prayer' is cited. Consider how it supports individual prayer: it is general, not specifying congregation.
The command is to pray, not to pray in congregation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may allow congregation for lunar eclipse. The Hanafi school restricts it to avoid hardship and fitna.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس في خسوف القمر جماعة لتعذر الاجتماع فى الليل أو لخوف الفتنة وانما يصلى كل واحد بنفسه لقوله اذا رأيتم شيئا من هذه الاهوال فافزعوا الى الصلوة وليس فى الكسوف خطبة لانه لم ينقل
And there is no congregation in the lunar eclipse due to the difficulty of gathering at night or out of fear of fitna. Rather, each person prays by himself, because of his statement: 'When you see any of these terrors, resort to prayer.' And there is no sermon in the eclipse because it has not been transmitted.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: first, that there is no congregational prayer for the lunar eclipse (khisuf al-qamar), and second, that there is no khutbah (sermon) in either the solar or lunar eclipse prayer. For the lunar eclipse, congregation is not established due to the practical difficulty of gathering at night and the potential for fitna (disorder). Therefore, each person should pray individually. The proof is the general command from the Prophet to resort to prayer when witnessing such terrors, which does not specify congregation. The second ruling—no khutbah in eclipse prayer—is based on the absence of transmitted evidence (lam yunqal). These rulings reflect the Hanafi adherence to the sunnah as transmitted and the principle of avoiding unnecessary hardship and fitna.

Key Terms
خسوف القمر (khusūf al-qamar): Lunar eclipse, the celestial event for which a sunnah prayer exists.
جماعة (jamā'ah): Congregational prayer, which is not established for lunar eclipse.
خطبة (khuṭbah): Sermon delivered often in Friday and Eid prayers; not transmitted for eclipse prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Supplication After the Eclipse Prayer
Ruling on supplication after solar eclipse prayer until the sun shines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of supplication after the eclipse prayer and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to make supplication after the eclipse prayer until the sun shines.

The eclipse prayer is followed by a supplication that continues until the sun reappears. This lesson examines the evidence for this practice and the manner in which it is performed. The author cites a direct command of the Prophet to turn to Allah during such panics, and the hadith of Abu Umamah about the best times for supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is supplication (du'a) after salat al-kusuf. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Not wajib, because the evidence indicates desirability.
2
Locate the dalil
The author quotes the hadith: 'When you see something of these panics, then turn eagerly to Allah with supplication.'
Also cites the hadith of Abu Umamah about 'after the obligatory prayers.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'irghabu' indicates desirability (nadb) not obligation. The hadith of Abu Umamah specifies timing after prayer.
In Hanafi usul, commands default to wujub unless there is a qarina (supporting evidence) here it is the nature of du'a.
4
Note the timing and manner
Supplication is after the prayer until the sun shines, facing qibla or the people, with congregation saying amin.
This is specific to solar eclipse (until sun shines).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدعو بعدها حتى تنجلى الشمس لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا رانتم من هذه الا فزاع شيئا فارغبوا الى الله بالدعاء والسنة فيالادعية تاخيرها عن الصلواة ترجمہ اور نماز کے بعد دعا کرے یہاں تک کہ آفتاب روشن ہو جائے کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب تم ان گھبرا دینے والی چیزوں میں سے کچھ دیکھو تو دعا کے ساتھ اللہ کی طرف رغبت کرو۔ اور دعاؤں میں سنت یہ ہے کہ نماز کے بعد ہو۔ تشریح فرمایا ہے کہ نماز کسوف کے بعد آفتاب روشن ہونے تک دعا کی جائے دعا قبلہ رخ بیٹھ کر کرے یا کھڑے ہو کر کرے خواہ لوگوں کی طرف منہ کر کے دعا کرے اور لوگ قبلہ رخ بیٹھیں اور امام کی دعا پر آمین کہتے رہیں۔ دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے اذا رأيتم من هذا الافذاع شيئاً فارغبوا الى الله بالدعاء صاحب کتاب فرماتے ہیں کہ دعاؤں میں مسنون یہ ہے کہ نماز کے بعد ہو۔ ابو امامہ سے مروی ہے قیل یا رسول الله الى الدعا اسمع قال جوف الليل الأخير ودبر الصلوة المكتوبة آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ کون سی دعا زیادہ مقبول ہے فرمایا کہ آخری رات کا درمیانی حصہ اور فرض نماز کے بعد اس حدیث سے فقط فرض نماز کے بعد دعا کا مسنون ہونا معلوم ہوا۔ اس کے علاوہ مغیرہ بن شعبہ نے کہا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نماز کے بعد دعا کرتے تھے۔ ( بخاری فی التاریخ الاوسط)
He makes supplication after it until the sun shines, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'When you see something of these panics, then turn eagerly to Allah with supplication.' And the sunnah regarding supplications is that they be delayed until after the prayer. Translation: And after the prayer, supplicate until the sun becomes bright, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'When you see something of these frightening things, turn towards Allah with supplication.' And the sunnah in supplications is that they be after the prayer. Elaboration: It is said that after the eclipse prayer, supplication is made until the sun shines; supplication should be made facing the qibla while sitting or standing, or facing the people while they face the qibla, and they say amin to the imam's supplication. The proof is this saying of the Prophet: 'When you see something of this panic, then turn eagerly to Allah with supplication.' The author says: Among supplications, the sunnah is that it be after the prayer. It is narrated from Abu Umamah: It was said, 'O Messenger of Allah, which supplication is most heard?' He said: 'The last part of the night and after the obligatory prayers.' This hadith indicates that supplication after obligatory prayer is sunnah. Additionally, Mughirah ibn Shu'bah said that the Prophet used to make supplication after prayer (Bukhari in Tarikh al-Awsat).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the supplication after the solar eclipse prayer. The author states that after the eclipse prayer, the imam and congregation should make supplication until the sun reappears, based on the hadith command to turn to Allah with supplication when seeing such phenomena. The sunnah manner is to delay the supplication until after the prayer, as supported by the hadith of Abu Umamah about the best times for supplication being the last part of the night and after obligatory prayers. The commentary elaborates on the etiquette: one may face the qibla or the people, and the congregation says amin. This applies specifically to the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf).

Key Terms
دبر الصلاة (dubr al-salat): After the prayer; the time immediately following the completion of the prayer.

Imam for Eclipse Prayer
Ruling on who leads the eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who leads the eclipse prayer and identify when individuals should pray alone.

Core Idea
The regular Friday imam leads; if absent, pray alone to avoid fitna.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on the imam for eclipse prayer. The school prescribes that the same imam who leads Friday and Eid prayers should lead the eclipse prayer to maintain order. However, if he is not present, individuals should pray separately rather than forming a new congregation, due to the risk of fitna (disorder).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is salat al-kusuf (eclipse prayer) and that the Hanafi school considers it a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Determine the preferred imam
Note that the text states the imam who leads Friday prayer should also lead the eclipse prayer. This is to preserve consistency and avoid disputes.
3
Understand the exceptional case
If the Friday imam is absent, the ruling changes: people should pray individually, not in congregation. This is to prevent fitna (conflict or disorder).
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The ruling is based on sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil) – the potential for chaos if multiple people vie for leadership is avoided by mandating individual prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى بهم الإمام الذى يصلى بهم الجمعة و ان لم يحضر صلى الناس فرادى تحرزا عن الفتنة ترجمہ اور نماز کسوف لوگوں کو وہ امام پڑھائے جو ان کو جمعہ پڑھاتا ہے اور اگر امام حاضر نہ ہوا تو لوگ تنہا نماز پڑھیں تا کہ فتہ پیدا ہونے سے بچار ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کسوف میں اس کو امام مقرر کیا جائے جو لوگوں کو جمعہ اور عیدین کی نماز پڑھاتا ہے اور اگر امام جمعہ موجود نہ ہو تو لوگ بینہ اتنہا [بذات خود] نماز ادا کریں کیونکہ اس میں فتنہ کا امکان نہیں ہے اور جماعت کی صورت میں فتنہ کا غالب امکان ہے بایں طور کہ ہر شخص امام بنے کی کوشش کرے گا یا اپنی حسب منشاء امام کو آگے بڑھائے گا۔ اس خلفشار سے بہتر یہی ہے کہ فرادی فرادی نماز کسوف ادا کریں۔
And the imam who leads them in Friday prayer should lead them, and if he is not present, the people pray individually to avoid fitna. Translation: And the eclipse prayer should be led by the imam who leads them in Friday prayer. If the imam is not present, then people pray alone to avoid fitna. Elaboration: The issue is that for eclipse prayer, the imam who leads Friday and Eid prayers should be appointed. If the Friday imam is not present, then people pray by themselves because there is no possibility of fitna, whereas with congregation there is a strong possibility of fitna, i.e., everyone would try to become imam or push forward their preferred imam. To avoid this confusion, it is better that they pray eclipse prayer individually.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the imam for eclipse prayer. The Hanafi school prescribes that the regular Friday imam should lead the eclipse prayer if he is present. If he is absent, individuals should pray alone rather than form a congregation, to prevent fitna (disorder) as people might dispute over who should lead. This is based on the principle of blocking the means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i').

Key Terms
الفتنة (al-fitna): Disorder, dissension, or conflict that may arise from competing claims to lead the prayer.
إمام الجمعة (imam al-jumu'ah): The person who regularly leads the Friday congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Lunar Eclipse: No Congregation, No Khutbah
Ruling on lunar eclipse prayer and its legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lunar eclipse prayer and explain why it is sunnah not wajib, citing the dalil and the principle of shi'ar.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse: pray individually, no congregation, no khutbah; the eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on prayer during a lunar eclipse (khusuf). The text presents the ruling that there is no congregation and no khutbah, and the prayer is performed individually. It also explains why the eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah rather than wajib, addressing the apparent conflict with the imperative in the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the prayer performed during a lunar eclipse. According to the Hanafi school, the ruling is sunnah muakkadah, performed individually without congregation or khutbah.
2
State the Hanafi position
The text explicitly says: there is no congregation in lunar eclipse prayer, each person prays by himself, and there is no khutbah.
The reasoning includes difficulty of gathering at night or fear of fitna.
3
Cite the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's statement: 'When you see something of these terrors, then flee to prayer.' The hadith does not mention congregation, so the default is no congregation.
The dalil is a hadith, which is zanni al-thubut.
4
Identify the potential objection
A reader might object: the hadith uses an imperative (fafzi'u), and in Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation (wujub). This would suggest eclipse prayer is wajib, not sunnah.
5
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that eclipse prayer is not from the distinctive rituals of Islam (sha'a'ir) because it is occasional, not continual. Therefore the imperative is interpreted as recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
The lack of being a shi'ar and the temporary nature of the event prevent the imperative from indicating wujub.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس في خسوف القمر جماعة لتعذر الاجتماع فى الليل أو لخوف الفتنة وانما يصلى كل واحد بنفسه لقوله اذا رأيتم شيئا من هذه الاهوال فافزعوا الى الصلوة وليس فى الكسوف خطبة لانه لم ينقل ترجمہ اور چاند کے گہن میں جماعت نہیں ہے یا تو اس وجہ سے کہ رات میں لوگوں کا جمع ہونا متعذر ہے یا اس وجہ ہے کہ فلتہ [فتنہ] کا خوف ہے اور ہر آدمی بذات خود اپنی نماز پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب تم ان ہولناک چیزوں میں سے کچھ دیکھو تو گھبرا کر نماز کی طرف جاؤ اور کسوف میں خطبہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ خطبہ پڑھنا منقول نہیں ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ چاند گہن کی صورت میں اگر نماز پڑھائی تو اس میں جماعت نہیں ہے یا تو اس لئے کہ رات میں لوگوں کا اکٹھا ہو نا متعذر ہے یا اس وجہ سے کہ رات میں فتنہ کا خوف ہے پس ہر آدمی بذات خود اکیلا اکیلا نماز پڑھے دلیل آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول اذا رأيتم شيئا من هذه الاهوال فافزعوا إلى الصلوۃ ہے وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں جماعت کی تصریح نہیں کی گئی ہے اور اصل عدم جماعت ہے اس لئے کہا گیا ہے کہ خسوف قمر میں جماعت نہیں ہے یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ فافز عوا الی الصلوۃ امرکا صیغہ ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اس لئے مناسب ہوگا کہ نماز کسوف کو واجب قرار دیا جائے جواب چونکہ نماز کسوف شعائر اسلام میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ عارض کسوف کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے نماز کسوف واجب نہ ہوگی لیکن چونکہ مدنی آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پڑھی ہے اس لئے مسنون ہوگی اور حدیث کے اندر امر کا صیغہ ندب کے لئے ہے نہ کہ وجوب کے لئے ۔
And there is no congregation in the lunar eclipse, due to the difficulty of gathering at night or due to fear of fitna. Rather, each person prays by himself, because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'When you see something of these terrors, then flee to prayer.' And there is no khutbah in the eclipse because it was not transmitted. Translation: And there is no congregation in the lunar eclipse, either because gathering at night is difficult or because of fear of fitna. And each person prays by himself, because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'When you see something of these terrors, then flee to prayer.' And there is no khutbah in the eclipse because it was not transmitted. Elaboration: If eclipse prayer is performed in a lunar eclipse, there is no congregation, either because gathering at night is difficult or because of fear of fitna. So each person prays alone individually. The evidence is the statement of the Prophet: 'When you see something of these terrors, then flee to prayer.' The reasoning is that the hadith does not specify congregation, and the original rule is no congregation. Here a question arises: The phrase 'fafzi'u' is a command form, and the command indicates obligation, so eclipse prayer should be wajib. The answer: Because eclipse prayer is not among the distinctive symbols of Islam (shi'ar), but rather due to the temporary phenomenon of eclipse, therefore eclipse prayer is not wajib. However, since the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم performed it, it is sunnah. And the command form in the hadith is for recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the lunar eclipse (khusuf). The Hanafi school states that there is no congregation for lunar eclipse prayer, based on the difficulty of nighttime gathering and potential for fitna, and because the hadith command to pray uses a general form without specifying congregation. The author also clarifies that eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib, addressing a potential objection: the hadith uses an imperative verb ('fafzi'u'), which normally indicates obligation. The Hanafi response is that the obligation (wujub) is negated because eclipse prayer is not from the established rituals (sha'a'ir) of Islam but rather a response to a temporary event; the imperative is interpreted as recommendation (nadb). Additionally, no khutbah is delivered because it was not transmitted from the Prophet.

Key Terms
خسوف القمر (khusuf al-qamar): Lunar eclipse; the prayer during it is performed individually without congregation.
شعائر الإسلام (sha'a'ir al-islam): Distinctive rituals of Islam that are regularly performed, such as the five daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because congregation is never allowed at night
B) Because of the difficulty of gathering at night or fear of fitna
C) Because the hadith explicitly says to pray alone
D) Because the lunar eclipse occurs rarely

Key Takeaway
Lunar eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah, performed individually without congregation or khutbah, because it is not a constant ritual of Islam and the hadith command is interpreted as recommendation.

Dispute on Khutbah in Eclipse Prayer
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on whether khutbah is recited in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on khutbah in eclipse prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using dalil and response.

Core Idea
The Prophet's khutbah during an eclipse was to correct a misconception, not a permanent sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine a classic inter-madhhab dispute: whether a khutbah (sermon) is recited after the eclipse prayer. The Hanafi school, following al-Quduri, holds that no khutbah is given. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a hadith of Aisha. We will carefully unpack the Hanafi response, which relies on juristic reasoning (istidlal) and critical evaluation of the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the khutbah in eclipse prayer. According to Imam al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah, there is no khutbah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that after the eclipse prayer, two khutbahs are delivered, similar to the Eid prayer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i position is based on the hadith of Aisha: 'The sun eclipsed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, so he prayed, then delivered a khutbah.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis offer multiple responses: (1) Khutbah is only prescribed as a condition of validity (like Jumu'ah) or for teaching (like Eid), neither applies here; (2) The Prophet's khutbah was specific to that event to correct a false belief; (3) The word 'khutbah' may mean 'supplication'; (4) The report is not widely transmitted (mashhur).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'is include two khutbahs in eclipse prayer; Hanafis do not, considering them unnecessary and not part of the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ کسوف اور خسوف کی نماز میں خطبہ نہیں ہے امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ سلام کے بعد عیدین کی طرح دو خطبہ ہیں اور دلیل میں حدیث عائشہ کو پیش کیا انها قالت كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى ثم خطب فحمد الله واثنی علیہ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ خطبہ دو باتوں میں سے ایک کے لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے یا تو خطبہ جواز صلوۃ کی شرط ہے جیسے نماز جمعہ میں ہے یا تعلیم احکام کے لئے ہے جیسے عیدین کی نماز میں ہے نماز کسوف کے اندر دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی نہیں ہے اس لئے نماز کسوف کے لئے خطبہ مشروع نہ ہوگا اور حدیث عائشہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے میں کسوف آفتاب سے لوگوں کو یہ وہم ہو گیا تھا کہ یہ حادثہ صاحبزادہ ومحترم حضرت ابراہیم کے سانحہ ارتحال کی وجہ سے پیش آیا ہے پس نماز کسوف کے بعد خطبہ کے ذریعہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس وہم کا ازالہ فرمایا اور کہا ان الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله تعالى لا ينكسفان لموت احد ولا لحیاتہ یعنی چاند اور سورج اللہ کی نشانیوں میں سے دو نشانیاں ہیں یہ کسی کے مرنے اور جینے سے گہن نہیں ہوتے۔ صاحب کفایہ نے کہا ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ کے قول خطب کے معنی دعا کے ہیں۔ کیونکہ دعا کو بھی خطبہ کہا جاتا ہے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ بطریق شہرت حدیث خطبہ منقول نہیں ہے اس لئے حدیث عائشہ قابل استدلال نہ ہوگی جمعیل عفی عنہ۔
Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that in the solar and lunar eclipse, there is no khutbah. Imam al-Shafi'i said that after the salam there are two khutbahs like the two Eids, and he cited the hadith of Aisha: 'The sun eclipsed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, so he prayed, then delivered a khutbah, praising Allah and extolling Him.' Our response is that the khutbah is prescribed for one of two things: either it is a condition for the validity of the prayer, as in Friday prayer, or it is for teaching rulings, as in Eid prayer. In eclipse prayer, neither of these applies, so khutbah is not prescribed for eclipse prayer. The response to Aisha's hadith is that at the time of the Prophet, people had the misconception that the eclipse was due to the death of his son Ibrahim, so the Prophet delivered the khutbah after the eclipse prayer to remove this misconception, saying: 'The sun and moon are two signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death or life of anyone.' The author of al-Kifayah said that 'khutbah' in Aisha's statement means supplication, because supplication is also called khutbah. The author of al-Hidayah said that the hadith of khutbah is not transmitted via a well-known (mashhur) chain, so Aisha's hadith cannot be used as evidence. Jameel 'afi 'anhu?
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage records an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a khutbah (sermon) is part of the eclipse prayer. The Hanafi position, stated by al-Quduri and the author, is that no khutbah is delivered. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for two khutbahs after the prayer, like the Eid prayer, citing a hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed then delivered a khutbah. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, khutbah is only legislated either as a condition for prayer validity (like Jumu'ah) or for teaching (like Eid), and neither applies to eclipse prayer. Second, the Prophet's khutbah on that occasion was to correct the false belief that the eclipse was caused by the death of his son, not to establish a sunnah. Additionally, al-Kifayah interprets 'khutbah' in the hadith as 'supplication', and al-Hidayah notes that the report of khutbah is not transmitted on the level of mashhur (widely known), thus not reliable as evidence.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): A sermon; in this context, the speech delivered after the eclipse prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They deny the hadith entirely
B) They say the Prophet did it only to correct a false belief, not as a sunnah
C) They say the khutbah was actually before the prayer
D) They claim the hadith is fabricated

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not prescribe a khutbah in eclipse prayer because the Prophet's khutbah was a one-time correction of a misconception, not a regular sunnah.

The Definition of Istisqa and Hanafi Position on Prayer
Definition and title justification for istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istisqa precisely and explain why the Hanafi school does not prescribe a specific sunnah prayer for it.

Core Idea
Istisqa is seeking rain by dua and repentance, not a prescribed sunnah prayer in the Hanafi school.

In this short passage, the author of Al-Hidayah breaks his usual pattern: instead of titling a chapter 'The Prayer of Istisqa', he simply says 'Chapter of Istisqa'. This deliberate choice flags a major fiqh point — that the Hanafi school does not recognize a specific sunnah prayer for seeking rain. Let’s unpack the definition and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Notice the title: why not 'Salat al-Istisqa'?
The author explicitly states he did not use 'صلاة' because Imam Abu Hanifa holds there is no sunnah prayer for istisqa. This is the key legal indicator.
The title reflects a deliberate omission, signalling a substantive difference from other schools.
2
Define istisqa linguistically and legally
Istisqa literally means seeking water. Legally, it is the act of going out to an open place to supplicate for rain when natural water sources are absent or insufficient for human and animal needs.
This definition sets the scope: it only applies when there is genuine need.
3
Extract the conditions for performing istisqa
From the text: istisqa is performed only when there is no river, lake, spring, etc., or when existing sources are insufficient. If water is sufficient, istisqa is not done.
The condition is severe need (shiddat al-haja).
4
Note the Hanafi position on prayer
Since there is no sunnah prayer, the istisqa consists solely of dua (supplication), repentance (istighfar), and possibly charity — not a formal prayer with rak'ahs.
Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki) do prescribe a prayer; this is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء ترجمہ (یہ) باب استقاء (کے احکام میں) ہے تشریح مصنف نے باب صلوۃ الاستقاء نہیں کہا ہے جیسا کہ گذشتہ ابواب میں مصنف کی عادت رہی ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس میں نماز مسنون نہیں ہے اسلئے عنوان میں صلوٰۃ کا لفظ ذکر نہیں کیا۔ استقاء سیرابی چاہنا واضح ہوا کہ استقاء ایسے مقام پر ہوتا ہے جہاں دریا جھیل اور چشمہ وغیر نہ ہوں جن سے خود پانی پئیں اور اپنے جانوروں کو پلائیں یا یہ چیزیں ہوں مگر ان کی ضرورت کو کافی نہ ہوں۔ اور اگر یہ چیزیں کافی نہ ہوں تو گوی استقاء کے لئے نہیں نکلیں گے۔ کیونکہ استقا شدت ضرورت کے وقت ہوتا ہے پھر جب

The reason is that in the Hanafi school, there is no specific sunnah prayer prescribed for seeking rain, unlike other chapters where a prayer is sunnah. The commentary defines istisqa as seeking water (water for drinking and animals) when natural water sources are absent or insufficient. No Sunnah Prayer for Istisqa: Abu Hanifa's View and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
States that no sunnah congregational prayer exists for istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on istisqa prayer, identify his Quranic and prophetic evidence, and explain the disagreement with his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Istisqa is dua and istighfar, not a congregational sunnah prayer.

Imam Abu Hanifa takes a distinctive position that seeking rain (istisqa) does not require a special congregational prayer. Instead, the core acts are supplication and seeking forgiveness. However, his two foremost students disagreed, and the later mufta bihi position follows them. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs, and the school's internal debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is istisqa? Seeking rain from Allah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no sunnah prayer in congregation for it. Individual prayer is permissible but not established as sunnah.
The ruling is a negation: 'no sunnah prayer'.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Imam Abu Hanifa cites Surah Nuh (71:10-11): 'Ask forgiveness of your Lord… He will send rain upon you.' The operative word is 'istaghfiru' (seek forgiveness), not 'sallu' (pray). This indicates that the prescribed means for rain is istighfar, not a formal prayer.
The verse connects istighfar directly to rain, establishing it as the primary cause.
3
Examine the Prophetic practice
The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed istisqa (supplicated for rain), but no specific prayer was reported from him. The absence of transmission (la tura 'anhu) is cited as evidence that he did not prescribe a congregational prayer for this occasion.
This argument relies on silence, which in usul is not proof of prohibition but here complements the Quranic emphasis on dua.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the imam leads two rak'ats in congregation for istisqa, similar to the Eid prayer. Their view is based on other hadiths and qiyas.
This disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi practice (tarjih of the muta'akhkhirin) adopts the view of the Sahibayn. The congregational prayer of two rak'ats is considered sunnah mu'akkadah. However, Abu Hanifa's view remains a legitimate variant.
The mufta bihi is the position of the Sahibayn, but the text here presents Abu Hanifa's original view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابو حنيفة ليس فى الاستسقاء صلوة مسنونة فى جماعة فان صلى الناس وحد اناجاز و انما الاستسقاء الدعاء والاستغفار لقوله تعالى فَقُلْتُ اسْتَغْفِرُوا رَبَّكُمْ إِنَّهُ كَانَ غَفَّارُ الآية و رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استسقى ولم ترو عنه الصلواة
Abu Hanifa said: There is no sunnah prayer in congregation for istisqa. If people pray individually, it is permissible. Istisqa is only supplication and seeking forgiveness, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So I said, 'Ask forgiveness of your Lord, indeed He is Oft-Forgiving'... and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed istisqa and prayer was not reported from him.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa that there is no established sunnah prayer for rain (istisqa) in congregation. The core of istisqa is supplication (dua) and seeking forgiveness (istighfar), not a specific prayer. The proof is the Quranic verse (Surah Nuh, 71:10-11) where seeking forgiveness is linked to sending rain, and the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed istisqa but no prayer was reported from him. Individual prayer is permissible but not the sunnah. This is a ruling statement with proof (dalil naqli). The commentary explains the reasoning and the evidence.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa'): Seeking rain from Allah through supplication and other acts.
مسنونة (masnunah): Established by the Prophet's continuous practice; a sunnah act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A congregational prayer of two rak'ats
B) Supplication and seeking forgiveness
C) A sermon
D) Fasting for three days

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that istisqa is dua and istighfar, not a sunnah congregational prayer; however, the mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn in prescribing two rak'ats in congregation.

Is the Istisqa Prayer Sunnah? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istisqa prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the istisqa prayer and evaluate the Sahibayn's argument for its sunnah status.

Core Idea
A single action does not establish a sunnah; continuity (istinbab) is required.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the Prophet's istisqa prayer should be considered a sunnah congregational prayer, while Abu Hanifa (and the Hanafi school as a whole) rejects that view. The disagreement hinges on how we interpret a single narrated action: does it establish a binding precedent?

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the exact point of contention: is the congregational prayer for istisqa a sunnah or not?
2
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn hold that the imam should lead two rak'ats, based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ats like 'Eid.
3
State the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and his followers respond that the Prophet did it only once and omitted it on other occasions, so it cannot be considered an established sunnah.
The key principle is that a single occurrence (fi'la wahida) does not create a continuous practice (sunnah).
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Sahibayn advocate a congregational prayer led by the imam with two rak'ats like 'Eid; Abu Hanifa holds that no such congregational prayer is sunnah, though individuals may pray if they wish.
5
Recognize the later mufta bihi
Although the source text presents Abu Hanifa's view, later Hanafi practice followed the Sahibayn, considering the prayer sunnah.
This demonstrates how the madhhab can evolve over time based on evidence and need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالا يصلى الامام ركعتين لما روى النبي صلى فيه ركعتين كصلوة العيد رواه ابن عباس قلنا فعله مرة وتركه اخرى فلم يكن سنة وقد ذكر فى الاصل قول محمد وحده

We (Hanafis) say: He did it once and left it another time, so it is not a sunnah. And it is mentioned in al-Asl the statement of Muhammad alone.

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the Imam should lead two rak'ats for istisqa, based on a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ats like 'Eid. The Hanafi response (following Abu Hanifa) is that the Prophet did this only once and omitted it on other occasions, so it does not become an established sunnah. The text notes that in al-Asl, only Imam Muhammad's statement is recorded, implying that Abu Yusuf may have later agreed with Abu Hanifa or that the narration is weak. The commentary explains the nature of the dispute: the issue is whether the prayer is sunnah or merely permissible. The hadith evidence is acknowledged but considered insufficient to establish istinbab (continuity).

Key Terms
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
استسقاء (istisqa): Prayer for rain.
سنة (sunnah): Established practice of the Prophet, either as a recommended act or as a binding precedent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Details of Istisqa Prayer: Jahri Recitation and Khutba
States Sahibayn's ruling on loud recitation and sermon in istisqa prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's ruling on jahr in istisqa prayer and distinguish between Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions on the number of sermons.

Core Idea
Istisqa prayer follows 'Eid: two rak'ats jahr, then a khutba — but Sahibayn differ on whether it's one or two sermons.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the details of the istisqa (rain prayer) according to the Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. It addresses two points: the recitation should be loud (jahr) by analogy to 'Eid prayer, and a sermon is delivered after the prayer. However, the two imams differ on the structure of that sermon. Understanding this internal Hanafi ikhtilaf clarifies the operative rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is the istisqa prayer. The Sahibayn hold that it is performed (unlike Abu Hanifa who doesn't require its performance). For them, it has specific sunnah details.
2
Note the ruling on recitation
Recitation is jahr (loud) in both rak'ats, by analogy to 'Eid prayer.
3
Note the ruling on sermon
After prayer, a khutba is delivered, as per Prophetic practice.
4
Analyze the internal ikhtilaf
Muhammad says two sermons (with sitting) like 'Eid; Abu Yusuf says one sermon. The text doesn't give tarjih, but later practice follows Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجهر فيهما بالقرأة اعتبارا بصلوة العيد ثم يخطب لماروى ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطب ثم هي كخطبة العيد عند محمد وعند ابي يوسف خطبة واحدة
And one should recite loudly in both (rak'ats) analogizing to the 'Eid prayer. Then he delivers a sermon, because it is reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) delivered a sermon. Commentary
This passage gives the ruling of the Sahibayn on the details of the istisqa prayer if it is performed. The recitation in both rak'ats should be loud, by analogy to 'Eid prayer. After the prayer, a sermon is delivered, as the Prophet did. There is a difference between the two: Imam Muhammad holds that the sermon consists of two parts like 'Eid (with a sitting in between), while Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is one single sermon. This ruling is built on the premise that the prayer is performed, which is the position of the Sahibayn, not Abu Hanifa. The commentary explains the analogy and the internal ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation audible to the congregation.
خطبة (khutba): Sermon delivered after the prayer.
استسقاء (istisqa): Prayer for rain.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's ruling on istisqa: loud recitation and a khutba, with a difference on its number: one (Abu Yusuf) or two (Muhammad).

Salah in Istisqa': Permissible or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istisqa' salah ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi position that salah in istisqa' is permissible (mubah) and the view that it is sunnah, and explain how the principle 'al-nadir ka al-ma'dum' resolves the apparent contradiction in the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Salah in istisqa' is permissible (mubah) but not sunnah in the relied-upon Hanafi view, because the Prophet sometimes omitted it and rare narrations are treated as non-existent.

In this passage from the Hidayah commentary, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of performing two rak'ahs in the prayer for rain (istisqa'). While Imam Muhammad and other schools consider it a sunnah, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that it is merely permissible. The discussion revolves around the strength of the hadith evidence and the Prophet's inconsistent practice. We will walk through the arguments and the Hanafi principle that resolves the tensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rival positions within the Hanafi school
First, note that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) initially appear together, but here Abu Yusuf sides with Abu Hanifa. The relied-upon view is that the prayer is permissible but not sunnah.
Imam Muhammad alone holds it is sunnah; Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa.
2
Analyze the opposing dalil: the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Abdullah ibn Zayd
These hadith explicitly mention the Prophet praying two rak'ahs for rain. Understand why they are strong evidence for permissibility but not for sunnah status.
The texts are ahad (not mutawatir) and the Prophet's practice was inconsistent.
3
Apply the Hanafi response: the principle of inconsistency and 'al-nadir ka al-ma'dum'
The Prophet sometimes performed the prayer and sometimes omitted it. This inconsistency prevents establishing it as a sunnah. Moreover, the narrations are rare (nadir), so they are treated as non-existent according to the Hanafi usul rule.
'Al-nadir ka al-ma'dum' means the rare is like non-existent.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction in the matn
The matn first says 'no prayer is narrated' then mentions a narration. The commentator resolves this by applying the same principle: since the narration is rare, it is considered as if not narrated.
This showcases the integration of usul al-fiqh in understanding fiqh texts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah al-khilaf
The relying-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: salah in istisqa' is mubah, not sunnah. The practical difference is that according to this view, one may perform it but is not encouraged to do so as a sunnah.
Imam Muhammad's view would make it recommended (sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء تشریح استقاء میں صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ امام لوگوں کو دو رکعت پڑھائے یہی قول امام مالک امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ دلیل ابن عباس کا قول ہے خرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم متبذلا متواضعا متضرعا حتى أتى المصلى فلم يخطب خطبتكم هذه ولكن لم يزل في الدعا والتضرع والتكبير وصلى ركعتين كما يصلي في العيدين (رواه أصحاب السنن) یعنی رسول اللہ انتہائی عاجزی اور انکساری کے ساتھ نکل کر عید گاہ تشریف لے گئے لیکن آپ نے خطبہ نہیں پڑھا اور برابر دعا اور گریہ وزاری میں لگے رہے اور آپ نے دو رکعت نماز پڑھی جیسا کہ عیدین میں پڑھی جاتی ہے دوسری روایت عبداللہ بن زید بن عاصم کی ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج بالناس يستسقي بهم فصلى بهم ركعتين وحول رداءه ورفع يديه فدعا واستسقى واستقبل القبلة (متفق علیہ) یعنی رسول اللہ لوگوں کو لے کر استقاء کے لئے نکلے پھر ان کو دو رکعت پڑھائی اور اپنی چادر کو الٹ دیا۔ اور دونوں ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کی اور استقاء کیا اور استقبال قبلہ کیا۔ ان دونوں روایتوں سے استقاء کے لئے نماز پڑھنا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ نے استقاء میں کبھی نماز پڑھی ہے اور کبھی اس کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے نماز استسقاء کا جواز تو ثابت ہو سکتا ہے لیکن مسنون ہونا ثابت نہ ہو گا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ جواز کا ہم بھی انکار نہیں کرتے بلکہ کلام نماز استقاء کے مسنون ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں ہے۔ اور سنت وہ ہے جس پر نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پیشگی فرمائی ہو۔ سوال: اس جگہ مصنف کی عبارت پر یہ اشکال ہو سکتا ہے کہ مصنف نے پہلے کہا لم يرو عنه الصلاة اور پھر فرمایا لما روی ظاہر ہے کہ ان دونوں عبارتوں میں تناقض ہے۔ جواب: حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے استقاء میں نماز کی روایت چونکہ شاذ اور نادر ہے اس لئے النادر کالمعدوم کے قاعدہ سے اس مروی کو بھی غیر مروی قرار دیدیا ہے پس اب کوئی تعارض نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ استسقاء میں نماز کا مسنون ہونا فقط امام محمد کا قول ہے اور امام ابو یوسف امام صاحب کے ساتھ ہیں اسی طرح مبسوط میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
Chapter of Istisqa'. Commentary: The madhhab of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the imam should lead the people in two rak'ahs. This is also the saying of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. The proof is the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, went out humbly, submissively, and supplicatingly until he came to the prayer ground. He did not deliver a sermon like this sermon of yours, but he continued in supplication, humility, and takbir, and he prayed two rak'ahs as he prays on the two Eids.' (Narrated by the authors of the Sunan). That is, the Messenger of Allah went out with extreme humility and meekness to the Eid ground, but he did not deliver a sermon and remained in supplication and weeping, and he prayed two rak'ahs as is prayed on the two Eids. Another narration is from Abdullah ibn Zayd ibn Asim: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, went out with the people to pray for rain, and he prayed two rak'ahs with them, turned his cloak, raised his hands, supplicated, prayed for rain, and faced the qibla.' (Agreed upon). That is, the Messenger of Allah went out with the people for istisqa', then he led them in two rak'ahs, turned his cloak, raised both hands in supplication, prayed for rain, and faced the qibla. From both these narrations, praying for rain is established. Our response is that he (peace be upon him) sometimes prayed for rain and sometimes omitted it. Therefore, the permissibility of salah al-istisqa' can be established from this, but not its being sunnah. And it is obvious that we do not deny permissibility; rather, the discussion is about whether it is sunnah or not. And sunnah is that which the Prophet, peace be upon him, consistently performed. Question: In this place, an objection can be raised on the author's text: he first said 'no prayer is narrated from him' and then said 'because it is narrated'. Clearly, there is a contradiction between these two statements. Answer: Since the narration of prayer in istisqa' from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is odd (shadh) and rare (nadir), by the principle 'the rare is like non-existent', this narration is also considered as not narrated, so there is no contradiction. The author of Hidayah says that the sunnah status of salah in istisqa' is only the opinion of Imam Muhammad, and Imam Abu Yusuf is with Imam Abu Hanifa. Similarly, it is mentioned in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of performing two rak'ahs of prayer in the istisqa' (prayer for rain). The two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the imam should lead the people in two rak'ahs, similar to the Eid prayer. This is also the opinion of the three other major imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad). They support this with two hadiths: the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa and supported by Abu Yusuf, is that although prayer for rain is permissible (ja'iz), it is not sunnah (masnun) because the Prophet did not consistently perform it; he sometimes omitted it. The author then addresses an apparent contradiction in the matn: the author of the matn (Quduri) stated that no prayer is narrated from the Prophet, yet later he mentions a narration. The commentator resolves this by invoking the principle 'al-nadir ka al-ma'dum' (the rare is like non-existent), deeming the narration as effectively unmarrated due to its rarity. Finally, the Hidayah clarifies the intra-Hanafi position: the sunnah status is only Imam Muhammad's view; Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa that it is not sunnah. This ruling is also found in al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa'): The prayer for rain; a specific form of supplication and prayer performed during drought.
النادر كالمعدوم (al-nadir ka al-ma'dum): A Hanafi usul principle that treats a rarely occurring narration or ruling as non-existent for legal purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that salah al-istisqa' is permissible (mubah), not sunnah, due to the Prophet's inconsistent practice and the rarity of the narrations, resolved by the principle 'al-nadir ka al-ma'dum'.

Recitation and Khutbah in Istisqa' Salah
Ruling on recitation and khutbah in istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting aloud and delivering the khutbah in istisqa' salah, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In istisqa', the Sahibayn require jahr and khutbah by qiyas to Eid; Abu Hanifa rejects the khutbah because no congregation.

This lesson examines two specific rulings for the istisqa' salah: the mode of recitation and the delivery of the khutbah. You will see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas to Eid and how an intra-madhhab difference arises on the status of congregation. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps clarify the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage addresses two separate issues in istisqa' salah: (1) whether the imam recites aloud (jahr) in the two rak'ahs, and (2) whether a khutbah is delivered after the salah.
These rulings are distinct but both are analogized to Eid prayer.
2
Apply the qiyas to Eid
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that jahr and khutbah are sunnah, based on qiyas to the Eid prayer. The common illa (effective cause) is that both are congregational prayers performed in an open space with a specific purpose.
The text says 'اعتبارا بصلوة العيد' – analogizing to Eid prayer.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on khutbah
Abu Hanifa holds that there is no khutbah in istisqa' because the khutbah is dependent on the existence of a congregation (jama'ah), and in his view istisqa' is not performed with a congregation. The Sahibayn hold that a congregation is present, so a khutbah is sunnah. Additionally, among the Sahibayn, Muhammad says two khutbahs (like Eid) and Abu Yusuf says one khutbah.
All three Imams agree on jahr; the ikhtilaf is solely on the khutbah.
4
Examine the dalil for both sides
The Sahibayn rely on qiyas to Eid and the hadith that the Prophet delivered a khutbah. Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that the khutbah is a follower of congregation; since he does not consider istisqa' a congregational prayer, the khutbah drops.
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: recite aloud in both rak'ahs and deliver a khutbah (either one or two, with the majority preferring one). This is because it is the more widely transmitted view (zahir al-riwayah) and is supported by hadith.
The commentator in Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Sahibayn's view as operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جہراً قرأت کا حکم ويجهر فيهما بالقرأة اعتبارا بصلوة العيد ثم يخطب لماروى ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطب ثم هي كخطبة العيد عند محمد وعند ابي يوسف خطبة واحدة ترجمہ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ دونوں رکعت میں جہر سے قرآت کرے عید کی نماز پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے پھر خطبہ پڑھے کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ اللہ کے نبی علیہ السلام نے خطبہ پڑھا ہے پھر یہ خطبہ عید کے خطبہ کے مانند ہے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایک ہی خطبہ ہے۔ تشریح صاحبین نے کہا کہ نماز عید کی طرح استقاء کی دونوں رکعتوں میں قرآت بالجبر کرے پھر خطبہ پڑھے۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے خطبہ پڑھنا ثابت ہوا ہے لیکن امام محمد کے نزدیک عید کی طرح دو خطبہ ہیں دونوں کے درمیان بیٹھ کر فصل کرے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایک ہی خطبہ ہے زمین پر کھڑے ہو کر لوگوں کی طرف متوجہ ہو کر پڑھے۔  باب الاستسقاء ۳۳۶ اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدایة بعد نماز استسقاء میں خطبہ کا حکم ولا خطبة عند ابي حنيفة لأنها تبع للجماعة ولا جماعة عنده ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک خطبہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ خطبہ جماعت کے تابع ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک جماعت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح عبارت واضح اور نا قابل تشریح ہے۔
Ruling on reciting aloud: And he recites aloud in both rak'ahs, analogizing to the Eid prayer. Then he delivers a khutbah because it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, delivered a khutbah. Then this khutbah is like the khutbah of Eid according to Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf, it is one khutbah. Translation: The two companions said that in both rak'ahs, he should recite aloud, analogizing to the Eid prayer. Then he should deliver a khutbah because it is narrated that the Prophet of Allah, peace be upon him, delivered a khutbah. Then this khutbah is like the Eid khutbah according to Imam Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf, it is one khutbah. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, there is one khutbah, delivered standing on the ground, facing the people. [PAGE_335] Chapter of Istisqa' 336 Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Bidayah. Ruling on khutbah in istisqa' prayer: And there is no khutbah according to Abu Hanifa because it is dependent on congregation, and he does not have congregation. Translation: And according to Abu Hanifa, there is no khutbah because the khutbah is dependent on congregation, and according to Imam Sahib, there is no congregation. Commentary: The expression is clear and needs no commentary.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage addresses two rulings in istisqa': recitation and khutbah. The two companions (Sahibayn) rule that the imam must recite aloud (jahr) in both rak'ahs, by analogy (qiyas) to the Eid prayer. After the salah, he should deliver a khutbah, based on the hadith that the Prophet delivered a khutbah. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the number of khutbahs: Imam Muhammad says two, like Eid, with a sitting between them; Imam Abu Yusuf says one khutbah, delivered while standing. Then the text presents Abu Hanifa's position: there is no khutbah at all in istisqa' because the khutbah is dependent on the existence of a congregation (jama'ah), and in his view, there is no congregation in istisqa' (since he does not consider the salah to be performed in congregation). The commentator notes that this ruling is clear.

Key Terms
الجهر بالقراءة (al-jahr bi al-qira'ah): Reciting the Quran audibly in the prayer.
الخطبة (al-khutbah): A sermon delivered after the salah in istisqa'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is there no khutbah in istisqa'?
A) Because the Prophet never delivered a khutbah
B) Because the khutbah is dependent on congregation, and Abu Hanifa holds there is no congregation
C) Because it is makruh to deliver a khutbah after prayer
D) Because the khutbah is only for Eid

Key Takeaway
In istisqa' salah, the imam recites aloud and delivers a khutbah after the prayer, following the Sahibayn's qiyas to Eid, though Abu Hanifa differed on the khutbah.

The Ruling on Turning the Cloak in Istisqa'
Rulings on facing qibla, turning cloak, and dhimmis in istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') during istisqa', explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
Turning the cloak is not required; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reject it; Imam Muhammad recommends it.

The prayer for rain (istisqa') includes several recommended acts. One of the most discussed is whether the imam should invert his cloak (qalb al-rida') while supplicating. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point, its evidence, and the practical ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts in istisqa'
The passage discusses three matters: facing the qibla, turning the cloak, and allowing dhimmis. Focus on the second: the imam turning his cloak.
Facing qibla is agreed upon; dhimmis are excluded.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not turn the cloak; Imam Muhammad does. This is a legitimate difference within the school.
The majority (including Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) follow Muhammad's view.
3
Analyze the dalil of Abu Hanifa
The du'a is analogous to other supplications (qiyas), and turning the cloak is not reported in other du'as.
The hadith of the Prophet turning is interpreted as a good omen (tafa'ul) or a revelation-based specific action.
4
Understand Muhammad's evidence
The hadith that the Prophet turned his cloak is taken literally as a sunnah, and the imam should follow it.
Muhammad also describes the method of turning.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: do not turn the cloak.
This is the position for fatwa.

رداء اگر چکور ہے تو اوپر کا حصہ نیچے کر دے اور نیچے کا حصہ او پر کر دے اور اگر مدرد ہے جیسے جیسع تو دایاں حصہ بائیں طرف کر دے اور بائیں حصہ دائیں طرف کر دئے اور بایاں حصہ دایاں حصہ کی طرف کر دے قلب جواب جس میں تحویل رد مروی ہے یہ ہے کہ یہ تفاؤلا تھا یا یہ حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کو وحی کے ذریعہ آسمان کے حال کا متغیر ہونا قلب رداء کے وقت معلوم ہو گیا ہوگا اس لئے آپ نے قلب رد فرمایا ہے۔ صاحب قدوری Ruling on facing qibla for du'a: And he faces the qibla with his supplication because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) faced the qibla and turned his cloak. And he turns his cloak – we have narrated this. He said: this is the saying of Muhammad. But according to Abu Hanifa, he does not turn his cloak because it is a supplication, so it is analogized to other supplications. And what was narrated was for good omens. And the people do not turn their cloaks because it is not transmitted that he commanded them to do so. And the people of dhimmah do not attend the istisqa' because it is to seek the descent of mercy, and only curses descend upon them. Translation: And the supplication: he should face the qibla because it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he faced the qibla and turned his cloak. And he should invert his cloak because of this hadith that we have narrated. The author said that this is the saying of Imam Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, he will not turn the cloak because it is a supplication, so it is analogized to other supplications. And what was narrated was for good omens. And the people do not turn their cloaks because it is not transmitted that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded them to do so. And the dhimmis should not attend istisqa' because istisqa' is a supplication seeking the descent of mercy, and curses descend upon them. Commentary: In the du'a of istisqa', the recommended method is to face the qibla because facing qibla and turning (the cloak) in du'a is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Sahib al-Quduri said that he should turn his cloak. The method is: if the cloak (rida') is square, he should put the top part down and the bottom part up; if it is a madrad (a striped garment) like a jaisa', he should put the right side to the left and the left side to the right. The proof for turning the cloak is the aforementioned narration. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The ruling of turning the cloak is the madhhab of Imam Muhammad; this is also the view of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. As for Imam Abu Hanifa, his madhhab is that he should not turn the cloak, and this is also the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that it is a du'a, so it should be analogized to other du'as, and in those there is no turning of the cloak. So in the du'a of istisqa' also, there is no turning of the cloak. And the answer to the narration in which turning the cloak is narrated is that it was for good omens, or that the Prophet (peace be upon him) knew through revelation that the condition of the sky would change at the time of turning, so he turned his cloak. Sahib al-Quduri said: The people should not turn their cloaks because the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned his cloak, but the people also turned theirs, and he... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings: facing qibla during the du'a, turning the cloak (qalb al-rida'), and the attendance of dhimmis. First, the imam should face the qibla when making the du'a for rain, based on the hadith that the Prophet did so. Second, regarding turning the cloak, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that the imam should turn his cloak, and this is also the view of Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Quduri. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that he should not turn it because it is a du'a, and other du'as do not involve turning. The narration about the Prophet turning his cloak is interpreted as either a good omen (tafa'ul) or a specific action based on revelation. The people (the congregation) are not to turn their cloaks because it is not reported that the Prophet commanded them. Third, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) should not attend the istisqa' because it is a prayer for mercy, and mercy does not descend upon them; rather, curses descend. The method of turning the cloak is described: for a square cloak, switch top and bottom; for a madrad (striped garment), switch left and right sides.

Key Terms
قلب الرداء (qalb al-rida'): The act of turning or inverting one's cloak during the istisqa' du'a.
التفاؤل (al-tafa'ul): Seeking a good omen; the Prophet's turning of the cloak is interpreted as a good omen for a change in weather.
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa'): The prayer for rain, performed when there is a drought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Turn it from top to bottom if it is square
B) Turn it from left to right if it is striped
C) Not turn it at all
D) Turn it in any direction to seek good omen

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative position is that the imam does not turn his cloak during istisqa', based on qiyas to other supplications, despite a contrary view from Imam Muhammad.

No Khutbah in Istisqa' Prayer (Hanafi View)
Ruling that no khutbah in istisqa' due to absence of congregation in Hanafi definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the khutbah in salat al-istisqa' and explain the reasoning based on the dependency on congregation.

Core Idea
No khutbah in istisqa' — the khutbah depends on congregation, and Abu Hanifa sees no formal congregation here.

This brief passage from Al-Hidayah encapsulates a distinctive Hanafi ruling: the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa') is performed without a khutbah. Why? Because the khutbah is tied to the concept of congregation (jamā'ah) in a specific legal sense, and Abu Hanifa holds that this type of congregation is absent in the istisqa' prayer. Understanding this ruling sheds light on how Hanafi jurists define congregational obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State what Abu Hanifa says about the khutbah in salat al-istisqa'.
The text explicitly states: 'ولا خطبة عند أبي حنيفة'.
2
Identify the reason
Find the reason given for the absence of the khutbah.
The reason is 'لأنها تبع للجماعة' — because it is a follow-up to congregation.
3
Understand the link
Explain how the khutbah is dependent on congregation according to Hanafi legal theory.
Hanafis view the khutbah as a secondary element that only becomes obligatory when a formal congregational prayer (like Jumu'ah or Eid) is established.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) require a khutbah for istisqa'.
This difference stems from varying definitions of jamā'ah and the nature of the prayer.
5
Apply the ruling
Determine what should be done in practice when performing istisqa' as a Hanafi.
Perform two rak'ahs without a sermon, then make supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا خطبة عند أبي حنيفة لأنها تبع للجماعة ولا جماعة عنده.
And there is no khutbah according to Abu Hanifa because it is a follow-up to congregation, and he does not consider a congregation present.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah. The passage states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no khutbah (sermon) in the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa'). The reason given is that the khutbah is dependent on the congregation (jamā'ah), and in the view of Abu Hanifa, there is no congregation in the sense required for the Friday sermon. This is because the istisqa' prayer is not a congregational prayer with the same conditions as Jumu'ah. The commentary in Ashraf al-Hidayah explains that this statement is clear and needs no further elaboration. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other imams may differ.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered in congregational prayers, especially Jumu'ah and Eid; here referring to its absence in istisqa'.
جماعة (jamā'ah): Congregation; here meaning the formal congregational prayer that makes khutbah necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is there no khutbah in salat al-istisqa'?
A) Because it is a sunnah prayer
B) Because the khutbah is dependent on congregation, and Abu Hanifa does not consider there to be a congregation
C) Because it is performed in the desert
D) Because the prayer is too short

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school omits the khutbah in istisqa' because it is contingent on a formal congregation absent in this prayer.

Facing Qibla and Turning the Cloak in Istisqa'
Ruling on facing qibla and turning the cloak with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla and turning the cloak in istisqa' and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding turning the cloak.

Core Idea
Facing qibla in istisqa' is sunnah; turning the cloak is disputed — Abu Hanifa rejects it as a mere omen.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the conduct of the imam during the supplication of istisqa' (prayer for rain). The author first affirms facing the qibla as established practice, then enters an intra-madhhab dispute regarding turning the cloak. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists weigh contradictory evidence between a prophetic action and legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The imam should face the qibla when supplicating during istisqa'. This is sunnah based on the Prophet's action. Also, there is discussion about turning the cloak.
The text begins with 'ويستقبل القبلة بالدعا'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) faced the qibla and turned his cloak. This is cited as evidence.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that the imam should also turn his cloak (قلب رداء) because the Prophet did so. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that he should not turn his cloak.
The matn presents Muhammad's view first, then Abu Hanifa's.
4
Trace the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa argues that istisqa' is a supplication, and other supplications do not involve turning the cloak. Therefore, by qiyas (analogy), turning is not required. The hadith is interpreted as an omen (tafa'ul) particular to the Prophet.
This is an example of istihsan overriding a weak dalil.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: the imam should not turn his cloak. The congregation also should not turn their cloaks.
Al-Marghinani supports Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستقبل القبلة بالدعا لما روى انه صلى الله عليه وسلم استقبل القبلة وحول رداءه ويقلب رداءه روينا قال لهذا قول محمد اما عند ابي حنيفة فلا يقلب رداءه لانه دعاء فيعتبر بسائر الادعية وما رواه كان تفاؤلا ولا يقلب القوم ارديتهم لانه لم ينقل انه امرهم بذلك ولا يحضر اهل الذمة الاستسقاء لانه لاستنزال الرحمة وانما تنزل عليهم اللعنة.
And he should face the qibla with supplication because it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, faced the qibla and turned his cloak. And he should turn his cloak, according to what we narrated. (The author) said: This is the statement of Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, he does not turn his cloak because it is a supplication, so it is analogized to other supplications; and what was narrated was an omen. And the people should not turn their cloaks because it was not reported that he commanded them to do so. And the dhimmis should not attend the istisqa' because it is for seeking mercy, while curses descend upon them.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Al-Hidayah rules on the supplication of istisqa'. It states that the imam should face the qibla when making supplication, based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) faced the qibla and turned his cloak. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on turning the cloak: Imam Muhammad holds that the imam should turn his cloak (change its position) as a practice; Imam Abu Hanifa holds that he should not, because it is a supplication and should be analogized to other supplications where turning is not done. The hadith about turning is interpreted as an omen (tafa'ul) or the Prophet's personal action, not a general command. Additionally, the people (congregation) should not turn their cloaks, as the Prophet did not command them. Finally, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) should not attend the istisqa' ceremony because it is a plea for mercy, and curses are sent down upon them.

Key Terms
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Turning the cloak; changing the position of the outer garment by reversing it (top-bottom or left-right) as a symbolic act.
تفأل (tafa'ul): Omen; interpreting an event as a good sign. Here, the Prophet's turning of the cloak is seen as an omen for changing of the weather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa reject turning the cloak in istisqa'?
A) Because the hadith is weak.
B) Because it is a supplication and should be analogized to other supplications where turning is not done.
C) Because the cloak is not available.
D) Because the Prophet never did it.

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla in istisqa' is sunnah, but turning the cloak is not part of Hanafi practice because qiyas overrides the hadith of the Prophet's action.
