Excluding Dhimmis from Istisqa' Prayer
Ruling on excluding non-Muslim subjects from istisqa' with the legal reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that dhimmis should not attend istisqa' and explain the legal reason (illah) based on the incompatibility of seeking mercy and their association with curse.

Core Idea
Dhimmis are excluded from istisqa' because mercy is sought, but they are associated with divine curse.

This short passage from Al-Hidayah extends the regulations of istisqa' to non-Muslim subjects. It prohibits their presence, grounding the ruling in the incompatible spiritual symbolism of mercy versus curse. Understanding this ruling clarifies the community boundaries in collective supplications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules that dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state) should not attend the istisqa' prayer.
The verb 'لا يحضر' indicates a prohibition.
2
Locate the legal reason (illah)
The reason given is that istisqa' is for seeking mercy (rahman), and dhimmis are associated with curse (lanah) because of their disbelief.
The illah is the contrasting spiritual states: mercy vs. curse.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Acts of worship that specifically seek divine mercy should be conducted by those who are in a state of faith and deserving of mercy, not by those who reject Allah.
This is not a general rule for all acts of worship; it is specific to istisqa' which is a plea for rain and mercy.
4
Note the application
In practice, the imam should ensure that dhimmis are not present during the istisqa' ceremony. This includes the prayer and the supplication.
The ruling applies to the entire istisqa' gathering, not just the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستقبل القبلة بالدعا لما روى انه صلى الله عليه وسلم استقبل القبلة وحول رداءه ويقلب رداءه روينا قال لهذا قول محمد اما عند ابي حنيفة فلا يقلب رداءه لانه دعاء فيعتبر بسائر الادعية وما رواه كان تفاؤلا ولا يقلب القوم ارديتهم لانه لم ينقل انه امرهم بذلك ولا يحضر اهل الذمة الاستسقاء لانه لاستنزال الرحمة وانما تنزل عليهم اللعنة.
And he should face the qibla with supplication because it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, faced the qibla and turned his cloak. And he should turn his cloak, according to what we narrated. (The author) said: This is the statement of Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, he does not turn his cloak because it is a supplication, so it is analogized to other supplications; and what was narrated was an omen. And the people should not turn their cloaks because it was not reported that he commanded them to do so. And the dhimmis should not attend the istisqa' because it is for seeking mercy, while curses descend upon them.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Al-Hidayah rules on the supplication of istisqa'. It states that the imam should face the qibla when making supplication, based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) faced the qibla and turned his cloak. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on turning the cloak: Imam Muhammad holds that the imam should turn his cloak (change its position) as a practice; Imam Abu Hanifa holds that he should not, because it is a supplication and should be analogized to other supplications where turning is not done. The hadith about turning is interpreted as an omen (tafa'ul) or the Prophet's personal action, not a general command. Additionally, the people (congregation) should not turn their cloaks, as the Prophet did not command them. Finally, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) should not attend the istisqa' ceremony because it is a plea for mercy, and curses are sent down upon them.

Key Terms
اهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimmah): Non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state who pay jizyah and are protected.
اللعنة (al-l'anah): Curse; Allah's displeasure and punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal reason (illah) for prohibiting dhimmis from attending istisqa'?
A) They are not required to pray.
B) Istisqa' is for seeking mercy, and curses descend upon them.
C) They do not believe in rain.
D) They would disrupt the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Dhimmis are excluded from istisqa' because mercy and curse are incompatible in the context of a supplication for rain.

8 min
Method of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer) in Intense Danger
Ruling describing the method of the fear prayer with proof from Ibn Mas'ud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the method of salat al-khawf when fear is intense, explain the roles of lahiqun and masbuqun, and cite the Prophet's practice as transmitted by Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf: the imam leads two groups in one rak'ah each; the first group completes silently, the second with recitation.

When Muslims face the enemy in battle, the obligation of prayer remains. The Shari'ah provides a practical method known as Salat al-Khawf, which balances worship with military vigilance. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the exact sequence for intense fear, along with the Prophetic proof, so that you can understand both the procedure and its basis in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger
Note that this method applies when fear is intense (اشتد الخوف). Understand that the ruling is conditional on extreme danger, not ordinary fear.
2
Divide the army into two groups
The imam splits the soldiers: one group faces the enemy, the other stands behind the imam for prayer. This ensures continuous defense.
3
Pray the first rak'ah with the first group
The imam leads the first group in one complete rak'ah (with two sajdahs). After the second sajdah, this group withdraws to the front line without saying salam.
The imam does not yet say salam.
4
Pray the second rak'ah with the second group
The second group joins the imam for one rak'ah. After this rak'ah, the imam says tashahhud and salam, but the second group does not say salam and immediately goes to the front.
The imam's prayer is complete after two rak'ahs.
5
Complete the prayer for each group
The first group returns and prays one rak'ah alone without recitation (they are lahiqun). The second group later returns and prays one rak'ah alone with recitation (they are masbuqun). Both then say tashahhud and salam.
Lahiqun: caught part with imam and complete later. Masbuqun: joined late and make up missed part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ا اشتد الخوف جعل الامام الناس طائفتين طائفة على وجه العدود وطائفة خلفه فيصلى بهدة الطائفة ركعة سجدتين فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية مضت هذة الطائفة الى وجه العدو وجائت تلك الطائفة على بهم الامام ركعة وسجدتين و تشهد وسلم ولم يسلموا وذهبوا الى وجه العدو وجاءت الطائفة اولى فصلوا ركعة وسجدتين وحدانا بغير قراءة لانهم لاحقون وتشهد و اوسلموا ومضوا الى وجه العدو جاءت الطائفة الأخرى وصلوا ركعة وسجدتين بقراءة لانهم مسبوقون وتشهدا وسلموا والاصل فيه رابة ابن مسعود ان البنى عليه السلام صلى صلوة الخوف على الصفة التي قلنا و ابويوسف وأن انكر وعيتها في زماننا فهو محجوج عليه بما روينا.
When fear becomes intense, the imam makes the people into two groups: a group facing the enemy and a group behind him. He prays with this group one rak'ah with two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, this group goes to face the enemy, and that other group comes. He leads them in one rak'ah and two prostrations, then recites tashahhud and says salam, but they do not say salam. They go to face the enemy, and the first group comes back. They pray one rak'ah and two prostrations alone without recitation because they are followers (lahiqun). Then they recite tashahhud and say salam, and go to face the enemy. The other group comes and prays one rak'ah and two prostrations with recitation because they are preceded (masbuqun), then recite tashahhud and say salam. The basis for this is the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed the fear prayer in the manner we have described. And Abu Yusuf said: And whoever denies its occurrence in our time is refuted by what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah provides the method of salat al-khawf (fear prayer) when the enemy is close and danger is severe. The imam divides the army into two groups. Group A prays one rak'ah with the imam. After the second sajdah, group A goes to the front, and group B comes. The imam leads group B in one rak'ah, including tashahhud and salam. Group B does not say salam but goes to the front. Group A returns and prays their second rak'ah alone without Quranic recitation because they are 'lahiqun' (those who followed part of the prayer with the imam and complete it later). They recite tashahhud and salam. Then group B returns and prays their second rak'ah with recitation because they are 'masbuqun' (those who joined late and must make up what they missed). The proof is a narration from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed this way. The text adds that Abu Yusuf affirmed the practice, and anyone who denies its occurrence in later times is refuted by the transmitted report.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The fear prayer; a specific method of performing obligatory prayer in congregation while facing the enemy during battle.
لاحقون (lahiqun): Those who have caught part of the prayer with the imam and complete the remainder individually.
مسبوقون (masbuqun): Those who joined the prayer late and missed part of it with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the first group (lahiqun) pray their second rak'ah without recitation?
A) Because they are tired from battle
B) Because they already recited in the first rak'ah with the imam and are considered followers
C) Because the imam recited for them
D) Because the prayer is shortened

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf in intense fear involves a specific rotation: the imam leads two groups in one rak'ah each, and the groups complete their second rak'ah alone – the lahiqun silently, the masbuqun with recitation, based on the Prophet's practice.

Ruling on Dhimmis Attending Istisqa' Prayer
Ruling on dhimmis attending istisqa' with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmis attending istisqa' and explain the dalil and rationale.

Core Idea
Dhimmis may attend istisqa' only if accompanied by Muslims to avoid fitna.

The prayer for rain (istisqa') is a communal supplication seeking Allah's mercy. But what about the participation of non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis)? This passage from Sahib Taduri presents the Hanafi ruling, supported by a Quranic verse and the agreement of Imams Malik, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad. Understanding this ruling reveals the school's concern for protecting the sanctity of worship and preventing misunderstandings about divine response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on whether dhimmis should attend the istisqa' prayer. The ruling is not a blanket prohibition but a nuanced position: they should not be commanded to go, but if they go voluntarily, they must be accompanied by Muslims.
The ruling is specific to external participants, not the prayer's validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 40:50: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is nothing but in error.' This is the primary proof. The verse indicates that the supplication of disbelievers is not accepted, so their presence in a prayer seeking mercy is problematic.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the Quran.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse describes disbelievers' supplication as 'fi dalal' (in error/loss). The Hanafi reasoning: if their supplication is futile, attending a congregational supplication for rain could mislead others into thinking their prayer is answered if rain falls, thus causing fitna. Therefore, they should not be invited, but if they come, Muslims must accompany them to prevent solo supplication.
The dalala is zanni (speculative) but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Note the consensus (ikhtilaf)
The passage claims agreement among Imams Malik, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad. This is not a dispute but a unified position across three schools.
No intra-Hanafi difference is mentioned; the ruling is mufta bihi per Sahib Taduri.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The ruling aims to avoid fitna: if dhimmis go alone and rain falls, people might attribute it to their supplication, weakening faith. The prescribed accompaniment ensures that any rain is attributed to the Muslims' prayer.
The rationale is protective (sadd al-dhara'i').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب تدوری نے کہا ہے کہ استقاء میں ذمی لوگ حاضر نہ ہوں کیونکہ مسلمانوں کا نکلنا نزول رحمت کی دعا کے لئے ہے اور کفار کے بارے میں اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا ہے وَمَا دُعَاءُ الكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِی ضَلال یعنی کفار کی دعا ضائع اور خسران ہے۔ امام مالک امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام احمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ ذمیوں کو استقاء کے واسطے نکلنے کا حکم نہ دیا جائے اور اگر وہ از خود نکلیں تو منع بھی نہ کیا جائے لیکن یہ بات ادا رکھی جائے کہ ذمی لوگ کسی ایک تن تنہا نہ نکلیں بلکہ جب وہ نکلیں تو کچھ مسلمان ان کے ساتھ ضرور نکلیں کیونکہ استقاء کے ذریعہ طلب ان مقصود ہوتا ہے اور اللہ تعالی مومن اور کافر سب کو رزق دیتا ہے پس اگر کفار کسی دن تنہا نکلیں اور بارگاہ ایزدی میں دعا کی اور اتفاق سے روز بارش ہو گئی تو بڑا فتنہ برپا ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ۔
Sahib Taduri said that dhimmis should not be present in istisqa' because the Muslims go out to supplicate for the descent of mercy, and regarding the disbelievers Allah Most High said: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is nothing but in error' (Quran 40:50), meaning that the supplication of disbelievers is wasted and loss. Imam Malik, Imam Abu Hanifa, and Imam Ahmad said that dhimmis should not be commanded to go out for istisqa', and if they go out on their own, they should not be prevented, but this matter should be observed: that dhimmis should not go out alone, but when they go out, some Muslims must also go out with them, because through istisqa' the request is intended, and Allah Most High gives sustenance to both believers and disbelievers. So if disbelievers go out alone one day and supplicate at the Divine Court, and by chance it rains, a great fitna would occur. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad ʿufiya ʿanhu.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the attendance of dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) at the istisqa' (prayer for rain). The author, Sahib Taduri (likely a Hanafi scholar), states that dhimmis should not be present because the purpose of the Muslims' gathering is to supplicate for mercy, and the Quran (40:50) indicates that the supplication of disbelievers is in vain. The ruling is supported by a consensus of Imams Malik, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad: dhimmis are not commanded to go out, but if they do so voluntarily, they should not be prevented. However, a precaution is added: they should never go alone; Muslims must accompany them. The rationale is that if dhimmis go out alone and by chance rain falls, it could cause fitna (trial) by making people think their supplication was accepted. This shows the Hanafi concern for protecting the faith and avoiding misattribution of divine response. The proof is from the Quran, making this a dalil naqli.

Key Terms
استقاء (istisqa'): A special prayer and supplication for rain during drought, performed in congregation.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a contract of protection (dhimma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why should dhimmis not attend istisqa' alone according to this passage?
A) They are not allowed to pray at all
B) Their supplication is not accepted and may cause fitna if rain occurs
C) They must always be accompanied by a Muslim imam
D) It is prohibited for them to even be present

Key Takeaway
To avoid fitna, dhimmis should not be commanded to attend istisqa', but if they do, they must be accompanied by Muslims.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Method of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer)
Detailed procedure of fear prayer with two groups and hadith basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for Salat al-Khawf with two groups, explain why the first group (lāḥiq) prays without recitation while the second (masbūq) recites, and identify the hadith proof that overrides Abu Yusuf's objection.

Core Idea
In fear prayer, the first group (lāḥiq) prays without recitation; the second group (masbūq) recites.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf as recorded in al-Hidayah. We will step through the two-group procedure, understand the distinct rulings for lāḥiq and masbūq, and see how the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud serves as the binding proof. We also address Abu Yusuf's doubt about the practice in later times—and why the majority Hanafi position rejects it.

Guided Path
1
Establish the scenario
Recognize that Salat al-Khawf is performed when the enemy is present. The text mentions 'ishtidd al-khawf' but the commentary clarifies that actual intense fear is not required; the mere presence of the enemy suffices.
The condition is relaxed, similar to travel concessions.
2
Walk through the imam's role
The imam divides the people into two groups. He prays one rak'ah with the first group (behind him), then after the second sajdah that group goes to face the enemy. The second group comes and the imam prays one rak'ah with them, recites tashahhud, and says salam. The second group does NOT say salam yet.
The imam's prayer is two rak'ahs total (one with each group), but he says salam only once.
3
Trace each group's independent rak'ah
After the imam's salam, the first group returns and prays one rak'ah individually without recitation (they are lāḥiq, having caught the beginning with the imam). The second group then prays one rak'ah individually with recitation (they are masbūq, having missed the first rak'ah with the imam). Both groups complete with tashahhud and salam.
Lāḥiq does not recite because he is considered to have completed the recitation with the imam; masbūq must recite his own.
4
Identify the proof and the dispute
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud describes this exact sequence. Abu Yusuf denied the practice in his time, but the commentary states he is 'refuted by the hadith'. The majority Hanafi position (including al-Hidayah) holds the hadith as authoritative and the method remains sunnah.
Abu Yusuf's objection is a legitimate ikhtilaf but the mufta bihi is the described method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الخوف
ترجمہ یہ باب نماز خوف کے بیان میں ہے۔
فریح استقاء اور خوف کی نماز کے درمیان مناسبت یہ ہے کہ دونوں کی مشروعیت عارض خوف کی وجہ سے ہے مگر اتنا فرق ہے کہ استقاء میں عارض یعنی بارش کا منقطع ہو جانا سماوی اور غیر اختیاری ہے اور نماز خوف میں عارض اختیاری ہے یعنی جہاد جس کا سبب کافروں کا کفر اور ظالم کا ظلم ہے پس چونکہ غیر اختیاری چیز اقوی ہوتی ہے اس لئے استقاء کو مقدم کیا گیا۔
صلوٰۃ الخوف پڑھنے کا طریقہ
إذا اشتد الخوف جعل الإمام الناس طائفتين طائفة على وجه العدو وطائفة خلفه فيصلي بهذه الطائفة ركعة وسجدتين فإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية مضت هذه الطائفة إلى وجه العدو وجاءت تلك الطائفة فصلى بهم الإمام ركعة وسجدتين وتشهد وسلم ولم يسلموا وذهبوا إلى وجه العدو وجاءت الطائفة الأولى فصلوا ركعة وسجدتين وحدانا بغير قراءة لأنهم لاحقون وتشهدوا وسلموا ومضوا إلى وجه العدو جاءت الطائفة الأخرى وصلوا ركعة وسجدتين بقراءة لأنهم مسبوقون وتشهدوا وسلموا والأصل فيه رواية ابن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى صلاة الخوف على الصفة التي قلنا وأبو يوسف وإن أنكر عينها في زماننا فهو محجوج عليه بما روينا
جمہ جب خوف بڑھ جائے تو امام لوگوں کو دو گروہ کر دے ایک گروہ کو دشمن کے سامنے چھوڑے اور ایک گروہ کو اپنے پیچھے کرے۔ اس گروہ کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے نماز پڑھائے۔ پس جب اس نے دوسرے سجدہ سے اپنا سر اٹھالیا تو یہ گروہ دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلا جائے اور وہ گروہ آئے پھر امام ان کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پڑھائے اور تشہد پڑھ کر سلام پھیر دے اور اس گروہ کے لوگ سلام نہ پھیریں (بلکہ اسی حالت میں) دشمن کے روبرو چلے جائیں اور پہلا گروہ آجائے۔ اس گروہ کے لوگ ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے تنہا تنہا بغیر قرآت کے پڑھیں۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ لاحق ہیں اور تشہد پڑھ کر سلام پھیر کر دشمن کے مقابلے میں چلے جائیں اور دوسرا گروہ آئے اور ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے قرآت کے ساتھ پڑھیں۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ مسبوق ہیں۔ اور تشہد پڑھ کر سلام پھیر دیں۔ اور اصل اس میں عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز خوف کو اسی صفت پر پڑھا جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور ابو یوسف نے اگر چہ ہمارے زمانے میں اس کی مشروعیت سے انکار کیا ہے مگر ابو یوسف پر حجت ان روایات سے قائم ہے جو ہم نے روایت کیں۔
تشریح قدوری کی عبارت اذا اشتد الخوف سے بظاہر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نماز خوف کے جواز کے لئے اشتداد خوف شرط ہے حالانکہ عامة المشائخ کے نزدیک اشتداد خوف شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ صلوٰۃ خوف کے جواز کے لئے دشمن کا نفس قرب کافی ہے اسی وجہ سے مبسوط میں کہا گیا کہ بعض لوگوں کے نزدیک خوف سے حقیقتہ خوف مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ دشمن کا حاضر ہونا مراد ہے پس دشمن کا موجود ہونا خوف کے قائم مقام ہے جیسے نفس سفر مشقت کے قائم مقام ہو کر رخصت صلوٰۃ اور رخصت افطار وغیرہ کا سبب ہے نماز خوف کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ امام وقت لوگوں کو دو گروہوں میں تقسیم کر دے ایک گروہ کو دشمن کے روبرو کھڑا کر دے اور ایک گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے۔ پس جب امام نے اس رکعت کے دوسرے سجدے سے سر اٹھالیا تو یہ گروہ پیدل چل کر دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلا جائے۔ اور وہ گروہ جو دشمن کے رو برو تھا وہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہو جائے ، امام ان کو ایک رکعت پڑھا کر سلام پھیر دے لیکن یہ لوگ سلام نہ پھیریں بلکہ دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلے جائیں ، اب پہلا گروہ آکر تنہا تنہا اپنی ایک رکعت پڑھ لیں۔ یہ رکعت بغیر قرآت کے ہوئی ، کیونکہ یہ لوگ تحریمہ سے امام کے ساتھ شریک ہونے کی وجہ سے لاحق ہیں اور لاحق پر قرآت واجب نہیں ہے اس گروہ کی نماز پوری ہو گئی ہے۔ لہذا یہ گروہ سلام پھیر کر دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلا جائے اور دوسرا گروہ اپنی ایک رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیر دے۔ ان کی یہ رکعت قرائت کے ساتھ ہے کیونکہ یہ لوگ پہلی رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ شریک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مسبوق ہیں اور مسبوق پر قرآت کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ لوگ قرآت کریں گے ، صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ صلوۃ خوف کے اندر اصل عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی روایت ہے الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں: عن ابن مسعود صلى رسول الله صلوة الخوف فقاموا صفا خلفة و صفا مستقبل العدو فصلى بهم ركعة ثم جاء الآخرون فقاموا في مقامهم و استقبل هؤلاء العدو فصلى بهم ركعة ثم سلم فقام هؤلاء العدو فصلوا لانفسهم ركعة وسلموا، ثم ذهبوا، فقاموا مقام اولئك مستقبلى العدو، و رجع اولئك الى مقامهم فصلوا لانفسهم ركعة ثم سلموا
ابن مسعودؓ سے مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز خوف پڑھی پس ایک گروہ آپ کے پیچھے کھڑا ہوا اور ایک دشمن کے مقابلہ میں ، آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو ایک رکعت پڑھائی ۔ پھر دوسرا گروہ ان کی جگہ آکر کھڑا ہو گیا ، اور یہ دشمن کے مقابلے پر چلے گئے، آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو بھی ایک رکعت پڑھائی پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سلام پھیر دیا، پھر ان لوگوں نے خود ایک رکعت پڑھ کر سلام پھیر دیا، اور جاکر ان کی جگہ دشمن کے مقابلہ میں کھڑے ہو گئے اور وہ ان کی جگہ آئے ، اور تنہا تنہا ایک رکعت پڑھ کر سلام پھیر دیا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر فرمایا ہے کہ اس طرح نماز خوف کی اجازت اس وقت ہے جب کہ ایک امام ہو ، اس کے علاوہ کے پیچھے لوگ نماز پڑھنے کو تیار نہ ہوں لیکن اگر چند امام ہیں اور ان پر کسی کو اختلاف بھی نہیں ہے تو افضل یہ ہے کہ ایک امام ایک گروہ کو پوری نماز پڑھا دے، اور ان کو دشمن کے مقابلہ میں بھیج دے اور دوسرا گروہ جو دشمن کے مقابلہ پر تھا ان میں سے ایک شخص کو حکم دے کہ وہ ان کو نماز پڑھائے۔
Chapter: Prayer of Fear
Translation: This chapter is about the description of the Prayer of Fear.
The connection between istisqa' and the fear prayer is that both have their legislation due to (the) cause of fear, but the difference is that in istisqa' the cause (i.e., the cessation of rain) is celestial and involuntary, while in the fear prayer the cause is voluntary, i.e., jihad, whose cause is the disbelief of disbelievers and the oppression of oppressors. Since the involuntary thing is stronger, istisqa' was given precedence.
The method of performing fear prayer:
When fear is intense, the Imam divides the people into two groups: a group facing the enemy and a group behind him. He prays with this group one rak'ah and two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, this group goes to face the enemy, and that group comes. Then the Imam prays with them one rak'ah and two prostrations, recites the tashahhud and says salam, but they do not say salam. They go to face the enemy, and the first group comes. They pray one rak'ah and two prostrations individually without recitation because they are lāḥiqūn (followers who caught the beginning). They recite tashahhud and say salam, and go to face the enemy. The other group comes and they pray one rak'ah and two prostrations with recitation because they are masbūqūn (those who joined late). They recite tashahhud and say salam. The basis for this is the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed the fear prayer in the manner we have described. And Abu Yusuf, although he denied its existence in our time, is refuted by the hadith we have narrated.
(Urdu explanation follows...)
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage expounds the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer) as presented in al-Hidayah. It begins by connecting the chapter to istisqa' (prayer for rain) by noting both are legislated due to fear, but istisqa' is involuntary (rain stopping) and thus stronger, so it was placed first. The core ruling: when fear is intense (ishtidd al-khawf), the imam divides the congregation into two groups. One group faces the enemy while the imam prays one rak'ah with the other group. After the second sajdah, the first group goes to the enemy, the second group joins the imam for his second rak'ah (which is the group's first). The imam says salam, but this group does not; they go to the enemy. The first group returns and prays one rak'ah individually without recitation (since they are lāḥiqūn, having caught the beginning with the imam). Then the second group prays their remaining rak'ah individually with recitation (as masbūqūn). The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is the basis. The commentary clarifies that 'ishtidd al-khawf' is not strictly a condition according to the majority of Hanafi scholars; rather, the mere presence of the enemy suffices, just as travel hardship permits concessions. A nuance from Sahib al-Inayah: this method applies when there is only one imam and people are unwilling to pray behind another; otherwise, it is better for one imam to lead one group fully and another imam the other group. Abu Yusuf's skepticism about the practice in his time is dismissed because the hadith is established.

Key Terms
لاحق (lāḥiq): One who joins the imam after the first rak'ah but before the second sajdah, thus catching the imam's prayer; they pray their missed rak'ah without recitation.
مسبوق (masbūq): One who joins the imam after the imam has already prayed one rak'ah; they pray their missed rak'ah with recitation.
اشتداد خوف (ishtidād al-khawf): Intensity of fear; the condition mentioned in the matn for the fear prayer, but clarified by the commentary as not strictly necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, why does the first group (lāḥiq) pray their second rak'ah without recitation?
A) Because they are tired from fighting
B) Because they already recited with the imam and are considered to have fulfilled recitation
C) Because the imam recited for them in both rak'ahs
D) Because they are in immediate danger

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is performed by dividing into two groups, each praying one rak'ah with the imam and completing one rak'ah alone; the first group (lāḥiq) prays without recitation, the second (masbūq) with recitation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Method and Proof of Salat al-Khawf
Explains Salat al-Khawf method and clarifies condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf and distinguish the rulings for lahiq and masbuq in this prayer.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the presence of the enemy suffices; the lahiq does not recite, but the masbuq must recite.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method of the Prayer of Fear (Salat al-Khawf) as derived from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. You will learn that the condition for this prayer is not extreme fear but the enemy's presence, and the procedure involves dividing the congregation into two groups. The rulings for recitation depend on whether the worshipper is a lahiq (who joined from the start) or a masbuq (who missed the first rak'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for Salat al-Khawf
The commentator clarifies a potential misunderstanding from Quduri: extreme fear is not a condition. The mere presence of the enemy is sufficient, as it implies fear and is analogous to the hardship of travel (which causes rukhsah).
This shows how the Hanafi school interprets the condition flexibly, focusing on the objective presence rather than subjective fear.
2
Understand the division of the congregation
The Imam splits the followers into two groups. One group faces the enemy while the other prays one rak'ah with the Imam.
The group facing the enemy is not praying during this time; they are guarding.
3
Trace the exchange and second rak'ah
After the first rak'ah, the group that prayed goes to face the enemy, and the guarding group joins the Imam for a second rak'ah. The Imam says salam, but this second group does not say salam; instead, they go to face the enemy.
The Imam's salam does not end the prayer for this group because they still owe one rak'ah.
4
Apply lahiq and masbuq rulings
The first group returns and prays one rak'ah individually without recitation (they are lahiq, having joined from the beginning). The second group later prays one rak'ah individually with recitation (they are masbuq, having missed the first rak'ah).
This distinction is key: lahiq does not recite, masbuq must recite in the missed rak'ah.
5
Confirm with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
The entire method is based on the prophetic practice reported by Ibn Mas'ud. The hadith describes the same sequence: two groups, one rak'ah each with the Prophet, then each group completes their prayer individually.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as evidence for this sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح قدوري کی عبارت اذا اشتد الخوف سے بظاہر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نماز خوف کے جواز کے لئے اشتد او خوف شرط ہے حالانکہ عامة المشائخ کے نزدیک اشتد اد خوف شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ صلوۃ خوف کے جواز کے لئے دشمن کا نفس قرب کافی ہے اسی وجہ سے مبسوط میں کہا گیا کہ بعض لوگوں کے نزدیک خوف سے حقیقتہ خوف مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ دشمن کا حاضر ہونا مراد ہے پس دشمن کا موجود ہونا خوف کے قائم مقام ہے جیسے نفس سفر مشقت کے قائم مقام ہو کر رخصت صلوٰۃ اور رخصت افطار وغیرہ کا سبب ہے نماز خوف کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ امام وقت لوگوں کو دو گروہوں میں تقسیم کر دے ایک گروہ کو دشمن کے روبرو کھڑا کر دے اور ایک گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے ۔ پس جب امام نے اس رکعت کے دوسرے سجدے سے سر اٹھالیا تو یہ گروہ پیدل چل کر دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلا جائے۔ اور وہ گروہ جو دشمن کے رو برو تھا وہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہو جائے ، امام ان کو ایک رکعت پڑھا کر سلام پھیر دے لیکن یہ لوگ سلام نہ پھیریں بلکہ دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلے جائیں ، اب پہلا گروہ آکر تنہا تنہا اپنی ایک رکعت پڑھ لیں۔ یہ رکعت بغیر قرآت کے ہوئی ، کیونکہ یہ لوگ تحریمہ سے امام کے ساتھ شریک ہونے کی وجہ سے لاحق ہیں اور لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہے اس گروہ کی نماز پوری ہو گئی ہے۔ لہذا یہ گروہ سلام پھیر کر دشمن کے مقابلہ پر چلا جائے اور دوسرا گروہ اپنی ایک رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیر دے۔ ان کی یہ رکعت قرائت کے ساتھ ہے کیونکہ یہ لوگ پہلی رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ شریک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مسبوق ہیں اور مسبوق پر قرآت کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ لوگ قرآت کریں گے ، صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ صلوۃ خوف کے اندر اصل عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی روایت ہے الفاظ حدیث یہیں ۔ عن ابن مسعود صلى رسول الله صلوة الخوف فقاموا صفا خلفة و صفا مستقبل العدو وفصلى بهم ركعة ثم جاء الآخرون فقاموا في مقامهم و استقبل هؤلاء العدو فصلى بهم ركعة ثم سلم فقام هؤلاء العدو فصلوا لانفسهم ركعة وسلموا، ثم ذهبوا، فقاموا مقام اولئک مستقبلى العدو، و رجع اولئك الى مقامهم فصلوا لانفسهم ركعة ثم سلموا
Explanation of Quduri's text: From 'when fear intensifies' it appears that intense fear is a condition for the permissibility of Salat al-Khawf, whereas according to the general mashayikh, intense fear is not a condition; rather, the mere presence of the enemy is sufficient. That is why in al-Mabsut it is said that by 'fear' actual fear is not meant, but the presence of the enemy. So the presence of the enemy stands in place of fear, just as the hardship of travel stands in place of travel itself, being the cause for the concession of shortening prayer and breaking fast. The method of Salat al-Khawf is that the Imam divides the people into two groups: one group faces the enemy, and the other group prays one rak'ah with him. When the Imam raises his head from the second sajdah of that rak'ah, this group (the one that prayed) goes on foot to face the enemy. Then the group that was facing the enemy comes and stands behind the Imam. The Imam leads them in one rak'ah and says salam, but they do not say salam; instead they go to face the enemy. Then the first group returns and prays one rak'ah individually. This rak'ah is without recitation because they are lahiq (those who joined the Imam from the beginning) and lahiq does not recite. Their prayer is complete, so they say salam and go to face the enemy. The second group completes their one rak'ah with recitation and says salam. Their rak'ah is with recitation because they are masbuq (those who missed the first rak'ah) and recitation is obligatory for the masbuq. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The basis in Salat al-Khawf is the narration of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The words of the hadith are: From Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah prayed Salat al-Khawf. One row stood behind him and one row facing the enemy. He led them in one rak'ah. Then the others came and stood in their place, and these (the first) faced the enemy. He led them in one rak'ah, then said salam. Then these (the second) stood up and prayed one rak'ah by themselves and said salam. Then they went and stood in the place of those (first) facing the enemy, and those (first) returned to their place and prayed one rak'ah by themselves and said salam.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe explaining the method of Salat al-Khawf (Prayer of Fear) as derived from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The commentator begins by clarifying a potential misunderstanding from Quduri's text: the condition for this prayer is not 'intense fear' but simply the presence of the enemy, as the presence itself implies fear. He then details the procedure: the Imam splits the congregation into two groups, leads one group in one rak'ah, then exchanges them with the other group, leads the second group in one rak'ah, and then each group completes their prayer individually. The key rulings are: the first group (lahiq) does not recite when completing their second rak'ah because they already recited in the first rak'ah with the Imam; the second group (masbuq) must recite in their second rak'ah because they missed the recitation with the Imam. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is provided as the primary evidence, showing the Prophet's practice. The commentary emphasizes that this method is specific to the prayer of fear, and the rulings of lahiq and masbuq are applied accordingly.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A person who joins the Imam from the beginning of the prayer but due to some reason (like moving to face the enemy) prays one rak'ah individually without recitation.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who misses the first rak'ah with the Imam and joins later; he must recite in the rak'ah he prays individually.
صلوة الخوف (salah al-khawf): The prayer performed during battle or in a state of fear of the enemy, with a specific method as described in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Salat al-Khawf as described by the Hanafi school, which group recites when completing their separate rak'ah?
A) The first group (lahiq) recites.
B) The second group (masbuq) recites.
C) Both groups recite.
D) Neither group recites.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, with the key ruling that the lahiq does not recite but the masbuq must recite.

The Perpetual Permissibility of Salat al-Khawf: Abu Yusuf's Objection and the Hanafi Response
Intra-Hanafi dispute on perpetual permissibility of fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Yusuf's objection to Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death and explain why the majority Hanafi position rejects it using the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the Companions' consensus.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf remains prescribed after the Prophet because its cause—fear—persists, and the Companions' practice constitutes consensus.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the continuation of the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf) after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Imam Abu Yusuf, a leading Hanafi authority, initially agreed with the majority but later retracted, arguing that the Quranic command (4:102) was specific to the Prophet's lifetime. The majority Hanafi position, however, maintains its permissibility based on the general cause (fear) and the Companions' unanimous practice. Let us analyze the proofs and the reasoning behind the mufta bihi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the precise issue: Is Salat al-Khawf valid and prescribed after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him)?
The dispute is not about its validity during the Prophet's life, but its continuance.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and his dalil
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that Salat al-Khawf is specific to the Prophet's lifetime. His evidence is Quran 4:102, which addresses the Prophet directly: 'When you are among them and lead them in prayer.' He argues that after the Prophet, the need for the two-group method ceases.
Abu Yusuf initially agreed with the majority, then retracted.
3
Examine the Hanafi response: dalalah-based evidence
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud describes the Prophet's practice of Salat al-Khawf. Although the literal wording does not refute Abu Yusuf, its implication (dalalah) is that the cause of the prayer—fear—is general and not restricted to the Prophet's time. Thus, the ruling applies whenever fear exists.
This is an argument from causality (ta'lil): the sabab (fear) is ongoing.
4
Examine the Hanafi response: Companions' consensus
Multiple Companions (Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abu Ubaydah, Abu Musa, etc.) performed Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death, and no Companion objected. This silent approval amounts to ijma (consensus), which is a binding source of law in Hanafi usul.
The commentator in the passage emphasizes that this ijma overrides Abu Yusuf's individual view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that Salat al-Khawf remains permissible after the Prophet's death, supported by the implication of the hadith and the Companions' consensus. This is the ruling in the Zahir al-Riwayah and accepted by the majority.
Imam Abu Yusuf's contrary view is considered a minority opinion not followed in fatwa.

نماز پڑھنے کی فضیلت کو حاصل کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا۔ آپ کی وفات کے بعد یہ جھگڑا مرتفع ہو گیا اور ہر گروہ علاوہ امام کے ساتھ پوری نماز ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے لہذا آمد و رفت کی صفت کے ساتھ ایک ایک رکعت ادا کرنا جائز نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی روایت امام ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت ہے کیونکہ ابن مسعود کی روایت جو آگے گذر چکی ہے اس میں بالتفصیل رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا نماز خوف پڑھنا ذکر کیا گیا ہے لیکن میں کہتا ہوں کہ امام ابو یوسف نے رسول اللہ کی حیات میں نماز خوف کے مشروع ہونے کا کہاں انکار کیا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف تو آپ کی حیات میں نماز خوف کے مشروع ہونے کے قائل ہیں البتہ وفات کے بعد کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ پس جب ابو یوسف رسول اللہ کے زمانے میں نماز خوف مشروع ہونے کے قائل ہیں تو رسول اللہ کا صلوۃ خوف پڑھانا ابو یوسف کے خلاف کیسے حجت ہو سکتا ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ابن مسعود کی روایت من حیث العبارت اگر ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت نہیں ہے مگر من حیث الدلالت حجت ہے ۔ بایں طور کہ نماز خوف کا سبب خوف ہے اور خوف جس طرح آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حیات میں تحقیق ہے اسی طرح آپ کی وفات کے بعد بھی متحقق ہے پس جس طرح رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں خوف کی وجہ سے نماز خوف مشروع تھی اسی سبب کی وجہ سے آپ کے بعد بھی مشروع ہو گی دوسرا جواب یہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وفات کے بعد صحابہ کا نماز خوف پڑھنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ سعد بن ابی وقاص، ابو عبیدہ بن الجراح اور ابو موسیٰ اشعری نے اصفہان میں نماز خوف پڑھی ہے نیز سعد بن ابی وقاص نے طبرستان میں مجوسیوں سے جنگ کی اور آپ کے ساتھ حسن بن علی ، حذیفہ بن اسحاق اور عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص تھے تو سعید بن ابی العاص نے ان حضرات صحابہ کو نماز خوف پڑھائی، اور کسی نے اس پر انکار نہیں کیا۔ پس یہ عدم انکار بمنزلہ اجماع کے ہو گیا۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وفات کے بعد نماز خوف کے جواز پر صحابہ کے اجماع کر لینے کے بعد حضرت امام ابو یوسف کا نماز خوف کی مشروعیت سے انکار کرنا اچھا سا نہیں لگتا۔
Is Salat al-Khawf legislated after the Prophet's death? According to Sahib al-Hidayah, Imam Abu Yusuf denied its permissibility after the Prophet's death. Initially, Abu Yusuf held it to be permissible like others, then he retracted and said that its permissibility is specific to the Prophet's lifetime. His evidence is that Allah Almighty said: 'And when you are among them and lead them in prayer' (Quran 4:102). This verse specifically commands the Prophet to establish Salat al-Khawf. When he is the Imam, each group will strive to attain the virtue of praying behind him. After his death, this competition is removed, and each group is able to pray the full prayer behind the Imam, so performing one rak'ah each with going back and forth is not valid. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the narration of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is evidence against Abu Yusuf because it details how the Prophet prayed Salat al-Khawf. But I say: Abu Yusuf never denied its permissibility during the Prophet's lifetime. He affirms it during the Prophet's time but denies it after. So how can the Prophet's action be evidence against Abu Yusuf? The answer is that the narration of Ibn Mas'ud is evidence not in its literal wording but in its implication, because the cause (sabab) of Salat al-Khawf is fear, and fear exists both during and after the Prophet's time. Just as fear caused its permissibility then, it should cause it after. A second answer is that it is established that the Companions prayed Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death. For example, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abu Ubaydah ibn al-Jarrah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari prayed it in Isfahan. Also, when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas fought the Magians in Tabaristan with Hasan ibn Ali, Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman, and Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Sa'id ibn al-As led them in Salat al-Khawf, and no one objected. This silence amounts to consensus (ijma). After the Companions' consensus on its permissibility after the Prophet's death, Abu Yusuf's denial seems unreasonable.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the perpetual permissibility of Salat al-Khawf after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentator begins by stating that Sahib al-Hidayah reports that Imam Abu Yusuf denied the continuation of this prayer after the Prophet's death, even though he initially agreed with the general view. Abu Yusuf's argument is based on the Quranic verse (4:102) which addresses the Prophet directly, implying that the specific form of prayer was tied to his presence. After his death, there is no need for the two-group method because everyone can pray fully behind a single Imam without the need for rotation. The commentator then presents the response: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which describes the Prophet's practice, is evidence for the general cause (fear) being the basis, not the Prophet's person. Fear remains a valid cause after his death. Moreover, the Companions themselves performed Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death, as shown by multiple reports, and their silence on its validity constitutes consensus (ijma). Thus, Abu Yusuf's view is outweighed by the practice of the Companions and the general applicability of the cause. The commentator concludes that Abu Yusuf's denial does not hold after the Companions' consensus.

Key Terms
مشروع (mashru'): Legislated or sanctioned by the Shari'ah; here it refers to the permissibility and prescribed nature of Salat al-Khawf.
حیات نبی (hayat al-nabi): The lifetime of the Prophet (peace be upon him), used as a temporal restriction for the permissibility of the prayer in Abu Yusuf's view.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions, which is used as evidence for the permissibility of Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Imam Abu Yusuf's main evidence for restricting Salat al-Khawf to the Prophet's lifetime?
A) The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
B) The Quranic verse 4:102
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) The practice of the Sahihayn

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf remains a valid Sunnah after the Prophet's death because its cause is general fear, supported by the Companions' consensus, and the majority Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Salat al-Khawf with a Resident Imam
States the method for resident Imam in Khawf prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct rak'ah distribution for a resident Imam leading Salat al-Khawf in both four-rak'ah and three-rak'ah prayers, and explain the rationale for the Maghrib method.

Core Idea
The resident Imam compensates the groups: two rak'ahs each for four, but two-plus-one for Maghrib.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a clear ruling on how a resident Imam (muqim) should lead Salat al-Khawf. It distinguishes between prayers with an even number of rak'ahs, like Zuhr, and the odd Maghrib prayer, where the distribution differs due to the indivisibility of a single rak'ah. The first group is given the extra rak'ah because of their precedence (sabq) in praying with the Imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Imam's status
The ruling applies when the Imam is a resident (muqim), not a traveler (musafir). This affects whether the Imam prays full or shortened prayers.
2
Learn the method for four-rak'ah prayers
For a four-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr, the Imam leads each of the two groups in two rak'ahs. Each group completes the remaining two rak'ahs on their own after the Imam finishes.
Based on the narration that the Prophet did so for Zuhr.
3
Learn the method for Maghrib
For the three-rak'ah Maghrib, the Imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second group. The first group already completed two with the Imam, so they pray one alone later; the second group prayed one with the Imam and must pray two alone.
4
Understand the rationale for Maghrib
A single rak'ah cannot be split (tansif), so the extra rak'ah must go entirely to one group. The first group is given priority due to their precedence (sabq) in joining the Imam.
This reasoning is based on legal analogy and fairness.

Source Text

فان كان الامام مقيما صلى بالطائفة الاولى ركعتين و بالطائفة الثانية ركعتين كما روى انه صلى الظهر بالطائفتين ركعتين ركعتين ويصلى بالطائفة الاولى من المغرب ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة واحدة لان تنصيف الركعة الواحدة غير ممكن فجعلها فى الاولى اولى بحكم السبق ترجمہ پھر اگر امام مقیم ہوتو پہلے گروہ کے ساتھ دو رکعت اور دوسرے گروہ کے ساتھ دو رکعت پڑھے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر کی نماز دونوں گروہوں کے ساتھ دو دو رکعت پڑھی ہے اور پہلے گروہ کے ساتھ مغرب کی دو رکعت اور دوسرے گروہ کے ساتھ ایک رکعت پڑھے ۔ کیونکہ ایک ایک رکعت کو آدھا آدھا کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے ۔ اور پہلے گروہ کے سابق ہونے کی وجہ سے اس ایک رکعت کو اس
If the Imam is a resident (muqim), he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and two rak'ahs with the second group, as it is narrated that he prayed Zuhr with both groups, two rak'ahs each. For Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second, because dividing a single rak'ah into halves is not possible, so giving it to the first group is preferable due to their precedence (sabq). Translation: If the Imam is a resident, then he should pray two rak'ahs with the first group and two rak'ahs with the second group, because it is narrated that the Prophet prayed Zuhr with both groups, two rak'ahs each. And for Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second, because splitting a single rak'ah into two halves is not possible, and giving it to the first group is preferable due to their precedence.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage provides a clear ruling regarding the performance of Salat al-Khawf when the Imam is a resident (i.e., not a traveler). The rule is that the Imam prays the full number of rak'ahs with each group: for a four-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr, he prays two rak'ahs with each group, so each group completes the prayer by doing the remaining two after the Imam finishes. For Maghrib (three rak'ahs), since it is odd, the Imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second group. The reasoning is that a single rak'ah cannot be split into halves, so the first group gets the extra rak'ah due to their priority (they prayed the first part with the Imam). This ruling is based on a narration that the Prophet did this for Zuhr. It is a straightforward memorization anchor for students to learn the variation in method for different numbers of rak'ahs when the Imam is a resident.

Key Terms
مقیم (muqim): A resident, as opposed to a traveler. In the context of Salat al-Khawf, the Imam who is not traveling performs the full prayer.
سبق (sabq): Precedence or priority. The first group is given the extra rak'ah in Maghrib because they had the priority of praying first with the Imam.
تنصیف (tansif): Dividing into halves. It is impossible to divide a single rak'ah, so the extra rak'ah goes to one group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Salat al-Khawf, how does a resident Imam lead Maghrib prayer for the two groups?
A) One rak'ah with each group
B) Two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second
C) One rak'ah with the first group and two rak'ahs with the second
D) Three rak'ahs with each group

Key Takeaway
A resident Imam in Salat al-Khawf leads four-rak'ah prayers with two rak'ahs per group and Maghrib with two rak'ahs for the first group and one for the second.

Dispute on the Legitimacy of Salat al-Khawf After the Prophet's Death
Discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on Salat al-Khawf's post-prophetic validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on the post-prophetic validity of Salat al-Khawf and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-argument using qiyas and ijma.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf remains valid after the Prophet because its cause (fear) continues and the Companions practiced it.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf) after the Prophet's death. While the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that it remains prescribed, Imam Abu Yusuf retracted his initial agreement and argued that it was specific to the Prophet's lifetime. We will examine the proofs on both sides and see how the commentator refutes Abu Yusuf's position using qiyas and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
Clearly state the point of disagreement: Is Salat al-Khawf legislated after the death of the Prophet?
The issue is not whether it was valid during his life (all agree it was), but whether it continues.
2
State the Hanafi Majority Position and Proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and later scholars) hold that it remains valid. Their primary proof is the continuation of the cause (fear) and the Companions' practice.
The commentator emphasizes that fear existed after the Prophet as it did before.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Dissenting View and His Dalil
Abu Yusuf argues that the Quranic verse (4:102) specifically addresses the Prophet, so the ruling is tied to his presence. After his death, the special occasion ends.
He also argues that the competition to pray behind the Prophet is gone, so the form is unnecessary.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response and Rebuttal
The commentator provides two rebuttals: (1) The cause (illah) is fear, which remains; by qiyas, the ruling continues. (2) The Companions performed it after the Prophet's death with tacit consensus (ijma sukuti).
The commentator even expresses surprise that Abu Yusuf would oppose this consensus.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Practical Impact
The majority view is mufta bihi, meaning Muslims in fear may perform Salat al-Khawf today. If Abu Yusuf's view were followed, they would have to pray normally, which could be impracticable.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is significant for communities in danger.

Source Text

نہیں ہیں۔ پس جب ابو یوسف رسول اللہ کے زمانے میں نماز خوف مشروع ہونے کے قائل ہیں تو رسول اللہ کا صلوۃ خوف پڑھانا ابو یوسف کے خلاف کیسے حجت ہو سکتا ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ابن مسعود کی روایت من حیث العبارت اگر ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت نہیں ہے مگر من حیث الدلالت حجت ہے۔ بایں طور کہ نماز خوف کا سبب خوف ہے اور خوف جس طرح آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حیات میں تحقیق ہے اسی طرح آپ کی وفات کے بعد بھی متحقق ہے پس جس طرح رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں خوف کی وجہ سے نماز خوف مشروع تھی اسی سبب کی وجہ سے آپ کے بعد بھی مشروع ہو گی دوسرا جواب یہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وفات کے بعد صحابہ کا نماز خوف پڑھنا ثابت ہے چنانچہ سعد بن ابی وقاص، ابو عبیدہ بن الجراح اور ابو موسیٰ اشعری نے اصفہان میں نماز خوف پڑھی ہے نیز سعد بن ابی وقاص نے طبرستان میں مجوسیوں سے جنگ کی اور آپ کے ساتھ حسن بن علی، حذیفہ بن اسحاق اور عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص تھے تو سعید بن ابی العاص نے ان حضرات صحابہ کو نماز خوف پڑھائی، اور کسی نے اس پر انکار نہیں کیا۔ پس یہ عدم انکار بمنزلہ اجماع کے ہو گیا۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وفات کے بعد نماز خوف کے جواز پر صحابہ کے اجماع کر لینے کے بعد حضرت امام ابو یوسف کا نماز خوف کی مشروعیت سے انکار کرنا اچھا سا نہیں لگتا۔
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear. According to the author of Al-Hidayah, Imam Abu Yusuf denied the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer after the death of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Imam Abu Yusuf initially believed in the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer like the two shaykhs, then withdrew from this statement and said that the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer is specific to the life of the Prophet. His evidence is that Allah said: 'And when you are among them and lead them in prayer...' This verse specifically commands the Messenger of Allah to lead the Fear Prayer. When you are the imam, each group will strive to attain the virtue of praying behind you. After your death, this competition is removed, and each group is able to perform the full prayer with an imam, so performing one rak'ah each with the characteristic of coming and going is not permissible. The author of Al-Hidayah said that the narration of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is evidence against Imam Abu Yusuf because the narration of Ibn Mas'ud has passed earlier in detail about the Prophet's Fear Prayer. But I say: Imam Abu Yusuf did not deny the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer during the Prophet's life. Rather, he acknowledges it during his life but not after death. So how can the Prophet's performance of Fear Prayer be evidence against Abu Yusuf? The answer is that Ibn Mas'ud's narration, even if not evidence literally (min hayth al-ibarah), is evidence implicitly (min hayth al-dalalah). Because the cause of the Fear Prayer is fear, and just as fear existed during the Prophet's life, it also exists after his death. So just as the Fear Prayer was legislated due to fear in the Prophet's time, it will be legislated after him due to the same cause. A second answer is that the Companions performed the Fear Prayer after the Prophet's death, as Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abu Ubaydah ibn al-Jarrah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari performed it in Isfahan. Also, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas fought the Magians in Tabaristan, and with him were Hasan ibn Ali, Hudhayfah ibn Ishaq, and Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, and Sa'id ibn Abi al-As led those Companions in the Fear Prayer, and no one objected. So this lack of objection amounted to consensus. After the Companions reached consensus on the permissibility of the Fear Prayer after the Prophet's death, Imam Abu Yusuf's denial of its legitimacy seems inappropriate.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legitimacy of the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf) after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The text presents the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, who initially agreed with the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) on its legitimacy, but later retracted and held that it was specific to the Prophet's lifetime. His evidence is the Quranic verse (4:102) which addresses the Prophet directly, implying a special ruling. The author of Al-Hidayah argues against this using Ibn Mas'ud's hadith, but the commentator (possibly the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah) notes that this hadith proves only the Prophet's practice, not post-prophetic validity. However, the commentator then provides two counter-arguments: first, that the cause (illah) of fear continues, so the ruling should continue by qiyas; second, that the Companions actually performed it after the Prophet's death with general acceptance, constituting tacit consensus (ijma sukuti). The commentator expresses surprise that Imam Abu Yusuf would go against this consensus. The passage demonstrates the method of using 'illah and consensus in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
صلوة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The fear prayer performed in times of danger, with specific rulings on congregation and shortening.
مشروعیت (mashru'iyyah): Legitimacy or being prescribed by Islamic law.
حیات نبی (hayat al-nabi): The lifetime of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in this passage, what is the strongest evidence that Salat al-Khawf remains valid after the Prophet's death?
A) The direct command in the Quran to the Prophet
B) The continuation of the cause (fear) and the Companions' practice
C) The opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf
D) The fact that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf remains a valid sunnah after the Prophet's death because its cause, fear, continues, and the Companions' tacit consensus confirms its legitimacy.

Salat al-Khawf with Muqim Imam: Rak'ah Distribution
Explains rak'ah distribution for muqim imam in Fear Prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Salat al-Khawf when the imam is a muqim and apply the half-prayer rule to determine rak'ah distribution for Zuhr and Maghrib, including the resolution of the indivisible half-rak'ah.

Core Idea
In Fear Prayer, each group gets half the prayer; for Maghrib, the first group takes the extra rak'ah because a rak'ah cannot be split.

This passage from Al-Hidayah details the specific method of performing Salat al-Khawf when the imam is a resident (muqim). It explains how the rak'ahs are distributed between two groups for both 4-rak'ah and 3-rak'ah prayers, grounded in the Prophet's practice. The ruling also contrasts with the Shafi'i view, highlighting a key difference in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify Imam's Status and Total Rak'ahs
The imam is muqim (resident), so he prays the full prayer. For Zuhr (4 rak'ahs), each group gets half: 2 rak'ahs. For Maghrib (3 rak'ahs), half is 1.5 rak'ahs.
Half-prayer rule: each group performs exactly half the total rak'ahs with the imam.
2
Apply the Half-Prayer Rule
The imam leads each group in half the prayer. For Zuhr, that's 2 rak'ahs each. For Maghrib, theoretically 1.5 rak'ahs each.
3
Handle the Indivisible Half-Rak'ah
Since a rak'ah cannot be halved (tansif al-rak'ah mustahil), the extra rak'ah (the half over one full rak'ah) is assigned to the first group due to precedence (sabq). Thus first group 2, second group 1.
The rationale: the first group is ahead in the prayer sequence, so they get the additional full rak'ah.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Imam Nawawi (Shafi'i) held the opposite: first group gets 1, second gets 2. His basis: obligatory qira'ah in the first two rak'ahs should be shared by both groups.
Hanafi prioritizes precedence over equal recitation opportunity.
5
Understand the Hanafi Dalil
The evidence is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr in Khawf with two groups, each 2 rak'ahs. For Maghrib, the ruling is derived by qiyas on the principle of half-prayer and the impossibility of splitting a rak'ah.
Hanafi reliance on precedence is consistent with general fiqh principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كان الامام مقيما صلى بالطائفة الاولى ركعتين و بالطائفة الثانية ركعتين كما روى انه صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى الظهر بالطائفتين ركعتين ركعتين ويصلى بالطائفة الاولى من المغرب ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة واحدة لان تنصيف الركعة الواحدة غير ممكن فجعلها فى الاولى اولى بحكم السبق. تشريح مسئلہ يہ ہے كہ امام اگر مقيم ہو تو وہ دونوں گروہوں کو دو دو ركعت پڑھائے كيونكہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بحالت اقامت ظہر كى نماز پڑھائى ہے اور مغرب كى نماز كو اس طرح پورا كرے كہ پہلے گروہ كو دو ركعت پڑھائے اور دوسرے گروہ كو ايك ركعت پڑھائے كيونكہ نماز خوف میں حكم يہ ہے كہ امام ہر گروہ كو نصف نماز پڑھائے۔ اور مغرب كى نماز كا نصف ايك پورى ركعت اور نصف ركعت ہے اور يہ بات مسلم ہے كہ ايك ركعت كو آدھا نہيں كيا جا سكتا۔ تو ہم نے كہا كہ پہلے گروہ كو تقدم كى وجہ سے دو ركعت پڑھائے اور دوسرے گروہ كو ايك ركعت پڑھائے۔ حضرت امام نووى نے كہا كہ اس كا برعكس كرے يعنى پہلے گروہ كو ايك ركعت اور دوسرے گروہ كو دو ركعت پڑھائے۔ اور وجہ يہ ذكر كى كہ پہلى دو ركعتوں میں قرأت فرض ہے اور مناسب يہ ہے كہ ہر گروہ كو اس میں سے حصہ ملے۔ اس لئے كہا گيا كہ پہلے گروہ كو ايك ركعت اور دوسرے گروہ كو دو ركعت پڑھائے تا كہ دونوں گروہ فرضِ قرأت میں امام كے ساتھ شريك ہو جائيں.
If the imam is a resident, he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second group two rak'ahs, as it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr with the two groups: two rak'ahs and two rak'ahs. And he prays with the first group of Maghrib two rak'ahs and with the second group one rak'ah, because dividing one rak'ah into halves is not possible, so it is better to give it to the first group due to precedence. Explanation: The issue is that if the imam is a resident, he leads both groups with two rak'ahs each, because the Messenger of Allah led Zuhr prayer in the state of residence. And he completes Maghrib prayer such that he leads the first group with two rak'ahs and the second group with one rak'ah, because the command in the Fear Prayer is that the imam leads each group with half the prayer. The half of Maghrib prayer is one complete rak'ah and half a rak'ah, and it is accepted that one rak'ah cannot be halved. So we said that the first group, due to precedence, is led with two rak'ahs, and the second group with one rak'ah. Imam Nawawi said to do the opposite, i.e., lead the first group with one rak'ah and the second with two rak'ahs, citing the reason that in the first two rak'ahs, recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory, and it is appropriate that each group gets a share of it. So he said that the first group should be given one rak'ah and the second two rak'ahs, so that both groups share in the obligatory recitation with the imam.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for Salat al-Khawf when the imam is a resident (muqim). The imam divides the congregation into two groups and leads each group in a portion of the prayer. For a 4-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr, each group performs 2 rak'ahs with the imam. For Maghrib (3 rak'ahs), the imam leads the first group in 2 rak'ahs and the second group in 1 rak'ah. The rationale is that the imam must lead each group in half the prayer. Since half of Maghrib is 1.5 rak'ah, and a rak'ah cannot be split, the first group gets precedence (because they are ahead in the prayer sequence). The commentator notes that Imam Nawawi (Shafi'i) held the opposite view: the first group should get 1 rak'ah and the second 2 rak'ahs, to allow both groups to share in the Qur'anic recitation, which is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs. This is a point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi ruling is based on the hadith of the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): A resident, not a traveler; prays full prayers.
تنصيف الركعة (tansif al-rak'ah): Dividing a rak'ah into halves, which is impossible in practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1 rak'ah
B) 2 rak'ahs
C) 3 rak'ahs
D) 1.5 rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
For Salat al-Khawf with a muqim imam, the Hanafi school distributes half the prayer to each group; for Maghrib, the first group gets the extra rak'ah because a rak'ah cannot be split.

Ruling on Fighting During Salat al-Khawf
States that fighting invalidates the prayer, with evidence from the Battle of the Trench

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that fighting invalidates Salat al-Khawf and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Fighting during prayer invalidates it; the Prophet's omission proves incompatibility.

This lesson examines a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf). While both agree on the general permissibility of carrying weapons during such prayers, they diverge on whether active fighting invalidates the prayer. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes prophetic practice (fi'l) over a general textual command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: fighting during Salat al-Khawf invalidates the prayer, and the prayer must be repeated.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Maliki evidence
Recognize that Imam Malik relies on Quran 4:102, which commands carrying weapons during prayer, implying that fighting is allowed.
The Quranic text is the primary proof for the opposing school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how Hanafis distinguish between carrying weapons for deterrence and active fighting, and why the Prophet's missing four prayers during the Battle of the Trench is a stronger precedent.
The response shows how a specific prophetic action can specify a general command.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi must repeat the prayer after fighting, while a Maliki may continue the prayer validly.
This difference has real-world implications for Muslims in combat zones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقاتلون في حال الصلوة فان فعلوا بطلت صلوتهم لانه صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم شغل عن اربع صلوات يوم الخندق، ولوجاز الاداء مع القتال لما تركها. تشريح مسئلہ يہ ہے كہ ہمارے نزديك نماز كى حالت میں كوئى گروہ قتال نہ كرے، اگر قتال كر ليا تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ از سرے نو پڑھنا لازم ہوگا۔ امام مالك كى دليل باری تعالیٰ كا قول وليأخذوا أسلحتهم ہے۔ وجہ استدلال يہ ہے كہ آیت میں نماز كے اندر ہتھيار ركھنے كا امر كيا گيا ہے اور ظاہر ہے كہ نماز كى حالت میں ہتھيار لينا قتال ہى كے واسطے ہو سكتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا كہ نماز كى حالت میں قتال كرنا جائز ہے ہماری دلیل يہ ہے كہ غزوہ احزاب كے موقع پر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم كى چار ركعتيں فوت ہو گئی تھیں، جنہيں آپ نے بعد میں قضاء كيا ہے اگر نماز كى حالت میں قتال جائز ہوتا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان نمازوں كو ان كے اوقات میں ادا كرنا نہ چھوڑتے معلوم ہوا كہ نماز كى حالت میں قتال كرنا جائز نہيں ہے۔ امام مالك كى دليل كا جواب يہ ہے كہ نماز كى حالت میں ہتھيار ساتھ ركھنے كا امر اس لئے كيا گيا كہ تا كہ كفار مسلمانوں كو غير مستعد جان كر ان پر حملہ آور نہ ہوں يا اگر قتال كى ضرورت پیش آجائے تو قتال كريں اور نماز كا اعادہ كر ليں.
And they should not fight during the prayer; if they do, their prayer becomes invalid, because he (peace and blessings be upon him) was occupied from four prayers on the day of the Trench. If performing (prayer) with fighting were permissible, he would not have missed them. Explanation: According to us, no group should fight during the prayer. If they fight, their prayer becomes invalid. It will be necessary to start anew. Imam Malik's evidence is the saying of Allah: 'And let them take their weapons.' The reasoning is that the verse commands carrying weapons during prayer, and it is obvious that carrying weapons during prayer can only be for fighting. So it is proven that fighting during prayer is permissible. Our evidence is that on the occasion of the Battle of the Ahzab (Trench), the Messenger of Allah missed four rak'ahs, which he later made up. If praying while fighting were permissible, he would not have missed those prayers at their times. Thus it is known that fighting during prayer is not permissible. The response to Imam Malik's evidence is that the command to carry weapons during prayer is given so that the disbelievers do not attack the Muslims, thinking them unprepared, or if the need for fighting arises, they can fight and then repeat the prayer.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses whether fighting is permitted during the actual performance of Salat al-Khawf. The Hanafi position is that fighting invalidates the prayer. The evidence is the incident from the Battle of the Trench (Khandaq) where the Prophet missed four prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha) and made them up later. If it were permissible to fight while praying, the Prophet would not have missed them. Imam Malik argues from Quran 4:102, which commands the believers to carry their weapons during the Fear Prayer, implying fighting is allowed. The Hanafi response distinguishes: carrying weapons is for deterrence or preparation, not for active fighting during the prayer. If fighting becomes necessary, they may stop the prayer, fight, and then repeat it later. The passage shows the use of practical precedent (the Prophet's action) over a general textual command, demonstrating the Hanafi method of reconciling evidences.

Key Terms
قتال (qital): Fighting in battle, including defending oneself against an enemy.
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): Fear Prayer, a shortened and adapted form of prayer performed during battle or danger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A Quranic verse commanding to lay down arms
B) The Prophet missed four prayers during the Battle of the Trench
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's omission of prayers during the Battle of the Trench demonstrates that fighting is incompatible with prayer, making it invalid.

Prayer on Mounts in Extreme Fear: Individual Gestures, No Qibla
Ruling of individual prayer on mounts during extreme fear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer during extreme fear, explain the Quranic proof (2:239), and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding congregation.

Core Idea
In extreme fear, prayer on mounts individually with gestures is valid; qibla is excused by necessity.

Imagine you are in a battle or fleeing from a predator. You cannot stop for prayer, let alone face Makkah. Does your prayer become invalid? The Hanafi school, relying on the Quran and the principle of necessity, provides a clear concession. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage specifies 'when fear intensifies.' At that point, the ruling is: pray individually on a mount, using gestures for ruku' and sujud, facing any direction if unable to face qibla.
The condition of 'inability to face qibla' is key; if possible, one must face it.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:239: 'And if you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding.' This verse directly permits prayer in a reduced form during fear.
The verse is mutlaq (general) and applies to both riding and walking.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'farijalan aw rukbanan' (on foot or riding) indicates that prayer can be performed without the normal conditions of standing and facing qibla, as long as there is fear.
The Hanafi school considers the command implied here as a rukhsa (concession) not an azima (original ruling).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad reportedly held that they should still pray in congregation. The author rejects this because the congregation requires unity of place (ittihad al-makan), which is absent in extreme fear.
This ikhtilaf is resolved in favor of Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Understand the tarjih and mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is individual prayer on mounts with gestures. The author explicitly states that Imam Muhammad's view is 'not correct' due to the impossibility of forming a cohesive congregation.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the dalil and the practical reality of extreme fear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان اشتد الخوف صلوا ركبانا فرادى يؤمون بالركوع والسجود الى اى جهة شاءوا اذا لم يقدروا على التوجه الى القبلة لقوله تعالى فان خفتم فرجالا او ركبانا وسقط التوجه للضرورة وعن محمد انهم يصلون بجماعة و ليس صحيح لانعدام الاتحاد المكان.
If the fear intensifies, they pray on mounts individually, gesturing with bowing and prostrating toward whatever direction they wish, when they are unable to face the qibla, due to His saying: 'And if you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding.' And facing the qibla drops due to necessity. And from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan) that they pray in congregation, but it is not correct due to the lack of unity of place.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for extreme fear where the enemy is in close proximity. The worshippers may pray individually while riding, using gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration, and they may face any direction because facing the qibla is waived due to necessity (darurah). The evidence is Quran 2:239: 'And if you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding.' Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) reportedly held that they should still pray in congregation if possible, but the author rejects this because in extreme fear, maintaining a unified line is impossible. The phrase 'lack of unity of place' refers to the impossibility of forming a congregation when everyone is moving or scattered. This ruling demonstrates the principle that necessity permits the relaxation of normal prayer conditions.

Key Terms
ركبانا (rukbanan): Riding on mounts (horses, camels, etc.).
فرادى (furada): Individually, not in congregation.
الاتحاد المكان (al-ittihad al-makan): Unity of place required for valid congregation.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits relaxation of normal fiqh rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when fear becomes extremely intense, how should one pray?
A) In congregation with the imam on foot
B) Individually on a mount with gestures toward any direction
C) In congregation while riding
D) Delay the prayer until safety

Key Takeaway
In extreme fear, the obligation of prayer is maintained, but normal requirements like facing qibla and physical postures are excused; individual prayer on a mount with gestures suffices.

Maghrib in Salat al-Khauf: The Hanafi Distribution
Explains Hanafi ruling for Maghrib in Khauf and responds to Imam Nawawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distribution of rak'ahs for Maghrib in Salat al-Khauf and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Half of three cannot be split equally; the first group gets precedence for two rak'ahs in Maghrib Khauf.

Salat al-Khauf allows a shortened form of prayer during battle. For a resident imam leading Maghrib, the Hanafi school applies the principle that the imam prays half of the prayer with each group. But with three rak'ahs, half is one and a half, and a half rak'ah cannot be performed. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school resolves this issue and how it differs from the Shafi'i approach of Imam Nawawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The imam prays half the prayer with each group. This is a foundational rule in Salat al-Khauf.
2
Calculate half of Maghrib
Maghrib has 3 rak'ahs; half is 1.5 rak'ahs.
3
Recognize the impossibility
A half rak'ah cannot be performed in practice. Therefore, the imam cannot pray exactly 1.5 with each group.
4
Apply precedence
The first group takes precedence, so they receive the extra whole rak'ah. Thus, the first group gets 2 rak'ahs, the second gets 1.
Precedence is a factor in the Hanafi reasoning.
5
Contrast with Nawawi's view
Imam Nawawi argues for the opposite distribution (1 and 2) to share the obligatory recitation in the first two rak'ahs.
This is the Shafi'i position.

Source Text
