اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام اگر مقیم ہو تو وہ دونوں گروہوں کو دو دو رکعت پڑھائے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بحالت اقامت ظہر کی نماز پر بھائی ہے اور مغرب کی نماز کو اس طرح پورا کرے کہ پہلے گروہ کو دو رکعت پڑھائے اور دوسرے گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے کیونکہ نماز خوف میں حکم یہ ہے کہ امام ہر گروہ کو نصف نماز پڑھائے۔ اور مغرب کی نماز کا نصف ایک پوری رکعت اور نصف رکعت ہے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ ایک رکعت کو آداھا نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ تو ہم نے کہا کہ پہلے گروہ کو تقدم کی وجہ سے دو رکعت پڑھائے اور دوسرے گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے ۔ حضرت امام نووی نے کہا کہ اس کا برعکس کرے یعنی پہلے گروہ کو ایک رکعت اور دوسرے گروہ کو دورکعت پڑھائے۔ اور وجہ یہ ذکر کی کہ پہلی دورکعتوں میں قرآت فرض ہے اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ ہر گروہ کو اس میں سے حصہ ملے ۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ پہلے گروہ کو ایک رکعت اور دوسرے گروہ کو دورکعت پڑھائے تا کہ دونوں گروہ فرضِ قرآت میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائیں۔
Chapter of Salat al-Khauf: It is better to make it part of. Commentary: The issue is that if the imam is a resident, he leads both groups with two rak'ahs each, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in a state of residence prayed Zuhr like that. And he should complete Maghrib prayer in this way: he leads the first group two rak'ahs and the second group one rak'ah, because in Salat al-Khauf the rule is that the imam prays half of the prayer with each group. And half of Maghrib prayer is one complete rak'ah and half a rak'ah, and it is established that one rak'ah cannot be performed singly. So we said: the first group, due to precedence, he leads two rak'ahs, and the second group one rak'ah. Imam Nawawi said to do the opposite, i.e., lead the first group one rak'ah and the second group two rak'ahs. He mentioned the reason that in the first two rak'ahs, recitation is obligatory, and it is appropriate that each group gets a share of it. Therefore it was said that the first group should be led one rak'ah and the second group two rak'ahs, so that both groups share in the obligatory recitation with the imam.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding how the imam should lead Maghrib prayer in Salat al-Khauf when he is a resident. The underlying principle is that the imam prays half of the prayer with each group. For Maghrib, which has three rak'ahs, half is one and a half rak'ahs. Since it is not possible to pray half a rak'ah, the imam gives two rak'ahs to the first group (due to their precedence) and one rak'ah to the second group. Imam Nawawi (Shafi'i) opposes this, arguing that the obligatory recitation in the first two rak'ahs should be shared by both groups, so the first group should get one rak'ah and the second two. The Hanafi view relies on the practical application of the half-prayer rule and the impossibility of fractional rak'ahs.

Key Terms
نماز خوف (Salat al-Khauf): The fear prayer, a shortened form of prayer allowed during battle or imminent danger.
نصف نماز (nisf al-salat): Half of the prayer, meaning half of the total rak'ahs of a particular prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two rak'ahs
C) Three rak'ahs
D) Half a rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the fractional half of Maghrib in Khauf by giving the first group two rak'ahs and the second group one, based on the principle of half-prayer and precedence.

Fighting During Salat al-Khauf Invalidates the Prayer
States ruling that fighting nullifies prayer and refutes Maliki view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that fighting during Salat al-Khauf invalidates the prayer and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the Prophet's example.

Core Idea
Fighting during prayer invalidates it — even in fear, the prayer must be repeated.

In the intense context of battle, Muslims are permitted to pray a shortened fear prayer (Salat al-Khauf) while keeping weapons. But what happens if they actually engage in combat during the prayer? The Hanafi school delivers a clear ruling: fighting nullifies the prayer. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, its proof from the Prophet's practice, and the counter-argument from Imam Malik based on a Qur'anic verse, concluding why the Hanafi view holds.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: fighting during prayer is not allowed, and if done, the prayer becomes invalid (batil) and must be repeated. This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
The ruling applies even in the heat of battle; there is no exception for self-defense.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that fighting during prayer is permissible, based on the apparent meaning of Qur'an 4:102 which commands keeping weapons during prayer. He argues that keeping weapons implies readiness to fight.
The Maliki view allows active combat if necessary, considering the prayer still valid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Maliki dalil: the verse 'wa liya'khudhu hidhrahum wa aslihatahum' (let them take their precautions and their weapons). The reasoning is that the command to keep weapons indicates that fighting is allowed during prayer, as the only purpose of weapons is combat.
This is a straightforward linguistic argument from the general command (amr) for precaution.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between preparing for possible fighting (which is allowed) and actually fighting. The Prophet (peace be upon him) missed four prayers during the Battle of Khandaq because he was occupied with fighting outside of prayer; if fighting during prayer had been permissible, he would have prayed on time while fighting.
This counter-proof relies on the Prophet's action (fi'l) as a stronger indication than the general command, because actions are more specific.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, if a person fights during prayer, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. In the Maliki school, the prayer remains valid and no repetition is needed. This affects soldiers and anyone in a dangerous situation who wishes to pray.
The Hanafi school emphasizes the sanctity of prayer and its separation from worldly actions, including combat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجم اور کسی گروہ کے لوگ نماز کی حالت میں قتال نہ کریں پس اگر انہوں نے قتال کیا تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم
خندق کے دن چار نمازوں سے مشغول کر دئیے گئے اگر قتال کے ساتھ ادا کرنا جائز ہوتا تو آپ ان نمازوں کو نہ چھوڑتے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک نماز کی حالت میں کوئی گروہ قتال نہ کرے، اگر قتال کر لیا تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ از سرے نو پڑھنا لازم ہوگا۔ امام مالک کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول ولياخذ واحذرهم و اسلحتھم ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ آیت میں نماز کے اندر ہتھیار رکھنے کا امرکیا گیا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ نماز کی حالت میں ہتھیار لینا قتال ہی کے واسطے ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ نماز کی حالت میں قتال کرنا جائز ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غزوہ احزاب کے موقع پر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی چار رکعتیں فوت ہو گئیں تھیں ، جنکو آپ نے بعد میں قضاء کیا ہے اگر نماز کی حالت میں قتال جائز ہوتا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان نمازوں کو ان کے اوقات میں اداء کرنا نہ چھوڑتے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز کی حالت میں قتال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نماز کی حالت میں بہتھیا ر ساتھ رکھنے کا امر اس لئے کیا گیا کہ تا کہ کفار مسلمانوں کو غیر مستعد جان کر ان پر حملہ آور نہ ہوں یا اگر قتال کی ضرورت پیش آجائے تو قتال کریں اور نماز کا اعادہ کر لیں۔
Ruling on fighting during prayer: They should not fight during prayer; if they do, their prayer becomes invalid, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was preoccupied from four prayers on the day of Khandaq, and if performing prayer with fighting were permissible, he would not have left them. Commentary: In our view, no group should fight during prayer; if they do, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. Imam Malik's proof is the verse: 'And let them take their precautions and their weapons.' The reasoning is that the verse commands keeping weapons during prayer, and it is apparent that taking weapons during prayer can only be for fighting. Thus, fighting during prayer is permissible. Our proof is that on the occasion of the Battle of the Confederates, the Prophet (peace be upon him) missed four prayers, which he later made up. If fighting during prayer were permissible, he would not have left performing them in their times. Hence, fighting during prayer is not permissible. The response to Imam Malik's proof is that the command to keep weapons during prayer is given so that the disbelievers do not attack the Muslims thinking them unprepared, or if the need for fighting arises, they fight and then repeat the prayer.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding whether fighting during Salat al-Khauf invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi ruling is clear: any fighting during prayer renders it invalid and requires repetition. The proof is the incident of the Battle of Khandaq (Ahzab) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) missed four prayers; if it had been permissible to fight during prayer, he would have done so instead of missing them. Imam Malik argues from the Qur'anic verse 'wa liya'khudhu hidhrahum wa aslihatahum' (let them take their precautions and their weapons) which indicates that keeping weapons (and thus potentially fighting) is allowed during prayer. The Hanafi response distinguishes between preparing for possible fighting (which is allowed) and actively fighting (which nullifies prayer). The command to keep weapons is precautionary, not permission to engage in combat during the prayer itself.

Key Terms
قتال (qital): Fighting or combat, specifically during the prayer in the context of Salat al-Khauf.
صلوۃ الخوف (Salat al-Khauf): The fear prayer performed during battle or danger with shortened and modified format.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fighting during prayer invalidates the prayer and requires repetition, even in Salat al-Khauf, as established by the Prophet's practice at Khandaq.

Prayer on Mounts in Extreme Fear and the Condition of Unity of Place
Rules for prayer on mounts when fear is intense, with reference to Imam Muhammad's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer on mounts during extreme fear and explain why Imam Muhammad's view on congregation is rejected based on the condition of ittihad al-makan.

Core Idea
Unity of place (ittihad al-makan) is essential for congregational prayer; separate mounts invalidate the congregation.

When fear is so intense that dismounting is impossible, the Hanafi school permits individual prayer on mounts with gestures. However, a narration from Imam Muhammad suggests congregation is commendable. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the decisive condition that settles the matter: the requirement of physical unity between imam and followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling for extreme fear
Read the passage to determine when prayer on mounts is allowed and how it is performed (individually, with gestures, facing any direction if necessary).
The ruling is based on the Quranic verse 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.'
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Find where the text mentions Imam Muhammad's view that congregation is commendable (mustahsan) and the commentator's response.
Imam Muhammad's view is reported but declared 'not sahih' (not sound).
3
Extract the proof for the standard position
Note the primary dalil: the Quranic verse (2:239) and the necessity that drops facing qiblah.
The verse is quoted as the basis for permissibility.
4
Examine the rebuttal of Imam Muhammad's view
Understand why the commentator rejects congregation: ittihad al-makan (unity of place) is a condition for valid imamah, and separate mounts violate it.
The exception is if a follower shares the same mount as the imam.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Conclude that the relied-upon position is individual prayer on mounts, not congregation, unless all are on the same mount.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سواری پر نماز پڑھنے کا حکم
فان اشتد الخوف صلوا ركبانا فرادى يؤمون بالركوع والسجود الى اى جهة شاء وااذا لم يقدروا على التوجه الى القبلة لقوله تعالى فان خفتم فرجالا او رکبانا وسقط التوجه للضرورة وعن محمد انهم يصلون بجماعة و ليس صحيح لانعدام الاتحاد المكان ترجمہ پھر اگر خوف میں شدت ہو تو سواری کی حالت میں تنہا تنہا نماز پڑھیں، رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کریں ، جس طرف ممکن ہو، جبکہ قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ ہونے پر قادر نہ ہوں کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم کو خوف ہو تو پیادہ نماز پڑھو۔ یا سوار ہو کر، اور قبلہ کی جانب متوجہ ہونا شرورت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھیں ، اور یہ روایت صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ اتحاد مکانی مین تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر دشمن کا خوف اس قدر شدید ہو گیا کہ وہ مسلمانوں کو سواری سے اتر کر نماز پڑھنے کا موقع نہیں دیتے تو اس صورت میں مسلمانوں کے لئے سواری ہی پر بیٹھے بیٹھے رکوع اور سجدہ کے اشارے کے ساتھ تنہا تنہا نماز ادا کرنا جائز ہے اور استقبال قبلہ کے سلسلہ میں حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر قبلہ کی طرف رخ کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو جس طرف چاہیں رخ کر لیں۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فان خفتم فرجلا اور کھانا ہے اور استقبال قبلہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا ہے، امام محمد سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ سواری پر رہ کر با جماعت نماز پڑھنا مستحسن ہے اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں لیکن یہ حکم صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ صحت اقتداء کے لئے مکان کا متحد ہونا شرط ہے اور وہ اس حالت میں معدوم ہے ہاں اگر کوئی آدمی امام کے ساتھ اس کی سواری پر ہو تو اس کی اقتداء کرنا صحیح ہے،
Ruling on praying on a mount: If fear intensifies, they pray on mounts individually, gesturing for bowing and prostration, facing whatever direction, if they are unable to face the qiblah, due to the verse: 'If you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding.' Facing qiblah is dropped due to necessity. From Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan) it is narrated that they pray in congregation, but it is not correct because of lack of unity of place. Commentary: If the fear from the enemy becomes so intense that they do not give the Muslims an opportunity to dismount and pray, then in that case it is permissible for the Muslims to pray individually on their mounts with gestures for bowing and prostration. Regarding facing qiblah, if it is not possible, they may face any direction. The proof is the verse: 'If you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding.' Facing qiblah is dropped due to necessity. From Imam Muhammad there is a narration that praying in congregation while on mounts is commendable; Imam Shafi'i also holds this view. But this ruling is not correct because for the validity of following an imam, unity of place (ittihad al-makan) is a condition, and that is absent in this situation. However, if a person is on the same mount as the imam, then his following is valid.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on prayer when fear becomes extreme, such that the enemy prevents dismounting. The Hanafi school allows praying on mounts individually, performing gestures for bowing and prostration, and facing any direction if qiblah cannot be faced. The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.' The necessity drops the condition of facing qiblah. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is reported to have a view that congregational prayer on mounts is commendable (mustahsan), but the commentator refutes this, stating that the condition for valid leadership (imamat) is unity of place (ittihad al-makan), which is lacking when people are on separate mounts. However, if a follower is on the same mount as the imam, their followership is valid. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position is individual prayer, not congregation.

Key Terms
اتحاد مکانی (ittihad al-makan): Unity of place: the condition that the imam and followers must be in the same physical location for the validity of congregational prayer.
اشارہ (isharah): Gestures: movements with the head or body to indicate ruku' and sujud when unable to perform them normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The follower must be on a different mount
C) The follower must face the qiblah
D) The follower must also gesture for ruku' and sajdah

Key Takeaway
Prayer on mounts during extreme fear is performed individually with gestures; congregation is invalid unless the imam and follower share the same mount.
